    《续夷坚志》　宋　元好问

    Explanation

    1

    Translation:

    Continuation of the Yijian Zhi
    Song Dynasty
    Yuan Hao Wen

    2

    续夷坚志一
    　　遗山，中原人。使生宋熙、丰间，与苏、黄诸人同时，当大有声。不幸出完颜有国日。虽偏方以文饰戎事，用科举选人，惜又在贞祐前后，不得掌其笺牒文柄，故闲居著述。观其文与诗词，宏肆轶宕。及所传其国人号《中州集》，人各有传，其颠叙其行业仕隐，诗则一联不遗；宋士夫沦陷其国者，概见于末。文有史法。其好义乐善之心，盖广矣！所续《夷坚志》，岂但过洪景卢而已！其自序可见也。恶善惩劝，纤细必录，可以知风俗而见人心？岂南北之有间哉？北方书籍，率金所刻。罕至江南，友人王起善见之，亟钞成帙。其学富笔勤又可知矣。持以示予，时日将夕，读至丙夜，尽四卷。深有启于予心！以病不能钞，姑识卷末而归之。壬申岁之除、商邱宋无子虚书于沙头白鸥眠处。
    　　中州曾历览，底处觅孤坟！勋业元无我，文章正数君！渊源由《史》、《汉》，警策出机、云。予亦尚奇者，何期广见闻。吴道辅景文。

    2

    Continuation of the Yiji Zhi

    Yishan was a person from the Central Plains. If he had lived during the Xining and Fengzhen periods of the Song Dynasty, he would have been famous alongside Su Shi, Huang Tingjian, and others. Unfortunately, he was born during the reign of the Jin Dynasty. Although he lived in a border region and used literature to support military affairs, and though he was selected through the imperial examinations, he was unfortunate enough to live during the reign of Emperor Xuanzong of Jin, and thus did not hold a position of power or influence in the literary or administrative circles. Therefore, he wrote while living in seclusion. His writings and poetry are expansive, unrestrained, and free-flowing. The collection of works by his compatriots, known as Zhongzhou Ji (Central Plains Collection), contains detailed accounts of their careers, official positions, and seclusion, with no single line of poetry omitted. The fate of Song Dynasty scholars who fell into the hands of the Jin Dynasty is generally recounted at the end of the collection. His writing follows historical methods, and his heart that loves righteousness and goodness is truly vast! The continuation of Yiji Zhi that he wrote surpasses even Hong Jinglu's work! This can be seen from his own preface. He praised good deeds and punished bad ones, recording even the smallest details, so that one can understand the customs and see the hearts of people. Is there any difference between the North and South? Northern books were mostly carved during the Jin Dynasty and rarely reached the South. My friend Wang Qishan saw one and quickly copied it into a volume. His rich learning and diligent writing are evident. He brought it to show me as the day was ending, and I read until the third watch of the night, finishing four volumes. It greatly enlightened my heart! Because of illness, I could not copy it, but I noted it at the end of the volume and returned it. On the first day of the year in the Ren Shen year, Shangqiu's Song Wuzixu wrote this at the place where white egrets rest.

    Once I have traversed the Central Plains, where shall I search for a solitary grave? My achievements were never mine, but your writings are truly counted among the great! Your literary traditions stem from Shiji and Hanshu, and your insightful remarks surpass those of Jī Yun. I, too, am one who values the extraordinary, and how did I expect to gain such broad knowledge? Wu Dao Fu Jingwen.

    3

    子思子云：“国家将兴，必有祯祥；国家将亡，必有妖孽。”洪景卢《夷坚志》多政、宣事；元好问《续志》多泰和、贞祐事。其视平世有闲耳！砦窳叟。
    　　吴中王起善博学且勤，人有异书，必手钞之，此其一也。按《续夷坚志》乃遗山先生当中原陆沈之时，皆耳闻目见之事，非若洪景卢演史寓言也。其劝善戒恶，不为无补。吾知起善推广之心，即遗山之心也。至顺三年，朱方石岩民瞻氏识。
    　　遗山先生《续夷坚志》二卷，乃吴中王起善钞本，今归芥甫夏侯。至正二十三年癸卯岁闰三月十七日丁亥借录，至四月七日丙午录毕于泗北村居映雪斋、华亭。在家道人孙道明明叔，时年六十有七也。予钞北地枣本《续夷坚志》四册，实遗山先生所撰也。至正戊子，武林新刻《金史》，因获一观。谨录此《传》，附于所书之后云。是年花朝日、吴下王东起善识。《传》不录

    Explanation

    3

    Zǐsīzi said: "When a state is about to rise, there will be auspicious signs; when a state is about to fall, there will be ominous signs." Hóng Jǐnglú's Economic and Political Miscellany contains many stories from the reigns of Emperor Huizong and Emperor Ningzong; Yuán Hǎowèn's Continued Economic and Political Miscellany contains many stories from the reigns of Emperor Xuanzong and Emperor Xianzong. In a peaceful era, such matters are just a matter of leisure! ——砦窳叟

    Wáng Qǐshàn of Wú, diligent and studious, whenever he encountered rare books, he would copy them by hand, which is one of his virtues. According to Continued Economic and Political Miscellany, it was compiled by Yuán Hǎowèn during the decline of the Central Plains, and all the stories were based on firsthand accounts, unlike Hóng Jǐnglú's Economic and Political Miscellany, which often included fictional elements. Its encouragement of good deeds and warning against evil are not without benefit. I know that Wáng Qǐshàn's intention to spread knowledge is the same as Yuán Hǎowèn's. ——Zhu Fāngshíyán Mínzhān, third year of Zhisun

    Yuán Hǎowèn's Continued Economic and Political Miscellany consists of two volumes, which are copies by Wáng Qǐshàn of Wú, and are now owned by Jièfǔ Xiàhóu. On the seventeenth day of the third month, leap year, of the twenty-third year of Zhizheng (1363 AD), I borrowed the manuscript and transcribed it, completing the task on the seventh day of the fourth month, at the Snow Reflection Study in the village of Sibei and in Huating. ——Sūn Dàomíng, aged sixty-seven, a lay follower at home

    I transcribed four volumes of Continued Economic and Political Miscellany from a jujube-bound manuscript from the north, which was indeed written by Yuán Hǎowèn. In the year of the Earth Rabbit (1360 AD), a new edition of the History of the Jin Dynasty was published in Wulin, and I had the opportunity to read it. I carefully recorded this preface and appended it to the manuscript. ——Wáng Dōngqǐshàn of Wú, on the Festival of Flowers, third year of Zhisun. (The preface itself is not recorded.)

    4

    余集序
    　　遗山先生当金源末造，备位下僚，浮湛散秩；洊登左司，旋遭丧乱，沦落以终。晚年以著述自任，颇有志于国史，又为人所沮。诗文之外，寄意于《中州》一集。文人少达而多穷，不信然哉！此《夷坚志》虽续洪氏，而适当百六之会，灾变频仍，五行乖舛，有开必先，动关运会。非吊诡之厄言，实禨祥之外乘。不贤识小，又何讥焉？仆来豫，荣别驾庆出以相，乃其尊甫筠圃先生读易楼藏本。书凡二卷，而宋子虚、王起善二跋皆云四卷，又称其别有自序，而卷中无之。不复可考矣！书中大半东京琐事。余初来，颇资闻见。因为较其讹脱，仍分四卷，以还旧观。手钞付梓，且依翁氏所辑遗山《年谱》，略为表系以附于后，庶览者粗悉其平生云。嘉庆戊辰冬日，杭郡余集书于大梁书院。《表》不录

    Explanation

    4

    Translation:

    Preface by Yu Ji

    Mr. Yuwen Xuzhong, during the late period of the Jin Dynasty, held a low-ranking position, fluctuating between various minor offices. He was repeatedly appointed to the Left Censorate but soon suffered from chaos and disaster, leading to his eventual downfall. In his later years, he took it upon himself to engage in literary pursuits, with a particular interest in national history, though he was often discouraged by others. Beyond poetry and prose, he expressed his thoughts in the Zhongzhou anthology. It is indeed true that scholars often face adversity rather than success. This Yiji Zhi, although a continuation of Hong Mai's work, was compiled during a time of great change, marked by frequent disasters and the imbalance of the five elements. It signifies the beginning of a new era and is closely tied to the workings of fate. It is not merely a collection of strange and ominous words but also a vehicle for auspicious and ominous signs. Not being a great man, I recognize small things, so why should I be criticized? When I came to Henan, the distinguished magistrate Rong Qing presented me with a copy from the Read Yi Tower, the collection of his father, Mr. Yuwen Junpu. The book consists of two volumes, but the prefaces by Song Zixu and Wang Qishan both state that it was originally four volumes, and they mention that it had a separate preface, which is missing from the current version. It is no longer possible to verify this. The book mostly contains trivial matters from the Eastern Capital. When I first arrived, I greatly benefited from it. I corrected its errors and restored its original structure, dividing it into four volumes. I hand-copied and printed it, and following Wang Zhen's compilation of Yuwen Xuzhong's Chronological Biography, I briefly outlined his life in an appendix to provide readers with a rough understanding of his life. This was written on a winter day in the year of Wu Chen during the reign of Emperor Jiaqing, by Yu Ji from Hangzhou at the Great Liang Academy. The appendix is not included.

    5

    镇库宝
    　　赵王镕炼丹成，不及饵，藏之镇州库藏中者余三百年。贞祐初，真定元帅三喜弃城，取之以行。行及平阳，为胥莘公所劾，收之。丹入汴京，下丰衍库收，名色谓之“镇库宝。”京城变后，予同户部主事刘彦卿往观之。丹以漆柜盛，旁画广成子问道像。中复有漆合，高五寸，阔三寸，合盖上作九环，外八中一，以金涂之，各有流去声道相贯，环中作小孔，予意其为九转也。合中复有银合盛丹。合盖上镂佛一，左龙右凤，在佛座下，亦皆金涂。开视，丹体殊轻，周匝合中，色如枣皮漆，而裂璺纵横，绝不与今世丹砂相似。予意颇轻之。问主库者此有何异，曰：“无他，但阴晦中恒出光怪，如火起然耳！”壬辰年亲见

    Explanation

    5

    Treasure of the Treasury
    Zhao Wang Rong successfully refined an elixir of immortality but did not consume it. It was stored in the treasury of Zhenzhou for over three hundred years. In the early years of the Zhenyuan era, the military commander of Zhending, Sanxi, abandoned the city and took the pill with him. When he reached Pingyang, he was impeached by Xushen Gong, and the pill was seized. The pill was brought to Kaifeng and stored in the Fengyan Treasury, where it was named "Treasure of the Treasury." After the chaos in the capital, I went with Liu Yanei, the Director of the Ministry of Revenue, to see it. The pill was stored in a lacquer cabinet, with a painting of Guangchengzi asking about the Dao on the side. Inside, there was another lacquer box, five inches high and three inches wide, with nine rings on the lid—eight on the outside and one in the middle, all coated with gold, each with a channel for the sound to flow through, and small holes in the rings. I thought it was the result of nine transformations. Inside the lacquer box, there was another silver box containing the pill. On the lid of the silver box, there was an engraved Buddha, with a dragon on the left and a phoenix on the right, at the feet of the Buddha, all also coated with gold. When opened, the pill was unusually light, with cracks running in all directions, the color like the bark of a jujube tree, and completely different from the cinnabar of today. I thought little of it. I asked the person in charge of the treasury what was special about it, and they said, "Nothing special, just that it constantly emitted strange light in dim conditions, like a fire." I personally saw it in the year Renchen.

    6

    金狮猛
    　　正大初，张圣俞客舞阳县北街。一日，家婢从一弓手家买得一牛腰肾。以刀割之，刀不能入。剥视之，得一石，作狮形，色如泥金所涂，前一蹄屈向内，一蹄枕之而睡。夜夜有光。高二寸余。殆秉异气所化。圣俞嫂吴收之。不知今存否也。圣俞说。
    　　康李梦应
    　　康伯禄、李钦叔，壬辰冬十二月行部河中。先城未破一日，康与钦叔求梦于某神，伯禄梦城隍破，争船落水中，为一锦衣美妇援之而出。美妇援出，满眼皆桃花。钦叔梦人与桃符二，上写：‘宜入新年，长命富贵。’明日城陷，伯禄争船不得上，落水死；李得船，走陕县。三四日改岁。陕令杨正卿令人送桃符，所书如梦中所云。正卿说。

    Explanation

    6

    Translation

    The Golden Lion

    In the early years of the Zhengda era, Zhang Shengyu was a guest in the northern street of Wuyang County. One day, a maid from his household bought a cow's kidney from a bowman's family. When she tried to cut it with a knife, the blade could not penetrate. Upon peeling it open, they found a stone shaped like a lion, colored as if coated with gold leaf. The stone had one paw bent inward and another resting under its head, as if it were sleeping. It emitted light every night. The stone was about two inches high and was likely formed by unusual forces. Zhang Shengyu's sister-in-law, Wu, collected the stone. It is unknown whether it still exists today. Zhang Shengyu recounts this.

    The Dreams of Kang and Li

    In the twelfth month of the year Renchen, Kang Bolu and Li Qins叔 traveled to Hezhong. The day before the city was captured, Kang and Li sought dreams from a certain deity. Kang Bolu dreamed that the city god broke the city, and he struggled to board a boat but fell into the water. A beautiful woman in fine clothing pulled him out. As he was pulled out, he saw a field of peach blossoms. Li Qins叔 dreamed that someone gave him two peach wood charms, inscribed with the words: "May you enter the new year with longevity and wealth." The next day, the city was captured. Kang Bolu failed to board the boat and drowned; Li Qins叔 managed to get on the boat and escaped to Shan County. After a few days, the new year began. The governor of Shan County, Yang Zhengqing, sent peach wood charms with the same inscriptions as in Li Qins叔's dream. Yang Zhengqing recounts this.

    7

    包女得嫁
    　　世俗传包希文以正直主东岳速报司，山野小民，无不知者。庚子秋，泰安界南征兵掠一妇还，云是希文孙女，颇有姿色。倡家欲高价买之，妇守死不行。主家利其财，捶楚备至，妇遂病。邻里嗟惜而不能救。里中一女巫私谓人云：“我能脱此妇，令适良人。”即诣主家，闭目吁气，屈伸良久，作神降之态。少之，瞑目咄咤，呼主人者出，大骂之。主人具香火，俯伏请罪，问何所触尊神？巫又大骂云：“我速报司也！汝何敢以我孙女为倡？限汝十日，不嫁之良家，吾灭汝门矣！”主家百拜谢过，不数日嫁之。

    Explanation

    7

    The Girl of the Bao Family Gets Married

    According to popular belief, Bao Xiwen served as the righteous and swift retribution officer of Mount Dong. This is known to all common people in the mountains and countryside. In the autumn of the Gengzi year, a woman from the south of Taian was captured by soldiers during a campaign and returned. She claimed to be the granddaughter of Bao Xiwen and had considerable beauty. A courtesan wanted to buy her at a high price, but the woman refused to go, even to the point of death. The master of the household coveted her wealth and subjected her to severe beatings, causing her to fall ill. The neighbors pitied her but could not help. A village woman who practiced witchcraft privately told someone, "I can free this woman and marry her to a good man." She then went to the master's house, closed her eyes and exhaled deeply, bending and stretching for a long time, acting as if a god had descended. After a while, she closed her eyes and shouted angrily, calling the owner out and cursing him severely. The owner prepared incense and fire, prostrated himself, and asked for forgiveness, wondering what he had offended the great god. The witch cursed again, saying, "I am the swift retribution officer! How dare you make my granddaughter a courtesan? I give you ten days. If you do not marry her to a good family, I will destroy your family!" The master bowed a hundred times to apologize, and within a few days, she was married.

    8

    铁中虫
    　　吾州会长老，住飞狐之团崖。初入院，典座僧白：“厨堂一镬，可供千人，然火则有声。今二年矣。人以为釜鸣不祥，废不敢用，妨大众作食。师欲如何？”会云：“吾就大众乞此镬，当任我料理。”众诺。乃椎破釜底，穴中得一虫，长二寸许，色深赤。盖此虫经火则有声。淄川杨叔能，亦尝见芒山均庆寺大镬破一窍，如合拳，中有一虫如蛴螬而红。此类大家往往见之。魏文帝《典论》以为火性酷烈，理无生物。特执方之论耳！团崖事，全唯识记

    Explanation

    8

    Insect in Iron

    The abbot of our temple, residing at the mountain cliff of Feixu, said: "When I first entered the temple, the monk in charge of the kitchen reported: 'There is a large cooking pot in the kitchen that can serve a thousand people, but it makes a sound when heated. It has been this way for two years. People believe that the sound of the cauldron is inauspicious, so they abandoned it and did not dare to use it, hindering the making of food for the community. What should the teacher do about it?' The abbot replied: 'I will ask the community to give me this pot, and I will take care of it.' The community agreed. So he pounded the bottom of the cauldron and found a creature in the hole, about two inches long, deep red in color. This creature makes a sound when heated. Mr. Yang Shuneng of Zichuan also once saw a large hole in the cauldron at Junqing Temple on Mang Mountain, about the size of a clenched fist, containing a red grub-like creature. Such creatures are often seen by many. Emperor Wei Wen's Dian Lun states that fire is intensely hot and should not produce living things. It is merely a strict doctrine! The matter of the mountain cliff is entirely based on the theory of consciousness-only."

    9

    王增寿外力
    　　秀容东南双堡王增寿，号为外力，善角抵，人莫能敌。泰和末，官括驼。钉去声驼足令跛，自羊头村背负驼至代州。州守信以为然，增寿复负之而归。樊帅说
    　　石中蛇蝎
    　　泰和中，柏山长老志贤，住西京东堂，常住足备，即弃去。修浑源乐安桥岭路，槌破一牛心大石。中有蛇蝎相吞螫，人不知其何从而入也！贤曰：“此在吾法，是怨毒所化，随想而入，历千万劫而不得解者。若不为解却，他日亦道曾见我来。”即以大杖击之，竟无他异。全唯识说
    　　任氏翁媪
    　　定襄沙村，樊帅所居。说：里中任实洎其妻张氏，七十三岁，同年月日时生，复同年月日时死。古今所无有。
    　　郑叟犯土禁

    Explanation

    9

    Translation

    Wang Zengshou, known as the "External Force" from Shuorong in the southeast, was renowned for his extraordinary physical abilities, particularly in wrestling, which no one could match. During the end of the Tahe period, he was tasked with transporting a camel. He made the camel's foot lame by nailing it, then carried the camel from Yangtou Village to Dazhou. The local official, likely a general named Fan, trusted that Wang had indeed made the camel lame, and Wang carried it back. (Note: The phrase "钉去声驼足令跛" is ambiguous and could mean "nailing with a specific sound to make the camel's foot lame.")

    At Baishan, Elder Zhi Xian, residing at the Western Gate Hall in Xijing, was known for his miraculous abilities. He once broke a large stone at the bridge road in Hunsun, revealing snakes and scorpions biting each other inside. The origin of these creatures was unclear, but Zhi Xian explained that the stone was transformed by resentment and poison, entering through the power of thought and remaining unresolved for countless eons. He said, "This is within my method. If not resolved, one day they will also say that they have seen me." He immediately struck the stone with a large stick, and there was no other unusual event. (Note: The phrase "全唯识说" is unclear and could refer to a specific text or doctrine.)

    In Dingxiang, in the village of Shacha, where General Fan resided, there was a couple named Ren Shi and his wife Zhang. They were both 73 years old and were born on the same day and time. They also died on the same day and time, a rare coincidence that has never been recorded in ancient or modern times.

    (Note: The phrase "郑叟犯土禁" is unclear and could mean "an old man from Zheng violated the earth's prohibition" or "an old man from Zheng broke the earth's rules.")

    10

    平舆南函头村郑二翁，资性强，不信禁忌。泰和八年，其家东南有所兴造，或言是太岁所在，不可犯。郑云：“我即太岁，尚何忌耶！”督役夫兴作。掘地不二尺，得妇人红绣鞋一双。役夫欲罢作，郑怒，取焚之，掘地愈急。又二三尺，得一黑鱼，即烹食之。不旬日，翁母并亡，又丧长子，连延十余口；马十，牛四十。死病狼藉。存者大惧，避他所。祸乃息。
    　　张童入冥
    　　平舆南函头村张老者，以捕鹑为业，故人目为鹌鹑。年已老，止一儿，成童矣，一旦死。翁媪自念老无所倚，号哭闷绝，恨不俱死。明日欲埋之，又复不忍。但累砖作邱，入地一二尺许。云：“吾儿还活！”人笑其痴，而亦有哀之者。三日复墓，恸哭不休。忽闻墓中呻吟声，翁媪惊曰：“吾儿果还魂矣！”撒砖曳棺出，舁归。儿果复活。俄索汤粥。良久，说初为人摄往冥司，儿哀诉主者：爹娘老可念，乞尽余年，葬送毕，死无所归恨！冥官颇怜之，即云：“今放汝归。

    Explanation

    10

    In the southern village of Hantou, Pingyu, there lived an old man named Zheng Er, who had a strong character and did not believe in taboos. In the eighth year of the Taihe era, when his family was building something in the southeast of their home, someone said that the site was where the Tai Sui (a term in Chinese astrology) was located and should not be disturbed. Zheng replied, "I am the Tai Sui, what should I fear?" and supervised the laborers to begin construction. When they dug the ground to a depth of not two feet, they found a pair of red embroidered shoes belonging to a woman. The laborers wanted to stop the work, but Zheng became angry, took the shoes and burned them, and dug the ground more urgently. After digging another two or three feet, they found a black fish, which they cooked and ate. Within ten days, Zheng's mother also died, and he lost his eldest son. More than ten people were affected, including ten horses and forty cattle. Deaths and illnesses were scattered. The survivors were greatly afraid and fled to another place. The disaster then ceased.

    Zhang's Son Enters the Underworld

    In the southern village of Hantou, Pingyu, there lived an old man named Zhang, who made a living by catching quails, and people therefore called him Quail. He was old and had only one son, who had grown into a young man. One day, the son died. The old man and his wife thought of their own old age with no one to rely on, wept and fainted, hating that they could not die together. The next day, they wanted to bury him, but could not bear to do so. They simply piled up bricks to make a mound, digging the ground to a depth of one or two feet. They said, "Our son will come back to life!" Some people laughed at their foolishness, while others pitied them. Three days later, they returned to the tomb, weeping uncontrollably. Suddenly, they heard a moaning sound from inside the tomb. The old man and his wife were startled and said, "Our son has indeed returned to life!" They removed the bricks and dragged the coffin out, carrying him back home. The son indeed came back to life. Soon, he asked for soup and porridge. After a while, he said he was first taken by someone to the underworld. The son pleaded with the officials in tears: "My parents are old and pitiable. I beg to live out my remaining years, to finish the funeral rites, and then die without regret." The officials of the underworld pitied him and said, "Now we will let you return."

    11

    语汝父，能弃打捕之业，汝命可延矣！”其父闻此语，尽焚网罟之属，挈儿入寺供佛。寺有一僧吕姓者，年未四十，仪表殊伟，曾上州作纲首。张童即前问僧：“师亦还魂耶？”吕云：“何曾死？”张童言，我在冥中引问次，见师在殿角铜柱上，铁绳系足，狱卒往来以棓撞师腋下，流血淋漓。及放归时，曾问监卒，吕师何故受罪？乃云：“他多脱下斋主经文，故受此报。”吕闻大骇。盖其腋下病一漏疮，已三年矣！儿初不知。吕遂洁居一室，日以诵经为课。凡三年，疮乃平。赵长官亲见之。
    　　土禁二
    　　乙巳春，怀州一花门生率仆掘地，得肉块一枚，其大三四升许。以刀割之，肉如羊，有肤膜。仆言：“土中肉块，人言为太岁，见者当凶，不可掘。”生云：“我宁知有太岁耶？”复令掘之，又得肉块二。不半年，死亡相踵，牛马皆尽。古人谓之“有凶祸而故犯之，是与神敌也！”申胡鲁邻居亲见之，为予言。

    Explanation

    11

    The father was told, "If you can abandon your trade of hunting and fishing, your son's life can be prolonged!" Upon hearing this, the father burned all his nets and traps, took his son to the temple to worship Buddha. There was a monk named Lu in the temple, who was not yet forty years old, with a distinguished appearance, and had once served as the head of a convoy in the state. Zhang the boy then asked the monk, "Did you also come back from the dead?" The monk replied, "How could I have died?" Zhang said, "I saw you in the underworld, tied with an iron rope around your feet on a copper pillar in the corner of a hall, and guards were hitting you with sticks on your armpit, causing you to bleed profusely." When he was released, he asked the guard why Master Lu was punished. The guard said, "He often took down the scriptures of the lay devotee, so he received this retribution." Master Lu was greatly startled. It turned out that he had a leaking sore on his armpit for three years! The son did not know about it at first. Master Lu then lived in a clean room, reciting scriptures as his daily practice. After three years, the sore healed. Zhao the official saw it with his own eyes.

    Earthly Taboo 2
    In the spring of the year Yishisi (乙巳), a student from Huizhou named Huamen led his servant to dig the ground and found a piece of meat, about the size of three or four sheng (升). They cut it with a knife, and the meat was like that of a sheep, with skin and membranes. The servant said, "A piece of meat in the earth is said to be the Tai Sui (太岁), and seeing it brings bad luck; it should not be dug up." The student said, "How could I know there is a Tai Sui?" He ordered them to dig again, and they found two more pieces of meat. Within half a year, deaths followed one another, and all the cattle and horses died. The ancients said, "To deliberately violate an ominous sign, is to defy the gods!" Shen Huru, a neighbor, witnessed it and told me about it.

    12

    群熊
    　　癸卯初，有熊数十万，从内乡硖石入西南山。衔枚并进。行既远，掌皆出血。有羸劣而死者，群熊自食之。州县有文移传报。予于彰德见之。
    　　刀生花
    　　济源关侯庙大刀，辛丑岁，忽生花十许茎，各长一指，纤细如发，茎色微绿，其颠作细白花，大于黍米。予同舍李庆之子正甫为予言。
    　　产龙
    　　平定苇泊村，乙巳夏，一妇名马师婆，年五十许，怀孕六年有余，今年方产一龙。官司问所由，此妇说，怀孕至三四年不产，其夫曹主簿惧为变怪，即遣逐之。及临产，恍忽中，见人从罗列其前，如在官府中。一人前自陈云：“寄托数年，今当舍去。明年阿母快活矣！”言讫，一白衣人掖之而去，至门，昏不知人。久之乃苏。旁人为说，晦冥中雷震者三，龙从妇身飞去，遂失身孕所在。

    Explanation

    12

    Crowds of Bears

    At the beginning of the year Jiwei, tens of thousands of bears emerged from the Xiaoshi of Neixiang and entered the southwestern mountains. They advanced silently and in unison. After traveling a great distance, their palms bled. Those who were weak or inferior and died were eaten by the other bears. The prefectures and counties had official documents transmitted and reported. I witnessed this in Changde.

    The Sword Blooming with Flowers

    In the year Xin Chou, a great sword at the Guan Yu temple in Jiyuan suddenly grew ten or so stems of flowers, each about an inch long, as fine as hair. The stems were slightly green, and the tips bore delicate white flowers larger than millet grains. My fellow resident, Li Qing's son Zhengfu, told me about this.

    Birth of a Dragon

    In the summer of the year Yi Si, in the village of Weipo in Pingding, a woman named Ma Shipo, around fifty years old, had been pregnant for more than six years. This year, she finally gave birth to a dragon. The officials asked about the circumstances. The woman said that she had been pregnant for three to four years without giving birth, and her husband, Cao Zhubu, fearing it would be a sign of an omen, sent her away. As she was about to give birth, she suddenly saw people lined up in front of her, as if she were in an official court. One person stepped forward and said, "I have been entrusted to you for several years, and now it is time for me to leave. Next year, Mother will be happy!" After speaking, a white-clad person supported her and took her away. She reached the gate and fainted, losing consciousness. After a long time, she regained consciousness. Others told her that there were three thunderclaps in the darkness, and the dragon flew away from her body, leaving the place of her pregnancy unknown.

    13

    萧卞异政
    　　萧卞，贞祐中为寿州。一日，杨津巡逻回，忽马前一黄犬掉尾驯扰，且走且顾，如欲导人者。卞遣二卒随之，径至西河岸眢井中，垂头下视。卒就观之，井垠有微血，一尸在内。即驰报卞，呼地主守护之。犬又导入城，望见一客店，鸣吠不已，如有所诉。卞呼主人者至。主人识此犬，云：“是朱客所畜。数日前僦舟西河，引此犬去，今犬独来，何也？”卞即拘船户，偕至县，令主人者认之。认是船户主，因问朱客所在，未加拷讯，随即首服。又有周立，采薪州西新寺滩，为虎所食。立妻泣诉于卞。卞曰：“吾为尔一行。”率僮仆十余辈，驰至新寺滩丛薄间，见一虎，帖耳瞑目，徐行而前，若有鬼神驱执者。卞以一矢毙之。剖其腹，中环故在身。范司农拯之说。

    Explanation

    13

    Unusual Governance by Xian Bian

    During the reign of Emperor Zhenyou, Xian Bian served as the governor of Shouzhou. One day, while Yang Jin was returning from a patrol, suddenly a yellow dog appeared in front of his horse, wagging its tail gently and playfully, walking and looking back as if guiding someone. Xian Bian sent two soldiers to follow the dog, which led them directly to a dry well on the west riverbank. The soldiers lowered their heads and looked down into the well. Approaching to observe, they found a trace of blood at the edge of the well and a body inside. They immediately rushed back to report to Xian Bian and called the landowner to guard the well. The dog then led them back into the city, where they saw a guesthouse. The dog barked continuously, as if it had something to report. Xian Bian called the owner of the guesthouse. The owner recognized the dog and said, "This dog belongs to Mr. Zhu. A few days ago, he rented a boat on the west river and took this dog with him. Now the dog has come alone—why is that?" Xian Bian immediately arrested the boat owner and went with him to the county, ordering the owner to identify the body. The owner identified the body as belonging to the boat owner. Xian Bian then asked where Mr. Zhu was, and without further torture or interrogation, the boat owner immediately confessed.

    There was also a person named Zhou Li who was collecting firewood on New Temple Beach west of the state. He was eaten by a tiger. Zhou Li's wife cried and reported this to Xian Bian. Xian Bian said, "I will go once." He led more than ten servants and rushed to New Temple Beach among the dense undergrowth. There, they saw a tiger, which had flattened its ears and closed its eyes, slowly walking forward as if being driven and held by ghosts and gods. Xian Bian killed the tiger with an arrow. He cut open the tiger's belly and found a ring still in its body. This account was provided by Fan Sinao, who said it was true.

    14

    土中血肉
    　　何信叔，许州人，承安中进士。崇庆初，以父忧居乡里。庭中尝夜见光，信叔曰：“此宝器也！”率僮仆掘之。深丈余，得肉块一，如盆盎大。家人大骇，亟命埋之。信叔寻以疾亡。妻及家属十余人相继殁。识者谓：“肉块，太岁也！祸将发，故光怪先见。”

    Explanation

    14

    Hearth Soil and Flesh

    He Xinsu, from Xuzhou, passed the imperial examinations during the Cheng'an era. In the early Chongqing era, he returned to his hometown due to his father's passing. One night, he saw a strange light in the courtyard and said, "This must be a treasure!" He led his servants to dig it up. They dug about ten feet deep and found a block of flesh as large as a basin. The family was greatly alarmed and quickly buried it. Soon after, He Xinsu died of illness. His wife and over ten family members also died in succession. Scholars say, "The flesh was the Tai Sui! The disaster was about to strike, hence the strange phenomena appeared first."

    15

    玉食之祸
    　　燕人刘伯鱼，以赀雄大定间。性资豪侈，非珍膳不下筋。闲舍数百人，悉召尚食诸人居之，且时有赒赡。问知肉食之品，或一二效之。既老而病，财日削，郁郁以死。十数年后，两儿行丐于市。玉食之祸，耳目所见不知其几人！聊记此耳。二事亦司农云。
    　　京娘墓
    　　都转运使王宗元老之父础，任平山令。元老年二十许，初就举选，肄业县廨之后园。一日晚，步花石间，与一女子遇。问其姓名，云：“我前任杨令女。”元老悦其稚秀，微言挑之，女不怒而笑，因与之合。他日寒食，元老为友招，击丸于园西隙地。仆有指京娘墓窝杨者，元老因问京娘为谁？同辈言：“前令杨公幼女，字曰京娘，方笄而死，葬此。”元老闻杨令之女，心始疑之。归坐书舍，少须，女至。娇啼宛转，将进复止。谓元老曰：“君已知我，复何言也！幽明异路，亦难久处。今试期在迩，君必登科，中间小有龃龉，至如有疾，亦当力疾而往。当见君辽阳道中。

    Explanation

    15

    The Disaster of Luxurious Living
    　　A man from Yan named Liu Boyu was wealthy and influential during the Dading period. By nature, he was extravagant and luxurious, refusing to eat unless it was a delicacy. His household housed hundreds of people, and he summoned all the cooks to reside there, often providing them with charity. He would ask about the quality of the meat and sometimes imitate their practices. When he grew old and fell ill, his wealth dwindled, and he died in sorrow and depression. Ten years after his death, his two sons went begging in the market. The disaster of luxurious living is a lesson that I have seen with my own eyes, and I cannot say how many others have suffered the same fate! I merely record this here. These two stories were also told by the Director of Agriculture.

    The Tomb of Jingniang
    　　The father of Wang Zongyuanlao, who served as the Director of Transport, was named Chu and served as the magistrate of Pingshan. When Wang was in his twenties, he first took the imperial examinations and studied in the garden behind the county office. One evening, while walking among the flower stones, he met a woman. He asked her name, and she replied, "I am the daughter of the previous magistrate Yang." Wang was pleased by her youthful beauty and gently teased her. The woman did not get angry but smiled, and so they had a relationship. On a later Cold Food Festival, Wang was invited by a friend to play with a ball in the empty land west of the garden. A servant pointed out the grave of Jingniang, and Wang asked who Jingniang was. His companions said, "She was the young daughter of the previous magistrate Yang, named Jingniang, who died at the age of 15 and was buried here." Upon hearing that Jingniang was the daughter of the previous magistrate Yang, Wang began to suspect her identity. Returning to his study, he waited a short while before the woman arrived. She wept softly, hesitating as she approached. She said to Wang, "You already know me, so what more can be said? The paths of the living and the dead are different, and it is also difficult to stay for long. The exam period is near, and you will surely pass. There will be minor difficulties in the middle, and even if you are sick, you should try your best to go. You will meet me on the road to Liaoyang."

    16

    ”言讫而去。元老寻病。父母不欲令就举。月余小愈，元老锐意请行，以车载之。途次辽河淀，霖雨泥淖，车不能进。同行者鞭马就道。车独行数里而轴折。元老忧不知所为。忽有田夫，腰斤斧负轴而来，问之，匠者也。元老叹曰：“此地前后二百里无民居，今与匠者值，非阴相耶！”治轴讫，将行，俄见一车，车中人即京娘也。元老惊喜曰：“尔亦至此乎？”京娘曰：“君不记辽阳道中相见之语乎？知君有难，故来相慰耳！”元老问：“我前途所至，可得知否？”京娘即登车，第言“尚书珍重”而已。元老不数日达上京，擢第。明昌中为运使，车驾享太室，摄礼部尚书。数日而薨。

    Explanation

    16

    After finishing his speech, he left. Soon after, the elder fell ill. His parents did not want him to undertake the journey. After a month, he slightly recovered, and the elder determinedly requested to go, having him carried in a cart. On the way, they reached the Liaohe Plain, where continuous heavy rain and muddy conditions made the cart unable to proceed. Those traveling with him whipped their horses to continue on the road, but the cart alone traveled several miles before its axle broke. The elder was distressed and did not know what to do. Suddenly, a peasant appeared, carrying an axe and a saw, and approached the cart. When asked, he identified himself as a craftsman. The elder sighed and said, "In this place, there are no human settlements for two hundred miles in either direction. Now encountering this craftsman, it is not by chance but by hidden assistance!" After repairing the axle, they were about to continue their journey when suddenly another cart appeared, and the person in the cart was none other than Jingniang. The elder was surprised and delighted, saying, "You have also come here?" Jingniang replied, "Do you not remember our conversation on the road to Liaoyang? Knowing you would face difficulties, I came to comfort you!" The elder asked, "Can you tell me where I will be going next?" Jingniang climbed onto the cart and simply said, "Minister, take care," before departing. Within a few days, the elder arrived at the capital and passed his examination. During the Mingchang period, he served as a transport commissioner. When the emperor participated in a ceremony at the Taishi, he acted as the Minister of Rites. A few days later, he died.

    17

    神霄丹宝
    　　宣和方士，烧水银为黄金，铸为钱。在神霄者，其文曰“神霄丹宝”；五福者曰“五福丹宝”；太乙者亦如之。汴梁下，钱归内府，海陵以赐幸臣。得者以为帽环，服之不中暍云。内藏库使王寿孙说
    　　槄画
    　　西京田叟，自号瓦盆子，年七十余。所作《尧民图》，青缣为地，槄桦皮为之。暗室中作小窍取明，与主客谈笑为之。尝戏于袖中掏虱数枚，乱掷客衣上，客以为真虱而拾之。其技如此。性刚狷，自神其艺，不轻与人。己所不欲，虽千金不就也。盖槄画不见于书传，当自此人始耳。事见平阳都运使张伯英文

    Explanation

    17

    Shenxiao Danbao
    During the Xuanhe era, alchemists transformed mercury into gold and cast it into coins. Those in the Shenxiao palace had the inscriptions "Shenxiao Danbao"; those for the Five Blessings were inscribed with "Wufu Danbao"; and those for Taiyi were similarly inscribed. When Kaifeng fell, the coins went to the imperial treasury, and Emperor Wanyan Liang of the Jin Dynasty gave them to his favored officials. Those who received them used them as hat rings, believing that wearing them would prevent heatstroke. This was recounted by Wáng Shòu Sūn, the Director of the Imperial Treasury.

    Slippery Painting
    An elderly farmer from the Western Capital, who called himself "Clay Pot Child," was over seventy years old. He created a painting called "The People of Yao," using green silk as the base and birch bark for the painting. He made a small hole in a dark room to get light and painted while talking and laughing with his guests. Once, he playfully picked lice from his sleeves and scattered them onto his guests' clothes, who thought they were real lice and picked them up. His skill was remarkable. He was a stern and reclusive person, proud of his art, and did not easily share it with others. If something he did not want himself, he would not accept it even if offered a thousand gold pieces. Slippery painting is not recorded in books, and it is said to have started with this person. This is documented in the records of Zhang Boyiwen, the Director of the Transport Office in Pingyang.

    18

    枸杞
    　　泰和初，定陶古城崩摧。出一枸杞根，方广一尺许，作卧狗状。足尾皆具，觜亦有细毛。上一枝直出。县外一农家得之，里社传玩。寻为县官所夺。崔君佐见此，时年十五六矣。
    　　诗谶
    　　梁仲经赴官，咸平道中，有诗云：“山云欲雨花先惨，客路无人鸟亦悲。”刘御史云卿诗：“坏壁秋镫挑梦破，老梧寒雨滴愁生。”李治中平甫云：“落叶扫不尽，寒花看即休。”未几皆下世。殆诗谶也！至如杨敏行《昼眠》云：“身如蝉蜕一榻上，梦逐杨花千里飞。”真鬼语，何谶之有！
    　　敏之兄诗谶
    　　敏之兄，贞祐元年癸酉中秋日，约与王元卿、田德秀、田献卿辈燕集，而其夜阴晦，罢。敏之有诗云：“佳辰无物慰相思，先赏空吟昨夜诗。莫倦更深仍坐待，密云还有暂开时。”王、田戏曰：“诗境不开廓，君才尽耶？”敏之叹曰：“我得年仅三十，境界得开廓否？”明年遭城陷之祸，年才三十二。

    Explanation

    18

    Translation

    枸杞

    At the beginning of the Tahe era, the ancient city wall of Dingtao collapsed. A lycium root emerged, approximately one foot square, shaped like a lying dog. It had feet and a tail, and even fine hair around its mouth. A branch grew straight up from it. A farmer outside the county obtained it, and the village community passed it around to admire. Soon, it was taken by the county official. Cui Junzuo saw this when he was around fifteen or sixteen years old.

    Poetic Prophecy

    Liang Zhongjing, on his way to his official post, wrote a poem on the road to Xianping: "Mountain clouds signal rain, flowers look sad first; on the traveler's road, even birds are sad." Liu Yushi Yunqing wrote: "Broken walls, autumn lamps, dreams shattered; old wutong trees, cold rain, sorrow arises." Li Zhong Pingfu wrote: "Fallen leaves cannot be swept away; cold flowers, look at them and they are gone." Not long after, they all passed away. It is likely a poetic prophecy! As for Yang Minxing's poem "Daytime Sleep," which says: "Body like a cicada shedding its shell on a bed; dreams follow willow catkins for a thousand miles," it is truly ghostly language. What prophecy is there?

    Poetic Prophecy of Cui Minzhi's Brother

    On the Mid-Autumn Festival of the first year of the Zhenyou era, Cui Minzhi's brother planned to meet with Wang Yuanqing, Tian Deshou, and Tian Xianqing. But that night was dark and gloomy, and the gathering was canceled. Cui Minzhi wrote a poem: "On a good day, nothing comforts longing; first, I recited the poem from last night. Do not grow tired, wait until late night; dense clouds will occasionally clear." Wang and Tian joked, "The poetic realm is not open; has your talent run out?" Cui Minzhi sighed, "I will only live to be thirty; will the realm open up?" The next year, he suffered the disaster of the city's fall, and he was only thirty-two.

    19

    申伯胜诗兆
    　　高平申万全，字伯胜，正大中，以史院编修官从宗室庆山南征。道中有诗云：“回首西风谢敝庐。崎岖又复逐戎车。人生行止元无定，一苇江湖听所如。”不数日，溺淮水死。
    　　天庆鹤降
    　　忻州西城，半在九龙冈之上。置宣圣庙、铁佛寺、天庆观，为州之镇。天庆观老君殿尊像极高大，唐七帝列侍。父老云：是神人所塑。晋天福二年重修。每岁二月十五日，道家号“贞元节，”是日有鹤来会。多至数十，少亦不绝一二，翔舞坛殿之上，良久乃去。州人聚观，旁近城上。州剌史约：先见鹤者有赏。四远黄冠及游客，来者三日不绝。贞祐兵乱，殿废，鹤遂不至。

    Explanation

    19

    Shen Bosheng's Poem as an Omen

    Shen Wanquan of Gaoping, styled Bosheng, was a historian during the reign of Emperor Zhengda. He followed Prince Qingshan of the imperial clan on a southern campaign as a compiler of historical records. On the journey, he wrote a poem that said:

    "Turning back to the west wind, I bid farewell to my humble abode.
    Once again, I follow the military chariot through rugged terrain.
    The course of life is inherently uncertain,
    Like a single reed on the lake, I drift wherever fate takes me."

    A few days later, he drowned in the Huai River and died.

    The Descent of Cranes at Tianqing Temple

    In the western part of Xinzhou, half of the city lies on the Nine Dragon Ridge. There are the Temple of the Sage, the Iron Buddha Temple, and the Tianqing Temple, which serve as the city's landmarks. The Tianqing Temple has a grand statue of Laozi in its main hall, attended by statues of seven Tang emperors. The elders say that these statues were sculpted by divine beings. The temple was rebuilt in the second year of Tianfu during the Later Jin dynasty. Every year on the 15th day of the second lunar month, known as the "Zhengyuan Festival" in Taoism, cranes gather at the temple. They often come in dozens, but even a few are not uncommon. They soar and dance above the altar and halls, staying for a long time before departing. The people of the city gather to watch, and the city walls are crowded with spectators. The local governor decreed that those who see the cranes first would receive a reward. Taoist priests and tourists from afar came in an unbroken stream for three days. During the military chaos of the Zhenyou period, the temple was destroyed, and the cranes no longer came.

    20

    告成旱魃
    　　贞祐初，洛阳界夏旱甚。登封西四十里告成，人传有旱魃为虐。父老云：“旱魃至，必有火光随之。”命少年辈合昏后凭高望之，果见火光入一农民家，随以大棓击之。火焰散乱，有声如驰。古人说，旱魃长三尺，其行如风。至于有驰声，则不载也。
    　　玉儿当是其名
    　　太原庙学，旧有鬼妇人。是宋时一提刑妾，为正室妒，捶而死，倒埋学旁，其处有桑生焉。此鬼时入斋舍，与人戏语，然不为祟也。大定中，有数人夜宿时习斋。三更后，忽闻窗外履声，须臾入斋，以手遍拊睡者云：此人及第，此人不及第。既而曰：“休惊、休惊也。”及至后，皆如其言。学正马持正说。睡者赵文卿、段国华、郭及之

    Explanation

    20

    Drought and the Drought Spirit

    In the early years of the Zhenyou era, there was a severe drought in the Luoyang region. In Guo Cheng, forty miles west of Dengfeng, people said that a drought spirit was causing harm. The elders reported: "When the drought spirit appears, there is always a fire-like light accompanying it." They instructed young men to watch from a high place after dusk. Sure enough, they saw a fire-like light enter a farmer's house, and they struck it with a large club. The flame scattered, and there was a sound like galloping horses. According to ancient texts, the drought spirit is three feet tall and moves as swiftly as the wind. The description of a galloping sound is not commonly found in traditional accounts.

    The Ghost of the Temple School

    In Taiyuan, there was a temple school where a ghost woman appeared. She was the concubine of a high-ranking official during the Song dynasty. She was beaten to death by the official's wife and buried upside down beside the school, where a mulberry tree grew. This ghost sometimes entered the study rooms and played games with the students, but she did not cause any harm. During the Dading era, several students stayed overnight in the study room. After midnight, they suddenly heard footsteps outside the window. Soon, the ghost entered the room and touched each of the sleeping students, saying, "This one will pass the imperial examination, and this one will not." She then reassured them, saying, "Don't be startled, don't be startled." As predicted, all the students' outcomes matched her words. Scholar Ma Chizheng recounted this story. The students involved were Zhao Wenqing, Duan Guohua, and Guo Jizhi.

    21

    王氏金马
    　　太原王氏，上世业医，有阴德闻里中。至君玉之父，翁母皆敬神佛。一净室中安置经像，扃钥甚严，于洒扫母亦亲为之。一日晚，入室中焚诵，忽供几下一细小物跳跃而出，有光随之，须臾，作声如马嘶。母起立祝曰：“古老传有金马驹，今真见之！果欲送福，来老妇衣襟中！”即以襟迎之，此物一跳而上，视之，金马也！君玉以天眷二年第，器玉、汝玉皇统元年相次科第。乡人荣之，号“三桂王氏。”府尹并以“三桂”名所居之坊。翁四子，三子登科，一子以荫补。至其孙仲泽，复为名进士，文章、政事、谈辨、字画，大为时辈所推。金马方广三寸，金作枣瓤色，项颈微高，尾上揭如艾炷，髀股圆滑。兵乱之后，予曾见之。浚州清卿房约为赋《金马辞》也

    Explanation

    21

    The Golden Horse of the Wang Family
    　　The Wang family from Taiyuan has been engaged in medicine for generations, accumulating hidden virtue known in the village. By the time of Junyu's father, both the grandfather and grandmother revered the gods and Buddha. In a clean room where scriptures and images were placed, the lock and key were very strict, and the grandmother personally did the sweeping and cleaning. One evening, while burning incense and reciting scriptures, a small object suddenly jumped out from under the table, followed by a light. In a moment, it made a sound like a horse neighing. The grandmother stood up and wished, saying, "Ancient legends speak of a golden foal; now I truly see it! If you truly wish to bring good fortune, come into the old woman's lapel!" She immediately welcomed it with her lapel, and the object jumped up once. Looking at it, it was a golden horse! Junyu passed the imperial examination in the second year of Tianjuan, and Qi Yu and Ru Yu passed the imperial examinations in the first year of Huangtong in succession. The villagers honored them, calling them the "Three Gui Wang Family." The governor also named the street where they lived "Three Gui." The grandfather had four sons, three of whom passed the imperial examinations, and one son was appointed through imperial favor. Down to his grandson Zhongze, who became a famous Jinshi (imperial scholar), his writing, governance, debate, and calligraphy were greatly admired by his contemporaries. The golden horse was three inches square, the gold was the color of dates, the neck was slightly raised, the tail was raised like a cone of mugwort, and the thighs and legs were round and smooth. After the chaos of war, I have seen it. Junzhou Qingqing Fangyue composed the "Ode to the Golden Horse."

    22

    王云鹤
    　　王中立，字汤臣，岢岚人。博览强记，问无不知。少日治《易》，有声场屋。家豪于财，客日满门，延待备极丰腆。其自奉则日食淡汤饼一杯而已。年未四十丧妻。不娶，亦不就举，独处一室中如僧。如是三四年乃出。时人觉其谈吐高阔，诗画超绝，若有物附之者。问之不言也。大安初，遇闲闲赵公于平定，遗之诗曰：“寄与闲闲傲浪仙，枉随诗酒堕凡缘。黄尘遮断来时路，不到蓬山五百年。”因言：唐士大夫五百人，皆仙人谪降。为世味所著，亦有迷而不返者，如公与我皆是也。一日来都下，馆于闲闲公家。《中秋》诗有：“印透山河影，照开天地心。人世有昏晓，我胸无古今”之句，闲闲大奇之。因索墨水一盂，如言与之。

    Explanation

    22

    Wang Yunhe
    　　Wang Zhongli, courtesy name Tangchen, was from Kailan. He had an extensive reading and a strong memory, knowing no question. In his youth, he studied the Yi Jing and was famous in the examination halls. His family was wealthy, and guests filled his door daily, treated with utmost generosity and luxury. However, his self-provision was merely a cup of plain soup and noodles each day. Before reaching forty, he lost his wife. He did not remarry, nor did he take up the imperial examinations, living alone in a room like a monk. After three to four years, he emerged. People noticed that his speech was lofty and broad, his poetry and paintings unparalleled, as if something mystical was attached to him. When asked, he remained silent. In the early years of the Da'an era, he met Zhao Gong, the leisurely scholar, in Pingding and left him a poem saying, "Entrust to the idle, free-spirited scholar, in vain, following poetry and wine, falling into worldly entanglements. Yellow dust blocks the path back, not reaching the fairyland for five hundred years." He then said, "Five hundred scholars of the Tang dynasty were all demigods who descended. Tainted by the flavors of the world, some are lost and do not return, like you and I are also such." One day, he came to the capital and stayed at Zhao Gong's house. His Mid-Autumn Festival poem included the lines, "The imprint penetrates the shadow of mountains and rivers, illuminating the heart of heaven and earth. The world has day and night, but my heart has no past or present." Zhao Gong found these lines extraordinary. He then asked for a bowl of ink and water, and as he said, he gave it to him.

    23

    明旦不告而去。壁闲留“龟鹤”二字，广长一丈，墨水具在不知何物书之也。少之，先生从外来，问所以然，不答。题其旁云：“天地之间一古儒，醒来不记醉中书。旁人错比神仙字，只恐神仙字不如。”先生诗如：“醉袖舞嫌天地窄，诗情狂压海山平。忽惊风浪耳边过，不觉神形来世中。因君感激从君说，凿破机关有亦惊。”此类甚多。人有问世外事者，亦一二言之。好作擘窠大字，势极飞动，闲闲极爱之。屏山李之纯尝见先生，商略前代人物，引先儒论议数十条在目前，如人人自相诘难，然后以己意断之。以为辨博中第一流也。临终豫克死期，如言而逝。年四十九。晚年易名云鹤，号拟栩道人。人物如世画吕公，肩微耸耳。

    Explanation

    23

    The next morning, he left without saying goodbye. On the wall, he left the characters "龟鹤" (tortoise and crane), each one zhang in width and length. The ink was present, but it is unknown what wrote it. After a while, the master returned from outside, and when asked about the reason for this, he did not answer. He wrote beside the characters: "Between heaven and earth, there is one ancient Confucian scholar. Awake, he does not remember the writing done in a drunken state. Others mistakenly compare it to immortal characters, only fearing that immortal characters are not as good." The master's poems, such as: "In a drunken sleeve dance, he finds the sky and earth too narrow; his wild poetic passion presses the sea and mountains flat. Suddenly startled by the wind and waves passing by his ear, he unconsciously brings his spirit and form to the other world. Because of you, he is grateful and follows your words, breaking through the mechanism, even if there is, it is also shocking." There are many such poems. When someone asks about matters outside the world, he also answers with a few words. He likes to write large characters, which are extremely dynamic and lively. He loves them very much. The man from Pingshan named Li Zhipin once met the master, discussing the people of previous generations, citing dozens of points from ancient scholars in front of them, as if everyone were challenging each other, then judging them based on his own opinion. He considered this to be among the best in eloquence and knowledge. On the verge of death, he previously set the date of his passing, and died as he had predicted. He was forty-nine years old. In his later years, he changed his name to Yunhe and was nicknamed Pseudo-Xu Daoist. His appearance resembled a worldly painting of Mr. Lü, with slightly raised shoulders and ears.

    24

    董国华
    　　董文甫，字国华，潞人，承安中进士。资淳质，泊于世味，人知重之，而不知其何所得也。子安仁，亦学道。闲居宝丰，父子闭户读书。朝夕不给，晏如也。先生历金昌府判官、礼部员外。正大中，以公事至杞县。自知死期，作书与家人及同官，又与杞县令佐诗，多至三十余首。书毕坐化。
    　　卫文仲
    　　卫文仲，襄城人，承安中进士。性好淡泊，读书学道，故仕宦不进。平居好歌东坡《赤壁词》。临终沐浴易衣，召家人告以后事，即命闭户。危坐床上，诵《赤壁词》，又歌末后二句。歌罢怡然而逝。

    Explanation

    24

    董国华

    董文甫，字国华，潞人，承安中进士。他天性淳朴，对世事无欲无求，人们都敬重他，却不知他为何能如此。他的儿子安仁，也学习道学。父子二人隐居在宝丰，闭门读书。虽生活困顿，却依然平静自若。董文甫曾任金昌府判官、礼部员外郎。正大年间，因公事前往杞县。他预知自己的死期，便写信给家人和同僚，并为杞县的县令和佐官作诗，多达三十多首。写完信后，他安然坐化。

    卫文仲

    卫文仲，襄城人，承安中进士。他性格淡泊，喜欢读书学道，因此在仕途上没有多大进展。平日里，他喜欢吟唱苏轼的《赤壁词》。临终时，他沐浴更衣，召来家人交代后事，随后命人关上门。他端坐于床，诵读《赤壁词》，又吟唱了最后两句。唱罢，他安详地去世了。

    25

    一行墓石记
    　　刘太博机，贞祐兵乱后，自管湖州刺史，迁济州。民居官舍皆被焚。机复立州宅。掘一黄土坡，偶值古冢，乃唐一行禅师墓。有石记云：“刘机当破吾墓。”
    　　明月泉
    　　明月泉，在五台山中。人至泉所，以纱帛障眼，下视泉水，或见月在水中，故泉以为号。历数千百人，乃一二见之。大参杨叔玉，五台人，为予言：“明月泉吾所亲见，非传闻也！”
    　　石守道心化石
    　　徂徕石守道墓，在奉符。泰和中，墓崩，诸孙具棺葬。骸骨与常人无异，独其心如合两手，已化石矣。
    　　毁宝鼎
    　　皇统中修内司，烧琉璃瓦。毁一大鼎，三日不镕。鼎欲败，有声如雷，闻三十里外。人谓：成败有数，数与阸会，虽神物不能自保，不特此鼎矣！希颜说
    　　田鼠
    　　正大壬戌，内乡北山农民告田鼠食稼。鼠大如兔，十百为群，所过禾稼为空。猎户射得数头，有重十余斤者，毛色似水獭。未尝闻如此大鼠也。

    Explanation

    25

    一行墓石记

    Dai Bo Ji, after the military chaos of the Zhenyou era, was appointed as the governor of Huzhou and later transferred to Jizhou. Both civilian and official residences were burned down. Dai Bo Ji then rebuilt the state residence. While digging into a yellow earth slope, he accidentally encountered an ancient tomb, which turned out to be the tomb of the Tang dynasty monk Yi Xing. There was a stone inscription that said, "Dai Bo Ji will destroy my tomb."

    明月泉

    The Moonlight Spring is located in Wutai Mountain. When people arrive at the spring, they cover their eyes with silk or cloth and look down at the spring water, sometimes seeing the moon reflected in it, hence the spring's name. After thousands of people, only one or two have seen this phenomenon. Grand Censor Yang Shuyu, a native of Wutai, told me, "I personally saw the Moonlight Spring, not just heard about it!"

    石守道心化石

    The tomb of Stone Shoudao is located in Fengfu. During the Taihe period, the tomb collapsed, and his grandchildren prepared a coffin for burial. The bones were no different from those of ordinary people, but his heart was like two hands joined together, already turned to stone.

    毁宝鼎

    During the Huantong period, the Internal Works Department was burning glazed tiles. They destroyed a large tripod, which did not melt for three days. The tripod was about to break, and there was a sound like thunder, heard thirty miles away. People say: success and failure are determined by fate, and fate meets with calamity. Even divine objects cannot protect themselves, not just this tripod! Xiyang said.

    田鼠

    During the Zhengda Renxu period, farmers in the northern hills of Neixiang reported that field mice were eating crops. The mice were as big as rabbits, and they came in groups of ten or a hundred, leaving the fields they passed through barren. Hunters shot and caught several of them, some weighing more than ten pounds, with fur color similar to that of otters. I have never heard of such large mice before.

    26

    天魔祟
    　　泰和末，雷景滂任寿州防御判官，弟希颜亦到官。有官妓香香，为魔所祟，神志恍惚，或睡数日不起。希颜谓其同列者言：“有一妇人为天魔所著，挈上浮图颠，凡妇意所欲，无不立致。一日见布幔车过塔下，妇谓魔言：‘车中贵人妻，汝取其钗来！’魔去良久乃至，无所得。妇问故，曰：‘彼福人，有神护之，望而不得前。’妇又问：‘彼以贵人妻，故有神护也？’曰：‘不缘贵人，但其不食牛肉故耳！’妇即发愿：‘我若脱此祟，不但我终身不食牛肉，誓尽此生劝人不食。’言未竟，魔大骂而去，遂不复至。妇大呼求救，其家以绳挽之而下，竟得全活。阿香能不食牛肉，发愿神佛前，祟宜不能近。”同列以其言告香，香即发愿。后十余日，靓妆袨服持酒来谢云：“得学士所教，今为平人矣！”

    Explanation

    26

    A Celestial Demon Affliction

    At the end of the Tahe era, Lei Jingpang served as the defense judge of Shouzhou, and his brother Xiyán also took up his post there. There was an official prostitute named Xiangxiang who was afflicted by a celestial demon, causing her to be mentally confused and sometimes sleep for several days without waking. Xiyán told his colleagues, “There is a woman possessed by a celestial demon who was taken to the top of a pagoda. Whatever she desired, the demon could immediately fulfill. One day, she saw a curtained carriage pass by the base of the pagoda and told the demon, ‘The wife of a nobleman is inside the carriage; go and fetch her hairpin!’ The demon went and came back after a long time, having found nothing. The woman asked why, and the demon replied, ‘That woman is blessed, and a spirit protects her, so I could not approach.’ The woman then asked, ‘Is it because she is the wife of a nobleman that she has a spirit to protect her?’ The demon answered, ‘It is not because she is a noblewoman, but because she does not eat beef!’ The woman immediately made a vow, ‘If I can be freed from this affliction, I will not only abstain from eating beef for the rest of my life, but I will also vow to encourage others to do the same.’ Before she finished speaking, the demon cursed and left, and it never returned. The woman cried out for help, and her family lowered her down with a rope, and she was ultimately saved. Since Xiangxiang could abstain from eating beef and made a vow before the gods and Buddhas, the demon could no longer approach her.” The colleagues relayed these words to Xiangxiang, and she made the same vow. After more than ten days, she came dressed in fine attire, holding wine to express her gratitude, saying, “Thanks to the teachings of the learned man, I am now a normal person!”

    27

    神哥
    　　孙国镇内翰族妇，有为山魈所污者。魈自言：“汝若资用所阙，我能立致。”尝积绢满庭，皆有真定库印。妇家以官物累己，乞屏去。俄顷，失绢所在。又一白马，金鞍宝勒，不知从来，而系之枥下。家人益惧。祈请良久，马忽不见。诸子窃议，呼魈为“五郎”，云：“设若人家无嗣，能为致一子否？”明旦，一孩子面目如画，锦绷绣褓，卧之床上。老幼拜祷，不愿受。竟留之。因字之曰“神哥”。年六岁病卒。

    27

    Shen Ge

    A woman from the family of the Secretary of State (内翰) of Sun Guozhen was defiled by a mountain spirit (山魈). The spirit said, "If you lack resources, I can bring them about immediately." It once gathered a pile of silk in the courtyard, all bearing the seal of the True Definition Treasury (真定库印). The woman's family, burdened by official property, begged for its removal. Soon after, the silk disappeared. Then, a white horse with a golden saddle and precious reins appeared, of unknown origin, and was tied to a manger. The family became increasingly afraid. After praying for a long time, the horse suddenly vanished.

    The children discussed the matter in secret and called the mountain spirit "Wu Lang." They asked, "If a family has no heir, can you bring about one?" The next morning, a child appeared with a well-formed face, wrapped in a luxurious silk swaddling cloth embroidered with patterns, and placed on the bed. The elderly and young people prayed for the child, but they did not wish to accept him. Finally, they decided to keep him. They therefore named him "Shen Ge." He died of illness at the age of six.

    28

    王确为兄所挞
    　　外祖柔服簿王君，大定中卒官。其最小弟确，酗酒，欺幼孤。外祖母张容忍既久，无所控诉，遂病不能起。一夕，与诸女并寝。夜半镫暗，闻骚窣声。少之，触双陆棋子乱，啧啧有声，屡叹。外祖母哭失声。因言：“五叔恃酒见陵，官法不能制。若不禁止之，母子将为鱼肉矣！”不数日，确承醉，夜出定襄，归，至赵村，值外祖于中路，画地大数，随以马策乱捶。确抱头窜伏，仅能至家。取火视之，衫服碎破，肿青满背。明日，就外祖像前百拜谢。后酒亦不饮。

    Explanation

    28

    Wang, being drunk, abused his younger brother's widow and orphaned children. The grandmother, Zhang, had endured Wang's behavior for a long time and had no one to turn to for help, so she fell ill and could not get up. One night, she slept with her daughters. In the middle of the night, when the lamp dimmed, she heard rustling sounds. Soon after, the checkers on the board were scattered, and there were sounds of clattering. She repeatedly sighed. The grandmother cried out in despair. She said, "My fifth uncle, drunk and abusive, cannot be controlled by the law. If this is not stopped, the mother and children will be at the mercy of others!" A few days later, Wang, drunk, left Dingxiang at night and returned. On the way to Zhao Village, he encountered his brother in the middle of the road, scolded him severely, and then beat him with a horsewhip wildly. Wang, holding his head, fled and barely made it home. When they lit a fire to examine him, his clothes were torn to pieces, and his back was covered with bruises. The next day, he bowed a hundred times in front of the image of his grandfather as a sign of apology. Afterward, he also stopped drinking.

    29

    王全美母氏诗语
    　　定襄王全美之母，从幼事佛，既老，奉香火益勤。先不知书，忽一日，谓敏之兄，言：“外生，我漫得一句，汝看作得偈否？”举似凡十数句，惟“天机割断繁华梦，”殆似从慧中得之。母未几下世。
    　　虱异
    　　德顺破后，民居官寺皆被焚。内城之下有礮数十，垂索在故营中。人有欲解此索者，见每一索，从上至下大虱遍裹，如脂蜡灌烛然。闻汴京被攻之后亦如是。丧乱之极，天地间亦何所不有也！

    Explanation

    29

    Wang Quanmei's Mother's Poetic Words

    The mother of Wang Quanmei from Dingxiang had served Buddhism since her childhood. When she grew old, she served incense and candles even more diligently. She did not know how to read or write before, but one day, she told her brother, saying, "Nephew, I casually came up with a line. See if you can make a verse out of it." She recited several dozen lines, but only "The celestial mechanism cuts off the dream of luxury" seems to have come from her wisdom. The mother passed away shortly after.

    Strange Things about Lice

    After the fall of Dezhou, all civilian homes and government temples were burned down. There were dozens of cannons under the inner city, with ropes hanging in the old camp. Someone wanted to untie these ropes and saw that each rope was completely covered with large lice from top to bottom, like wax poured over a candle. It is said that after the attack on Bianjing (Kaifeng) it was the same. In the extreme chaos and disorder, what cannot be found in the world?

    30

    单州民妻
    　　贞祐初，虞县黄九者，从佛儿堌贼钻天怪作乱于单父，虏老幼数百。中一妇有姿色，黄欲劫取。妇阳谓贼曰：“吾夫少选至，愿一见，嫁君未晚。”及见其夫，诉以劫取之事，因指黄九恶语大骂。贼不胜愤，砍杀之，被砍处不血出，但白膏流。黄冠禹冀之说。
    　　戴十妻梁氏
    　　戴十，不知何许人。乱后，居洛阳东南左家庄，以佣为业。癸卯秋八月，一通事牧马豆田中，戴逐出之。通事怒，以马策乱捶而死。妻梁氏舁尸诣营中诉之。通事乃贵家奴，主人所倚。因以牛二头、白金一笏，就梁赎罪。且说之曰：“汝夫死亦天命。两子皆幼，得钱可以自养。就令杀此人，于死者何益？”梁氏曰：“吾夫无罪而死，岂可言利？但得此奴偿死，我母子乞食亦甘分！”众不可夺，谓梁氏曰：“汝宁欲自杀此人耶？”梁氏曰：“有何不敢！”因取刀，欲自斫之。众惧此妇愤恨通事，不令即死，乃杀之。梁氏掬血饮之，携二子去。洛阳翟志忠云。

    Explanation

    30

    The Wife of a Man from Danshou
    In the early years of the Jurchen Jin Dynasty, Huang Jiu from Yuxian, who was part of the band of rebels known as "Zhutian Guai" from Fuer Gu, caused unrest in Shanfu and captured hundreds of elderly and young people. Among them was a woman of great beauty, whom Huang Jiu wanted to take by force. The woman pretended to the bandits, saying, "My husband will arrive shortly. I would like to see him before I marry you." When she saw her husband, she told him about the act of kidnapping and then pointed at Huang Jiu and cursed him with foul language. The bandits could not bear their anger and cut her down. The place where she was cut did not bleed, but white grease flowed instead. This is explained by the theory of Huang Guan and Yu Ji.

    The Wife of Dai Shi, Liang Shi
    Dai Shi, whose origins are unknown, lived in the left village of Luoyang after the chaos, working as a hired laborer. In the eighth month of the year Gengchen, an interpreter was herding horses in a bean field. Dai drove him out. The interpreter became angry and beat him to death with a whip. His wife, Liang Shi, carried the body to the camp to complain. The interpreter was a servant of a noble family and relied upon by his master. They offered two cows and a piece of white gold to Liang Shi to redeem the crime. They also said to her, "Your husband's death is also fate. Your two sons are young, and with money, you can support yourselves. Even if this person is killed, what good is it to the deceased?" Liang Shi replied, "My husband died without a crime, how can we talk about profit? But if this servant pays for his death, my mother and I will be content even if we have to beg for food!" The crowd could not persuade her. They said to Liang Shi, "Would you rather kill this person yourself?" Liang Shi replied, "What is there to be afraid of!" She then took a knife and wanted to cut him down herself. The crowd, fearing that this woman would hate the interpreter, did not let her kill him immediately, so they killed him. Liang Shi gathered blood and drank it, then took her two sons away. According to Zhai Zhizhong of Luoyang.

    31

    李昼病目
    　　聊城李昼生二子，其一失明，其一生而无目。李去岁一目复枯。问神霄何道士求治疗。何问：“渠宁作亏心事耶？”李言：“平生塑神像，急须用目睛，则往往就神像摧塌处剜取之，殆以此故耶？”丁酉岁春，何来阳平，谓予言。李吝少费，受此报！
    　　人生尾
    　　清河王博，以裁缝为业，年三十七。一日，诣聊城何道士，言：丁酉初春，醉卧一桃园中。忽梦一神人，被金甲执戟，至其旁蹴之使起。王问何为神？曰：“吾为汝送尾来。”自后觉尻骨痛痒。数日，生一尾，指许大，如羊退毛尾骨然。欲勒去，痛贯心髓，炙之亦然。因自言不孝于母，使至饥饿，故受此报。每逢人看，则痛痒少止，否则不可耐也。因问何求疗。何无所措手，乃去。今在新店住。何道士云。

    Explanation

    31

    Li Zhou's Eyes Were Sick
    　　Li Zhou of Liaocheng had two sons; one was blind, and the other was born without eyes. Last year, one of his eyes dried up again. He asked the Daoist from Shentiao for treatment. The Daoist asked, "Has he ever done anything wrong?" Li replied, "All my life, I sculpted statues of gods, and whenever I needed eyeballs, I would often take them from collapsed statues. Is this the reason?" In the spring of Dingyou year, the Daoist came to Yangping and told me about it. Li was stingy with small expenses and thus received this retribution!
    　　A Human with a Tail
    　　Wang Bo of Qinghe, who makes a living as a tailor, was thirty-seven years old. One day, he visited the Daoist from Liaocheng and said: In early spring of Dingyou year, he was drunk and slept in a peach garden. Suddenly, he dreamed of a god in golden armor holding a halberd, who kicked him to make him get up. Wang asked, "Who are you?" The god replied, "I am sending you your tail." Afterward, he felt pain and itching in his coccyx. After several days, a tail grew, about the size of a finger, like the tail bone of a sheep that has shed its wool. He wanted to remove it, but the pain went through his heart and marrow, and even burning it didn't help. He said he was ungrateful to his mother, which led to his starvation, and thus he received this retribution. Every time someone looked at it, the pain and itching lessened a bit, but otherwise it was unbearable. He asked the Daoist for treatment. The Daoist had no way to treat it, so he left. Now he lives in Xin Dian. The Daoist from Shentiao said.

    32

    石公阴德
    　　国初定州唐县王八郎，姿容雄伟，膂力绝人。为相者所惑，谋作乱。因设诡计，籍乡人姓名。未及引诱，为人所告。州将高某捕获，按籍逮捕，凡数千人。高欲一切以造逆当。石公时为都司，谏止之曰：“以诡计籍人名，罪止王八。其他无豫谋者，使其在诖误之列且不可，况诬以从逆乎？”州将不悦，命他吏鞫其事。吏承风旨，文致其罪。然州将以石公一言遂疑之。明日召石公，王八而下皆自伏。“公所言，何不惜死之甚也？”石公曰：“雪人之冤，一死何惜！”州将良久曰：“有是哉！吾更思之。”明日，即从石公议，戮首恶二三人，余悉纵遣。并取旧案焚之。石公之子琚，业进士，天眷初，第一人擢第。大定中，以左丞相致政。故石公阴德，乡人无大小能备道之。

    Explanation

    32

    Zhi Gong's Hidden Virtue

    At the beginning of the Ming Dynasty, in Dingzhou Tang County, there was a man named Wang Ba, who was physically imposing and dignified, with remarkable physical strength. He was deceived by the chancellor into planning a rebellion. As a result, he set up a deceitful plan and enlisted the names of fellow villagers. Before he could begin to recruit, his plot was discovered, and he was arrested. The governor Gao, upon learning of this, arrested several thousand people according to the list. Gao wanted to charge everyone with treason. Zhi Gong, who was the commandant at the time, advised against it, saying, "By enlisting people's names through deceit, the crime should be limited to Wang Ba. Those who were not involved in the plot, it would be even worse to have them in the list of those misled, and how much more so to accuse them of rebellion?" The governor was not pleased and ordered another official to investigate the matter. The official, following the governor's orders, fabricated charges against them. However, the governor, influenced by Zhi Gong's words, began to doubt the fairness of the proceedings. The next day, he summoned Zhi Gong and asked, "Why do you go to such lengths to save these people?" Zhi Gong replied, "To clear the names of the innocent, what is there to fear in death?" After a long pause, the governor said, "You are right. I will reconsider this." The next day, he followed Zhi Gong's advice, executing the main culprits and releasing the rest. He also burned the old case files. Zhi Gong's son, Shi Jue, passed the imperial examination as the first-place winner in the early Tianjuan era and later retired as Left Chancellor. Therefore, Zhi Gong's hidden virtue was widely recognized by all villagers, regardless of age.

    33

    马三诋欺报
    　　恩州刘马三，以钩距致富。尝用诡计取邻舍袁春田。春诉于官，马三出契券为质，竟夺之。春不能平，日为乡人言：“渠诋欺如此，已将为异类矣！”马三亦自誓云：“我果诈取汝田，当如所言也！”泰和二年，马三以病死。袁春家犬乳数子，中一小花狗，腹毛纯白，有朱书：“我是恩州刘马三”七字。马三素多怨家，竟欲出钱买之。寻为州刺史所取。阖郡皆知。马氏子孙不胜其辱，购而藏于家。
    　　白神官
    　　鄜州洛交，大定中有妖人白神官者，能以左道作怪变。如平地起龙、卷袖出金手、或端坐见佛像，光怪夺目。数百里间无不归向，莫有忤其意者。外祖王君，时为此县主簿，捕得之。问所以能怪变者，皆托以天神所为。及掘得狐涎一罂，神官乃伏罪。决杖二百而死。县境为之肃然。其后吾舅彦师，再到洛交，去外祖已四十年。访旧事，父老尚能言之，因问曰：“君是杖杀白神官王主簿子孙乎？”

    Explanation

    33

    Ma San's Deceitful Report

    In Enzhou, Liu Ma San became wealthy through cunning and deceit. He once used trickery to take over the land of his neighbor Yuan Chuntian. Yuan Chuntian complained to the authorities, but Ma San produced a contract as proof and ultimately took the land. Yuan Chuntian could not accept this, and he told the villagers every day, "He has slandered and deceived like this, and has already become a different kind of being!" Ma San also swore to himself, "If I indeed fraudulently took your land, then I will do as you say!" In the second year of Taihe, Ma San died of illness. Yuan Chuntian's dog gave birth to several puppies, among which was a small spotted dog with pure white belly fur and a red inscription on its belly reading, "I am Liu Ma San of Enzhou." Ma San had many enemies, and he eventually wanted to buy the dog. The dog was soon taken by the state governor. The entire prefecture knew about it. The descendants of the Ma family could not bear the shame and bought the dog back to keep it at home.

    White Shen Guan

    In Luojiāo, Fuzhou, during the Dading era, there was a fraudster named Bai Shen Guan who could create strange phenomena using unorthodox methods. He could make dragons appear out of nowhere, pull out golden hands from his sleeves, or see Buddha statues while sitting. His tricks were so dazzling that people within hundreds of miles flocked to him, and no one dared to oppose him. My maternal uncle, Wang Jun, was the county magistrate at the time and captured him. When asked how he could create these strange phenomena, Bai Shen Guan claimed it was done by gods. Later, when they dug up a jar of fox saliva, Bai Shen Guan confessed his crimes. He was executed with two hundred strokes of the stick and died. The county became peaceful as a result. Later, my uncle Yan Shi returned to Luojiāo after forty years. When he asked about old matters, the elders still remembered them and asked, "Are you the descendant of County Magistrate Wang who executed Bai Shen Guan with a beating?"

    34

    贾道士前身
    　　宣德朝元观贾道士，鱼儿泊贾大夫之子，知其前身本潞州人义镇王秀才。贞祐之兵，为北骑所俘乘骑他出，逃去。骑追及，枪中其额而死。死后性不昧。顾盼中有二人来扶之，使历观诸狱，不忍恐怖，复扶之出。过一石桥，见莲花盆子中，贮恶血汁，令饮之。觉腥，口不可近，不肯饮。二人不之强，但推堕水中。既而开目，知受生此家。三日洗儿，及满月，乡邻来贺，皆见，但语不出。六七岁说前事，即求出家。父母不得已许之。送朝元观作道童。一日，俘主来观中，人说前事。俘主亦了了能记，都不差。视其额角，疮瘢犹存。

    Explanation

    34

    The Previous Life of Taoist Priest Jia

    In the Xuande era, Taoist Priest Jia of the Chao Yuan Temple was the son of Grand Secretary Jia of Yuerupo. He knew that his previous life was that of Wang Xiucai, a scholar from Yizhen in Luxiu. During the military campaigns of Emperor Xuanzong of the Jin Dynasty, he was captured by the northern cavalry and forced to ride away, but he escaped. The cavalry pursued him, and he was killed by a spear that hit his forehead. After death, his consciousness was not lost. Two people came to support him, showing him the various prisons, and he could not bear the terror, so they supported him out. He passed over a stone bridge and saw a lotus pot containing evil blood, and was ordered to drink it. He found it stinky, and his mouth could not approach it, so he refused to drink. The two people did not force him, but pushed him into the water. Afterward, he opened his eyes and knew he had been reborn into this family. On the third day, he was washed, and on the one-month celebration, neighbors came to congratulate, and he saw everything, but could not speak. At six or seven years old, he spoke about his previous life and asked to become a monk. His parents had no choice but to agree. He was sent to the Chao Yuan Temple to become a Taoist novice. One day, the captor came to the temple, and people told him about his previous life. The captor also clearly remembered, and there was no mistake. He looked at his forehead, and the scar still existed.

    35

    旬会之异
    　　定襄魏仲仪，以经童出身，得辽阳警巡院判官。将复应词赋举，与同辈结夏课，十日一宴集。中一举子物故。他日旬会，诸人感叹存殁，仍于故人设位。少选，食至，诸人举匕筯，而设位者亦然，合坐哭皆失声，竟至罢食。
    　　济源灵感
    　　济源庙，隋时建。庙后大池，邑人以海子目之。献酒及冥钱，或他有所供，悉投此海池。每岁春暮，纸灰从水底出，谓之海醮。水亦有澄彻时，池底物历历见之。或时水底酒尊、伞扇浮游水面，谓之神赐。虽重若银杯、香合，亦浮。观者环水而立，物所至，人得之，以长漉篱挹取，拜赐而去。酒尊皆有镌记，年月、姓名。饮之往往有味云。
    　　续夷坚志二
    　　贞鸡
    　　房皞希白，宰卢氏时，客至，烹一鸡。其雌绕舍悲鸣，三日不饮啄而死。文士多为诗文。予号之为“贞鸡”。

    Explanation

    35

    Translation:

    Unusual Event of a Ten-Day Gathering
    　　Wei Zhongyi from Dingxiang, having passed the imperial examinations as a child, became a judge in the police court of Liaoyang. He was preparing to retake the imperial examinations for poetry and prose and joined a summer course with his peers, gathering every ten days. One of the participants passed away. On another day of the ten-day gathering, the others expressed their feelings about the living and the dead, still setting up a place for the deceased. Soon after, the food arrived, and the others picked up their chopsticks, and the person setting up the place for the deceased did the same. They all cried together, losing their voices, and eventually stopped eating.

    Jiyuan Temple and the Sea Pond
    　　The Jiyuan Temple was built during the Sui dynasty. Behind the temple was a large pool, which the locals called the Sea Pond. Offerings of wine and paper money, or other items, were all thrown into this sea pond. At the end of spring each year, paper ashes rose from the bottom of the water, known as the Sea Offering. The water was also clear at times, and the objects at the bottom of the pool were clearly visible. Sometimes, wine vessels and parasols would float to the surface from the bottom of the water, known as divine gifts. Even heavy items like silver cups and incense boxes would float. Spectators stood around the water, and when the floating items reached them, they would pick them up with a long-handled sieve, bow, and leave. The wine vessels all had inscribed marks with dates and names. The wine often tasted good.

    Continued Stories from the Yi Jian Zhi
    　　Loyal Chicken
    　　Fang Hao Xi Bai, when serving as the governor of Luzhou, had a guest arrive and cook a chicken. The female chicken circled the house, mourning, and died after three days without eating or drinking. Many literati wrote poems and essays about the event. I named the chicken "Loyal Chicken."

    36

    王氏孝犬
    　　王怀州家小儿子五哥畜一犬，甚驯。五哥十二、三死，犬随至葬所徘徊望顾，如有所见者。自后，日一往墓侧，暮乃归。如是近百日。人以“孝犬”目之。
    　　狐锯树
    　　阳曲北郑村中社铁李者，以捕狐为业。大定末，一日张网沟北古墓中，系一鸽为饵，身在大树上伺之。二更后，群狐至，作人语云：“铁李、铁李，汝以鸽赚我耶？汝家父子，驴群相似，不肯做庄农，只学杀生。俺内外六亲，都是此贼害却。今日天数到此，好好下树来。不然，锯倒别说话！”即闻有拽锯声，大呼搘镬煮油，当烹此贼！火亦随起。铁李惧，不知所为。顾腰惟有大斧，思树倒则乱斫之。须臾天晓，狐乃去。树无锯痕，旁有牛肋数枝而已。铁李知其变幻无实，其夜复往。未一更，狐至，泣骂俱有伦。李腰悬火罐，取卷爆潜爇之，掷树下。药火发，猛作大声，群狐乱走。为网所胄，瞑目待毙，不出一语。以斧椎杀之。

    Explanation

    36

    The Filial Dog of the Wang Family

    The fifth son of the Wang family in Huizhou, named Wuge, had a very well-behaved dog. When Wuge, who was around twelve or thirteen years old, died, the dog followed him to the burial site, where it wandered and looked around as if it had seen something. Afterward, the dog went to the tomb side every day and returned at dusk. This continued for nearly a hundred days. People called it a "filial dog."

    The Foxes and the Sawed Tree

    In the village of Zheng in the north of Yangqu, there lived a man named Tie Li, whose profession was catching foxes. At the end of the Dading era, one day he set up a net in an ancient tomb north of a ditch, tying a pigeon as bait. He was on a big tree waiting for the foxes. After the second watch of the night, a group of foxes arrived and spoke in human language, saying, "Tie Li, Tie Li, did you use a pigeon to trick us? Your family, father and son, are like a herd of donkeys. You don't want to farm, only learning to kill living beings. Our relatives inside and outside are all harmed by this thief. Today the fate has come to this, come down from the tree nicely. Otherwise, we will saw it down and not talk anymore!" Immediately, they heard the sound of pulling the saw. They shouted loudly, lifting the pot to boil oil, to cook this thief. The fire also started. Tie Li was afraid, not knowing what to do. Looking at his waist, he only had a big axe. Thinking if the tree falls, he would chop it randomly. Soon it became dawn, and the foxes left. The tree had no saw marks, only several cow ribs on the side. Tie Li knew that their transformations were not real. That night he went again. Before the first watch of the night, the foxes came, weeping and cursing in a reasonable manner. Tie Li hung a fire pot on his waist, took some firecrackers, secretly lit them, and threw them under the tree. The firecrackers exploded, making a loud noise. The foxes ran around in confusion. They were caught by the net, closed their eyes waiting to die, not uttering a word. He killed them with an axe.

    37

    济水鱼飞
    　　壬寅岁，济源水中鱼飞起，鸟鹊啄食之而堕，人取食，无他异。甲辰冬，安贤镇西南之马陵，平旦无风云，忽空中堕鱼七八头，不知所来。又比济源者差小。陶朱种鱼法：池中著鳖，不尔，则飞去。
    　　石佛动
    　　正大八年，滕州东三里，有石佛一躯，忽自动摇者数月。及州将死，乃定。禹冀之闻张仲安说。
    　　鬼拔树
    　　兴定末，曹州一农民，一日行道中，忽骤雨。闻空中人语云：“敢否”？俄又闻大笑声。此人行半里，见道左大柳树拔根出，掷之十步外；泥中印大臀髀痕，如麦笼许。盖神拔树，偃坐泥中，破笑耳。

    Explanation

    37

    Fish Flying in the Ji River

    In the year Renyin (1242), fish were seen flying in the waters of Jiyuan. Birds pecked at them, causing them to fall, and people collected and ate them, with no other strange occurrences. In the year Jia Chen (1244), at dawn without wind or clouds, several fish suddenly fell from the sky in the southwest of Anxian Town, southwest of Ma Ling. It was unknown where they came from. The fish were slightly smaller than those from Jiyuan. According to the fish farming methods of Tao Zhu Gong: "Put turtles in the pond, otherwise they will fly away."

    Stone Buddha Moving

    In the eighth year of Zhengda (1251), a stone Buddha in Tengzhou, three miles east of the city, suddenly began to move for several months. It stopped moving only after the local official died. This was reported by Zhang Zhong'an of Yuji.

    God Pulling Out a Tree

    At the end of the Xingding period (1224), a farmer in Caizhou saw a sudden rainstorm while walking in the fields. He heard voices in the air saying, "Dare you?" Then he heard a loud laugh. Half a mile away, he saw a large willow tree uprooted and thrown ten steps away. The mud was imprinted with large buttock marks, about the size of a grain basket. It was a god who uprooted the tree, sitting down in the mud, laughing loudly.

    38

    高尉阴德
    　　高工部有邻，字德卿。父飞狐令集，尝尉南和，以公事活千余人。德卿生于此邑。四十年后，拜安国军节度使。父老有及见当时事者，扶杖迎劳，欢呼马前。德卿亦为立碑尉厅，道所以阴德阳报之故。不逾月，子嵩、犹子铸，同榜登科。时人荣之。
    　　胡公去狐
    　　胡彦高，明昌二年以廉举为即墨令。县廨在古城之隅，为妖狐所据，昼伏夜出，变化狡狯：或为狱卒，纵遣囚系；或为官妓，盗驿传被幞，媚惑男女。有迷乱至死者。邑人无如之何，反以香火奉之，余五十年矣！彦高到官，问知其然。顾谓同僚：“官舍所以居贤，今令不得居，而鬼物据之耶？”时室空已久，颓圯殊甚。即令完葺之。明日，即厅事理务，抵暮张烛而坐。夜半，狐鸣后圃中，一倡百和，少顷坌集，周匝庭内。中一大白狐据地而吼，如欲抟噬然。

    Explanation

    38

    Final Translation

    High Official’s Hidden Virtue

    Gao Gongbu, a high-ranking official, had a son named Deqing. Gao’s father once served as the magistrate of Feixu and Nanhe, saving over a thousand people through his official duties. Deqing was born in this county. Forty years later, he was appointed as the military governor of An Guo Army. The elders who had witnessed his father’s deeds welcomed him with support staff, cheering at his arrival. Deqing also erected a stele in the county office to explain the reason for hidden good deeds and public rewards. Within a month, his son Song and his nephew Zhu both passed the imperial examinations. People regarded this as a great honor.

    Governor Hu Exorcises the Fox Spirit

    Hu Yan Gao, appointed through a recommendation for integrity as the magistrate of Jimo County in the second year of the Mingchang era, faced a problem when he arrived. The county office was located in a corner of an ancient city, occupied by a mischievous fox spirit. The fox would hide during the day and emerge at night, taking on various forms: sometimes it would appear as a prison guard, releasing prisoners; sometimes it would disguise itself as an official entertainer, stealing clothing and seducing men and women. The fox’s mischief was so severe that it even led to deaths. The people of the county had no way to deal with it and instead offered incense and sacrifices to the fox, a practice that had continued for fifty years. When Hu arrived, he learned about the situation and told his colleagues, “The official residence should be occupied by virtuous people, not by spirits!” The office had been vacant for a long time and was in a state of disrepair. Hu immediately ordered it to be repaired. The next day, he sat in the office with a lit candle, determined to confront the fox. At midnight, the fox began to howl in the garden behind the office, followed by a chorus of other foxes. Soon, they surrounded the courtyard. In the center stood a large white fox, roaring as if it were ready to attack.

    39

    卒伍散走，投避无所。彦高端坐不动，而狐亦不前，良久引退。如是者三日，遂不复来。又十许日，传一女奴，跳踯歌笑，狂若寐语。彦高以朱书置奴钗间，逼逐之，奴即日知人。明旦，尉自巡逻还，遭群狐数百，由县东南去。狐复惑登州吏目江崇家一妇。崇就海岛中请道士行法：乘妇人狂乱，缚置车轮上，埋轴地中，令人转之。既久，妇人快吐腥涎，乃道是即墨狐，为胡公逐至此。即墨父老为彦高刻石，名：“胡公去狐碑。”屏山李之纯之记也。彦高，武安人，仕至凤翔同知。

    Explanation

    39

    In a panic, the soldiers fled in all directions, finding no place to hide. Yan Gao sat calmly and composed, and the foxes also did not advance. After a long while, they retreated. This situation lasted for three days, and then the foxes did not return. After another ten or so days, a female servant was possessed, leaping and laughing madly, as if speaking in her sleep. Yan Gao wrote in red ink and placed it in the servant's hairpin, forcing her away. On the same day, she regained her senses. The next morning, the magistrate returned from his patrol and encountered hundreds of foxes heading southeast of the county. The foxes again possessed a woman in the household of Jiang Chong, the magistrate of Dengzhou. Jiang Chong went to an island to invite a Taoist priest to perform rituals: binding the possessed woman to a wheel and burying the axle in the ground, then having people turn the wheel. After a while, the woman quickly spat out foul saliva, revealing that she was a fox from Jimo, driven away by Hu Gong. The elders of Jimo carved a stone in honor of Yan Gao, naming it "The Stone of Hu Gong Driving Away the Foxes." This was recorded by Li Zhi of Ping Mountain. Yan Gao, from Wu'an, served as the Deputy Magistrate of Fengxiang.

    40

    吕守诗谶
    　　吕卿，字祥卿，大兴人。刺汝州一月而罢。题诗望崧楼有：“珍重楼中旧山色，好将眉黛事新官。”未几物故。人以为诗谶云。
    　　孟内翰梦
    　　孟内翰友之，大定三年，乡、府、省、御，四试皆第一，供奉翰林。历曹王府文学，以疾寻医。久之，授同知单州军州事。丁内艰，哀毁致卒。友之未第前。梦中豫知前涂所至，其后皆验。邻人李生言：友之死之年，六月中，连夕星殒于虚轩前。汴人高公振特夫挽之曰：“见说平生梦，前途尽目前。”又云：“人嗟埋玉树，天为启文星。”诗虽不甚工，有以见友之出处之际，死生之变，造物者皆使之前知。其以海内重名畀之者，为不偶然也。

    Explanation

    40

    Poetic Prophecy of Lu Shou
    Lu Shou, courtesy name Xiangqing, was from Daxing. He served as the governor of Ruzhou for a month before being dismissed. On the Looking at Song Tower, he inscribed a poem: "Cherish the old mountain scenery in the tower, good to use the delicate eyebrows to serve the new official." Not long after, he passed away. People considered it a poetic prophecy.

    Dream of Minister Meng
    Minister Meng Youzhi, during the third year of the Dading era (1163 AD), passed all four examinations at the local, provincial, national, and imperial levels, all with first place, and served as a翰林 (Imperial Academy member). He served as a literary official in the Prince's mansion and sought medical treatment due to illness. After a long time, he was appointed as the deputy governor of the military and state affairs in Shanzhou. When he suffered the death of a close relative, he died from grief and sorrow. Before he passed the imperial examination, he foresaw his future path in dreams, and all of which later proved true. A neighbor named Li Sheng said: In the sixth month of the year when Meng passed away, stars fell continuously in front of the empty pavilion. A person from Bian (Kaifeng) named Gao Gongzhen, also known as Te Fu, wrote a poem in mourning: "It is said that his lifelong dreams, the future is all before him." He also said: "People lament the burial of the jade tree, heaven opens the star of literature."
