The poem is not very well-crafted, but it shows that in the moments of his rise and fall, life and death, the creator made him know in advance. The reason he was given a heavy reputation throughout the country, was not accidental.

    41

    麻神童
    　　麻九畴字知几，献州人。三岁识字，七岁能草书，作大字有及数尺者。所至有神童之目。章宗召见，问：“汝入宫中，亦惧怯否？”对曰：“君臣犹父子也，子宁惧父乎？”上奇之。明昌以来，以神童称者五人：太原常添寿，四岁作诗云：“我有一卷经，不用笔笔成”；合河刘文荣，六岁作诗云：“莺花新物态，日月老天公”；刘微七岁，被旨赋《凤皇来仪》；新恩张世杰，五、六岁，亦召入，赋《元妃素罗扇画梅》云：“前村消不得，移向月中栽”，其后常隐居不出；余三人皆无可称道，独知几能自树立。一旦名重天下，耆旧如闲闲公，且以“征君”目之而不名云。

    Explanation

    41

    The Child Prodigy Ma

    Ma Jiuchou, also known as Zhiji, was from Xianzhou. He recognized characters at three years old and could write cursive script at seven years old, producing large characters that could be as big as several feet. Wherever he went, he was called a prodigy. Emperor Zhang of Jin summoned him, asking, "Are you also afraid when you enter the palace?" He replied, "The relationship between ruler and subject is like that between father and son. Would a son fear his father?" The emperor found this remarkable. Since the Mingchang period, there have been five people called prodigies: Chang Tian-shou from Taiyuan, who wrote poetry at four years old with the lines, "I have a scroll of scriptures, not needing to write it down stroke by stroke"; Liu Wenrong from Hehe, who wrote poetry at six years old with the lines, "The new forms of flowers and birds, the old sky of sun and moon"; Liu Wei, who was seven years old and was ordered to compose 'The Phoenix Comes in Order'; Zhang Shijie from Xin'en, who was five or six years old and was also summoned, composing 'The Empress's White Silk Fan Painting Plum Blossoms' with the lines, "The village cannot be destroyed, moving it to the moon to plant," and later often lived in seclusion without coming out; the other three were not worthy of mention, but only Ma Jiuchou could establish himself. One day, his fame spread throughout the world, and respected elders like Xianxian Gong referred to him as a "reclusive scholar" without naming him.

    42

    陈守诚感
    　　陈大年字世德，吉州人。泰和中刺吾州。时秋旱，蝗自南而北。世德祭于石岭关，遂不入境。死囚马柏儿，移勘更数州，已十三年矣！陈已决其死，止待署字矣。陈夜祷星下：“决囚无复疑，尚虑有冤。今旱已极，囚果不冤，明当大雨；如冤，则雨且止。以此卜之。”明日大雨，遂决此囚。是岁大熟。

    Explanation

    42

    陈守诚感
    　　陈大年，字世德，是吉州人。在泰和年间担任我们州的刺史。当时正值秋季大旱，蝗虫从南向北蔓延。陈大年在石岭关进行祭祀，蝗虫便不再进入州境。有一个死囚名叫马柏儿，已经辗转多个州府调查了十三年！陈大年已经决定判处他死刑，只等签署文书。陈大年在夜晚对着星星祈祷：“决定囚犯的生死不再有疑虑，但仍然担心可能有冤情。现在旱情已经非常严重，如果囚犯确实没有冤情，明天将会下大雨；如果有冤情，那么雨就会停止。以此来占卜。”第二天果然下了大雨，于是陈大年决定释放了这个囚犯。那一年，庄稼获得了大丰收。

    43

    虞令公早慧
    　　虞令公仲文质夫，四岁赋《雪花》诗云：“琼英与玉蕊，片片落阶墀。问著花来处，东君也不知。”仕为辽相，归朝授平章政事、濮国公。
    　　陈希夷灵骨
    　　华山张超谷，陈希夷灵骨在焉。山径险绝，下临无地。河中李钦叔尝至其处。陈骨长大，异于今人，坚重腴莹如青玉。道力所至，具见于此。弟子某，遗骸亦在其旁，以陈比之，仙凡为不侔矣！
    　　马光尘画
    　　马资深之子光尘，十许岁，画山水，有远意。甫成童而卒。王子端内翰题其画云：“珠璧佳城下，丹青败稿闲。残年两行泪，绝笔数重山。”人谓童丱而以画称，且为名流所嗟惜，古亦不多见也。

    Explanation

    43

    Yú Lìnggōng, the Early Sage
    Yú Lìnggōng Zhōngwén, also known as Zhìfū, composed a poem about snowflakes at the age of four, which reads: "Jade flowers and jade buds, one by one falling on the steps. Asking where the flowers come from, even the Eastern Lord does not know." He served as a chancellor in the Liao dynasty and was granted the position of Pingzhangzhengshi and the title of Puguo Gong upon returning to the Song dynasty.

    Spiritual Remains of Chen Xi Yi
    In Zhang Chaogu, Mount Hua, the spiritual remains of Chen Xi Yi are found. The mountain path is perilously steep, with no ground below. Once, Li Qinsu of Hedong visited this place. Chen's bones were large and different from those of modern people, hard, heavy, smooth, and lustrous like blue jade. The power of the Dao is evident here. His disciple's remains are also nearby, and when compared to Chen, the difference between the divine and the mortal is clear!

    Paintings by Mǎ Guāngchén
    Mǎ Guāngchén, the son of Mǎ Zhīshēn, was around ten years old when he painted landscapes with a sense of distance. He died shortly after becoming a young adult. Wáng Zǐduān, the Grand Secretary, inscribed on his paintings: "In the fine tomb, paintings and drawings lie idle. Tears in his final years, his last brush strokes across many mountains." People say that he was known for his painting at a young age and lamented by famous scholars, a rare occurrence in ancient times.

    44

    马啮定襄簿
    　　泰和中，一国姓人为定襄簿。一日，河西程氏马逸，直上厅啮主簿倒。旁立数十人，号叫捶楚，不能救。不半时顷，啮簿死。伤折处所不忍视。马走出城，罗得之。三日葬簿，缚马投火中。人谓：此马不为物所凭，则他世报怨也。
    　　鬼市
    　　裴翰林择之，阳武人。六七岁时，以大父马上抱往县东北庄。至外壕，见门南北有市集，人物皆二尺许，男女老幼，吏卒僧道，穰穰往来，市人买卖，负担、驴驼、车载，无所不有。以告其大父，大父以为妄，不之信也。盖三、四至其处，亦皆见之。此与《吕氏碣石录》记武平周鼎，童时村居，一日，县人市集，鼎骑长耳，从父入市。时地色微辨，见道旁两列皆佛像，闭目不敢视，开目又不见。两事大相类。但佛像之多，何也？

    Explanation

    44

    A Horse Biting the Official of Dingxiang
    During the Tahe period, a man surnamed Guo served as an official in Dingxiang. One day, a horse belonging to the Cheng family from the western region broke loose and charged directly into the hall, biting the official and causing him to fall. Dozens of people stood by, shouting and beating the horse, but they could not stop it. Within a short while, the horse bit the official to death. The injuries were so severe that they could not be looked at. The horse then ran out of the city and was eventually caught. Three days later, the official was buried, and the horse was tied and thrown into a fire. People said: This horse is not possessed by any spirit; it must be seeking revenge from another life.

    Ghost Market
    Pei Zhe, a翰林 from Yangwu, was six or seven years old when he was carried on his grandfather's horse to a place in the northeast of the county. Upon reaching the outer moat, he saw a market on both sides of the gate, with people and objects all about two feet tall. Men, women, the elderly, children, officials, soldiers, monks, and Taoists were bustling about. Merchants were buying and selling, with people carrying loads, riding donkeys and camels, and using carts—there was nothing they did not have. He told his grandfather about this, but his grandfather thought it was nonsense and did not believe him. However, on several occasions, he also saw the same thing. This is similar to what is recorded in Lü Shi's Jie Shi Lu about Zhou Ding from Wuping, who lived in a village as a child. One day, when the county people were at the market, Ding rode a long-eared donkey and went with his father to the market. At that time, the ground was slightly visible, and he saw rows of Buddha statues on both sides of the road. He closed his eyes in fear and dared not look, but when he opened his eyes again, they were gone. The two stories are very similar, but why were there so many Buddha statues?

    45

    原武阎氏犬
    　　原武附城堤下阎老家，其翁母遭辛卯冬兵乱死。其家墙下丁壮被虏，不及埋掩。此时僵尸满野，例为狐犬所食，不辨谁某。阎氏犬亦食人，但守护翁母，日与众犬斗，他犬无敢近者。前后月余。阎氏子侄有逃归者，竟得全骸而瘗。真孝犬也！
    　　历年之谶
    　　古人上寿皆以千万岁寿为言，国初种人纯质，每举觞惟祝百二十岁而已。盖武元以政和五年、辽天庆五年乙未为收国元年，至哀宗天兴三年蔡州陷，适两甲子周矣！历年之谶遂应。

    Explanation

    45

    The Dog of the Yan Family in Yuanwu

    In the suburbs of Yuanwu, there was a family of the Yan clan living near the city wall. The old man and his mother died during the winter of the year of Xinmao due to military chaos. The young men under the wall were captured and not given time to bury or cover up their bodies. At that time, the fields were filled with corpses, which were usually eaten by foxes and dogs, and it was impossible to distinguish who they belonged to. The Yan family's dog also ate people, but it protected the old man and his mother, fighting daily with other dogs, none of which dared to approach. This continued for over a month. Some of the Yan family's relatives escaped and returned, eventually managing to find and bury the remains. Truly, it was a filial dog!

    Prophecy of the Years

    Ancient people often spoke of a lifespan of tens of thousands of years. At the beginning of the state, the people were pure and simple, and each time they raised their cups, they only wished for a lifespan of one hundred and twenty years. The founder, Wumu, used the fifth year of Zhenghe and the fifth year of Tianqing in the year of Yiwei as the first year of the state. Until the third year of Tianxing in the reign of the Emperor Ai, when Cizhou fell, it was exactly two cycles of sixty years! The prophecy of the years was thus fulfilled.

    46

    巽齐之谶
    　　天会八年，册刘豫为大齐皇帝，都大名。诸门旧有巽齐、安流、顺豫之号，以门名色瑞，因取三市门名阜昌者建元。虽出于傅会，亦有数焉。
    　　桃杯
    　　巩下韩道人，本出衣冠家，曾以荫补官。中年遇异人，有所得，即弃官学道。予曾见之秦州之陇城。说泰和初，秋雨后行山间，忽见一大叶随流而下，韩初不以为意，俄数叶间一桃大如杯盌，为石所碍而止。韩取得之。桃红而香，非凡目所常见，知为希遇。望三峰再拜食之。尽，怀枝叶归。就洞穴高绝处，钻桃核破，取仁吞之，甘如酥蜜。因以核为两酒杯，各受一勺余。韩从此或食或辟谷。时年已六十，状貌只如四十许人。一日从予乞酒，以此杯酌。核得酒，红润如新。约予赋《桃杯诗》，因循未暇。北渡后，长春尹师亦有一桃杯，云是宣、政内府物云。

    Explanation

    46

    The Omen of the Xun Gate

    In the eighth year of Tianhe, Liu Yu was enthroned as the Emperor of Great Qi, with Daming as his capital. The gates had old names such as Xun Gate, Anliu Gate, and Shunyu Gate, which were considered auspicious. Thus, he took the name of the gate called Fuchang as his era name. Although it was somewhat contrived, there was also a certain rationale behind it.

    The Peach Cup

    The Taoist Master Han from Gongxia, originally from a family of officials, once appointed to an official position through hereditary privilege. In his middle age, he met a strange person and gained something, which led him to resign and study the Dao. I once saw him in Longcheng, Qin Prefecture. He said during the early years of Taihe, after the autumn rain, he walked through the mountains and suddenly saw a large leaf floating downstream. Han initially did not pay much attention to it. Soon, among several leaves, a peach as large as a cup and plate appeared, but it stopped due to an obstruction by a stone. Han picked it up. The peach was red and fragrant, not something commonly seen by ordinary eyes. He knew it was a rare occurrence. He bowed twice to the Three Peaks and ate it. After finishing, he carried the branches and leaves back. He went to a high and secluded cave, drilled through the peach pit, took out the kernel, and swallowed it. It was as sweet as cream and honey. He then made two wine cups from the pit, each capable of holding more than a ladle. From then on, Han either ate or practiced fasting. At the time, he was already sixty years old, but his appearance was like that of a forty-year-old man. One day, he asked me for wine and used these cups to pour wine. The pit, when filled with wine, turned red and fresh. He asked me to compose a poem titled "The Peach Cup," but I had not yet had the time to do so. After crossing north, the Master Yin of Changchun also had a peach cup, which he said was from the inner palace during the Xuan and Zheng reigns.

    47

    溺死鬼
    　　泽州有针工。一日人定后，方阅针次，闻人沿濠上来，喜笑曰：“明日得替矣！”人问替者为谁？曰：“一走卒自真定肩伞插书夹，来濠中浴，我得替矣。”针工出门望，无所见，知其为鬼。明日立门首待之。早食后，一疾卒留伞与书夹针工家，云欲往濠中浴。针工问之，则从真定来。因为卒言：城中有浴室，请以揩背钱相助。卒问其故，工具以昨所闻告，辞谢再三而去。其夕二更后，有掷瓦砾于门大骂曰：“我辛苦得替，却为此贼坏却，我誓拽汝水中！”明旦，见瓦砾堆。数夕不罢。此人迁居避之。秘水焦符村说
    　　棣州学鬼妇
    　　王右司仲泽，少日住棣州学。厨人告言：“一妇人鬼，每夜来搅扰，不得睡。”泽言：“今夕若复来，汝捽其衣大叫，我辈往视之。”其夜果来，其人把其臂不放，因大叫。诸生持镫往视之，乃一古棺板。焚之，而怪遂绝。仲泽说

    Explanation

    47

    The Drowned Ghost

    In Ze Prefecture, there was a needleworker. One day, after the evening meal, he was arranging his needles when he heard someone coming up the moat. He laughed and said, "Tomorrow I will get a replacement!" Someone asked who the replacement would be. He replied, "A messenger from Zhen Ding carrying an umbrella and a book folder is coming to bathe in the moat. I will get a replacement." The needleworker went out to look but saw nothing, realizing it was a ghost. The next day, he stood at the door waiting for him. After breakfast, a messenger left his umbrella and book folder at the needleworker's house, saying he wanted to go bathe in the moat. The needleworker asked where he was from, and he replied that he was from Zhen Ding. The needleworker then told the messenger that there was a bathhouse in the city and offered to pay for a back-scrubbing. The messenger asked why, and the needleworker told him what he had heard the previous day. The messenger refused and left after several thanks. That night, after the second watch, someone threw stones and tiles at the door, cursing, "I worked hard to get this replacement, but this thief ruined it for me. I swear I will drag you into the water!" The next morning, the needleworker found a pile of stones and tiles. This continued for several nights. The person moved to another house to avoid the ghost. This story is told in the village of Jiaofu near Secret Water.

    The Ghost Woman of the School in Di Prefecture

    Wang Zhongze, the Right Censor, lived in a school in Di Prefecture when he was young. The cook reported, "There is a ghost woman who comes every night to disturb us, and we cannot sleep." Wang said, "If she comes again tonight, grab her clothes and shout, and we will go see what is happening." That night, she indeed came. The person grabbed her arm and shouted. The students took a lantern and went to see, and they found an ancient coffin board. They burned it, and the ghost disappeared. This story is told by Wang Zhongze.

    48

    汤盘周鼎
    　　秀岩安常字顺之，常从党承旨学大篆，多识古文奇字。泰和末，尝见内府所藏汤盘，作白玉方斗，近四小寸，底铭九字，即：“德日新、又日新、日日新”者也。章宗有旨令辨之。又一方鼎，耳二，足四，饕餮象在雷文中。铭云：“鲁公作文王尊彝”。铜既古，莹如碧玉，无复铜性矣。
    　　莲十三花
    　　同年康良辅说，磁州观台刘轨家，承安中，池莲一茎开十三花。是岁，轨登科。终于京兆按察判官。
    　　瑞禾
    　　凤翔虢县太子庄，庚子岁，郝氏谷田八十亩，每茎一叶一小穗，至十二数，并大穗为十三。试割一丛治之，得谷十升。明年，郝使统军万人，佩金虎符。偏将李慥曾见古有一茎九穗，盖不如是之多也。

    Explanation

    48

    汤盘周鼎
    An Chang, courtesy name Shunzhi, studied seal script under Party Chengzhi and was well-versed in ancient characters. At the end of the Taihe period, he once saw a white jade square vessel in the imperial treasury, nearly four small inches in size, with a base inscription of nine characters: "Virtue is renewed day by day, and day after day it is renewed." Emperor Zhangzong ordered him to authenticate it. There was also a square bronze vessel with two ears and four feet, adorned with a饕餮 pattern on the thunder motif. The inscription read: "Duke Lu made a ritual bronze vessel for King Wen." The bronze was ancient and polished to a jade-like luster, no longer showing its metallic nature.

    莲十三花
    Kang Liangfu recounted that in Guantai, Cizhou, during the Cheng'an period, a lotus flower with thirteen petals bloomed in a pond. That year, Liu Gui passed the imperial examination. He eventually became the magistrate of Jingzhao, the inspector of judicial affairs.

    瑞禾
    In Taizi Village, Guo County, Fengxiang, in the Gengzi year, Hao Shi's eighty-acre field produced a plant where each leaf had a small ear, and there were twelve more, making a total of thirteen. When one stalk was harvested and processed, it yielded ten liters of grain. The next year, Hao Shi was appointed to lead ten thousand troops and wore the golden tiger talisman. A subordinate general, Li Zao, had once seen an ancient plant with nine ears on one stem, but it was not as numerous as this.

    49

    黄真人
    　　修武张字君冕，其父仲和，少日为府史，好祈仙。一日，黄翻绰降，因留事之，谓之黄真人。悬笔画像前，每事祷之。君冕崇庆二年赴帘试。仲和问云：“儿子入试，御题得闻乎？”批曰：“天机不容泄！”及试期过，问之，即批云：“臣作股肱弼予违赋，成绩纪太常诗。”又问：“儿登第否？”批曰：“黄裳头、绿衣尾。”张不解，请解之，又批曰：“天机不容泄！”及四月，当唱名，张又问：“榜旦夕至，幸先告之！”即批云：“绿衣、六衣也，非君冕名乎？”及榜至，黄吉甫真第一人，而君冕名最下。此类甚多。亦有俳谐诗，可笑。
    　　摩利天咒
    　　忻州刘军判，贞祐初，闻朔方人马动，家诵摩利天咒。及州陷，二十五口俱免兵祸。独一奴不信，迫围城始诵之，被虏四五日亦逃归。南渡后，居永宁，即施此咒。文士薛曼卿记其事。

    Explanation

    49

    黄真人

    In the region of Xiuwu, there was a man named Zhang Zhi, whose courtesy name was Junmian. His father, Zhonghe, served as a low-ranking official in his youth and was fond of praying for immortality. One day, Huang Fanchuo descended and stayed with him, and he was called Huang Zhenren. They hung a painting of Huang Zhenren in front of their home and prayed for everything. In the second year of Chongqing, Junmian took the imperial examination. Zhonghe asked, "Son, have you heard the emperor's question for the exam?" Junmian replied, "The heavenly mechanism cannot be revealed!" After the exam, when Zhonghe asked again, Junmian wrote, "I composed a poem about the loyal ministers supporting the emperor and the virtuous deeds recorded in the Taichang (a historical text)." Zhonghe then asked, "Did you pass the exam?" Junmian replied, "Yellow robe on top, green robe on bottom." Zhonghe did not understand and asked for an explanation, to which Junmian wrote, "The heavenly mechanism cannot be revealed!" By April, when the results were to be announced, Zhonghe asked, "The list will soon be released, please tell me in advance!" Junmian wrote, "Green robe, six robes, is it not your name, Junmian?" When the list was finally released, Huang Jifu was indeed the first place winner, while Junmian's name was at the very bottom. There were many such instances. There were also humorous poems that were quite amusing.

    摩利天咒

    In Xinzhou, there was a judge named Liu Junpan. In the early years of Zhenyou, he heard that there was military activity in the northern regions. He began reciting the Molixian Tianzuo (a specific incantation) at home. When the city was captured, all twenty-five members of his family were spared from the war. Only one servant did not believe in the incantation and started reciting it only when the city was under siege. He was captured for several days but managed to escape back. After the Southern Migration, he settled in Yongning and continued to recite the incantation. The literatus Xue Manqing recorded this event.

    50

    王叟阴德
    　　穰县宋庄王叟，人目为王评事。身年八十一，妇八十，四子，有孙二十余人，曾孙亦娶妇。自叟至其曾，凡三十六房，夫妇皆结发，推户为县中第一。第四子荣，以军功官宣武军鲁山尉；长孙中武举，某州巡检。宋庄四区宅前大槐，数百年物，老干已枯，而五枝内向，各成大树，荫数十步。予在镇平日，尝过其家，见其康健如六十许。人谓必有阴德致然，问之不答。旁一叟云：“王评事年虽高，乃以诊治为生。病家来请，上马去，不以僮仆自随；为人处方，一药不备，不以和剂；贫家调患，夏月日二、三往，不倦，病既平，不责一钱。此非阴德耶？”叟乃肯自言：“今商贩家自临洮山外，以长耳负甘草来，尘垢粪秽，何所不有？卸之药肆中，随即剉以与人。某每用此草，必以水洗潠，暴晾如法，然后和药。他品悉然。非敢自为阴德，但心之所安，不能不尔也。”予酌酒与之曰：“此公阴德大矣！”

    Explanation

    50

    Wang Sǒu's Unseen Virtue

    In Songzhuang, a village in Rang County, there lived an elderly man named Wang Sǒu, who was known as Wang Pingshi. He was eighty-one years old, his wife was eighty, they had four sons, and more than twenty grandchildren, including great-grandchildren who had already married. From Wang Sǒu down to his great-grandchildren, there were thirty-six households, all of whom had been married for a long time, and they were recommended as the first household in the county. His fourth son, Rong, became a military officer in the Lushan region of the Xuanwu Army due to his military achievements; his eldest grandson passed the military examination and became a patrol officer in a certain state. In front of the four districts of Songzhuang, there stood a large locust tree that was several hundred years old, with a trunk that had withered, but five branches growing inward, each forming a large tree, providing shade for dozens of steps. When I was stationed in Zhenping, I once visited his home and found him to be as healthy as someone in their sixties. People said that such health must be due to his unseen virtue, but when I asked him, he did not respond. An elderly man beside me said, "Although Wang Pingshi is old, he makes a living by treating illnesses. When a sick family invites him, he goes on horseback without bringing servants; when prescribing medicine, if one ingredient is missing, he does not mix the medicine himself; he treats the sick in poor families, visiting two or three times a day in the summer without tiring, and after the illness is cured, he does not ask for a single coin. Is this not unseen virtue?" Wang Sǒu then agreed to speak for himself, saying, "Nowadays, merchants from areas outside Lintao Mountain come with camels or donkeys carrying ginseng, which can be covered in dust and filth. After unloading them at the medicine shop, they immediately cut and give them to others. Whenever I use this herb, I must wash it with water, dry it according to the proper method, and then prepare the medicine. The same is true for other herbs. I do not dare to claim that I do good deeds for their own sake, but I cannot help but do so because it is what my heart finds at peace with." I offered him wine and said, "This gentleman's unseen virtue is great indeed!"

    冯妇诗
    　　武安县新安农冯氏病后，忽道一诗云：“城南池馆夹蒲津，野色林光物色真。满目烟霞蓬岛远，一溪花木武陵春。”泰和末病卒。胡国瑞说
    　　石中龟
    　　金门羽客李炼师，和顺人，尝为章庙所诏，提点天长观。平生灵异，如“金盂出水”之类甚多，至八十一事，图于邢州神霄宫壁间。门人王守中，又欲刻碑以传。召匠者攻石。石中得一龟，日在几案闲驯狎。如是百日。风过，失所在。武安王安卿说。

    Translation:

    The Poem of Feng Fu

    After falling ill, Feng, a farmer from Xian'an in Wuan County, suddenly recited a poem: "South of the city, pavilions and halls line the banks of the Pu River; the wild colors and forest light are truly authentic. My eyes are filled with mist and clouds, far from the fairyland; a stream flows with flowers and trees, like the spring of Wu Ling." He died of illness at the end of the Taihe era. This was said by Hu Guorui.

    The Turtle in the Stone

    Li Lianshi, a Taoist priest from Heshun and a resident of the Jinnmen Gate, was once summoned by the Zhaofang Temple to oversee the Tianshang Temple. Throughout his life, he performed many miraculous feats, such as the "Golden Bowl Emerging from Water," among eighty-one such events. These were painted on the walls of the Shenzhao Palace in Xingzhou. His disciple Wang Shouzhong wished to engrave them on a stele for posterity. When a craftsman began to carve the stone, a turtle was found inside. The turtle spent days at the desk, becoming tame and familiar. For a hundred days, it remained there. Then, as the wind passed, it disappeared. This was said by Wang Anqing from Wuan County.

    52

    石中
    　　长葛禹冀之，见华山隐者薛自然说，泰和中，华山石工破一石，石中一跳出，寻入水中。
    　　高监偿债
    　　遂平斗城镇高监，初到斗城，就富民高氏求相绍继。高氏农民，淳质，堕其术中。所借钱麦积数百缗，后百方诋欺，一钱不偿。未几高监死，生一赤犊，腹下白毛成字云：“还债人高都监。”时武州人吴成可罢鄜畤丞，闲居此镇，作《牛报文》。
    　　范元质决牛讼
    　　范元质令平舆。函头村彭李家，兄弟皆豪于财。彭李三水牯生一犊，数日死，弃水中。邻张氏水牯亦生一犊。李三为牧儿所诱，窃张犊去，令其家水牯乳之。张家挞之，遂告张曰：“李家犊死，投水中；今所乳，君家犊也！君告官，我往证之。”张愬之官。元质曰：“此不难。”命汲新水两盆，刺两牛耳尖，血沥水中，二血殊不相入。又捉犊子亦刺之，犊血沥水上，随与张牛血相入而凝。即以犊归张氏。县称神明。元质名天保，磁州人。进士赵公祥亲见

    Explanation

    52

    A Baby from a Stone
    During the Tahe period, Longge Yu Jiqi heard from Xue Ziran, a hermit on Mount Hua, that a stone mason broke open a stone on Mount Hua, and a baby emerged from the stone, quickly diving into the water.

    Gao the Supervisor Pays His Debt
    Gao, the supervisor of Suiping Douzhen Town, arrived in Douzhen and approached the wealthy Gao family to request a succession. The Gao family were simple and honest farmers, and they fell into Gao's scheme. He borrowed hundreds of strings of cash worth of wheat, and later used various deceitful tactics to avoid paying a single coin. Soon after, Gao the supervisor died, and a red calf was born. The white hair on the calf's belly formed words that read, "Debtor Gao the Supervisor." At that time, Wu Chengke, a former official from Wuzhou who had been demoted to the position of Fu Zhi Cheng, was living in this town and wrote a document titled "The Cattle's Retribution."

    Fan Yuanzhi Resolves a Cattle Dispute
    Fan Yuanzhi, the magistrate of Pingyu, heard about a dispute involving cows in the village of Hantou. The Peng Li family, who were both wealthy, had a water buffalo named Peng Li San that gave birth to a calf, which died after a few days and was thrown into the water. A neighboring Zhang family's water buffalo also gave birth to a calf. Peng Li San, lured by a herder boy, stole the Zhang family's calf and had his own water buffalo nurse it. The Zhang family beat the herder boy, and he accused the Zhang family, saying, "Peng Li San's calf died and was thrown into the water; the calf being nursed now is yours! You should report this to the authorities, and I will testify against you." The Zhang family reported the matter to the authorities. Fan Yuanzhi said, "This is not difficult." He ordered two new pots of water to be fetched and pricked the tips of the ears of the two water buffaloes, allowing their blood to drip into the water. The two streams of blood did not mix. He then pricked the calf and let its blood drip into the water, and it mixed with the Zhang family's buffalo's blood and coagulated. Immediately, he returned the calf to the Zhang family. The county praised him as a god-like judge. Fan Yuanzhi's name was Tianbao, and he was from Cizhou. The Jinshi Zhao Gongxiang personally witnessed this event.

    53

    贾叟刻木
    　　平阳贾叟，无目而能刻神像，人以待诏目之。交城县中寺一佛，是其所刻，仪相端严。僧说：贾初立木胎，先摸索之。意有所会，运斤如风。予因记赵州没眼僧，能噀墨作画，上布五彩亦噀之。毛提举家一虎，蹲大树下，旁卧一青彪，虎目烁烁如金，望之毛发森立。虽赵邈龊不是过。佛氏所谓六根互用者，殆从是而进耶？
    　　阎大凭妇语
    　　穰县孙庄农民阎大，正大中，与同里刘进往商洛买牛，而阎病死。刘以书报其家。阎母与妇望祭于所居之前，有回风吹纸灰往西南庄。此庄是阎小妇所居，相去五六里。少之，有人来报，阎大凭妇语，欲与母妻相见。母妻奔往，相持而哭，问：“汝何死？”曰：“我死天命，但为刘进所欺，先此相告。某牛价几何，用绢若干；某牛价几何，用银若干；彼乘我死无证，欲相欺昧耳！”布金价直，皆令以笔记之。

    Explanation

    53

    Carving Wood by the Old Man Jia

    In Pingyang, there was an old man named Jia who, despite being blind, could carve divine images. People referred to him as "appointed to serve the imperial court." In the temple of Jiaocheng County, there was a Buddha statue carved by him, which was graceful and dignified. The monk said that Jia first felt and probed the wooden frame, then, having a sudden insight, he swung his axe like the wind. I recall the blind monk of Zhaozhou, who could spit ink to paint and sprinkle colors on top, also spitting them. At the home of a magistrate named Mao, there was a tiger crouching under a large tree, with a green panther lying beside it. The tiger's eyes shone like gold, and looking at it made one's hair stand on end. Even Zhaozhou's monk was not beyond this. The Buddhist concept of the six sense organs functioning interchangeably, perhaps this is how they progress.

    The Mediumistic Communication of Yan Da

    In Rang County, there was a farmer named Yan Da. During the reign of Emperor Chengzong, he went with his fellow villager Liu Jin to Shangluo to buy cattle, but Yan died of illness. Liu Jin wrote a letter to Yan's family. Yan's mother and wife performed worship and offerings in front of their home, and a gust of wind blew the ashes of the paper towards the southwest village. This village was where Yan's young wife lived, about five or six li away. Soon after, someone came to report that Yan Da spoke through his wife, wanting to meet his mother and wife. His mother and wife rushed to the village, embraced him, and cried, asking, "Why did you die?" He replied, "I died by fate, but I was deceived by Liu Jin. I told you this beforehand. What was the price of a certain cow, using silk; what was the price of another cow, using silver; he took advantage of my death without evidence, wanting to deceive and defraud me!" The prices of gold and silver were all recorded in writing.

    54

    又云：“此人情理不可耐，我已死，渠有布绢，乃以行缠蔽我面。”傍一屠者云：“汝欠我肉钱若干，汝家以汝死，遂不见还，今令我取还。”阎俯首久之，仰视屠云：“我已死，更理会甚？”观者大笑。他日，刘进及家。人说：向云阎大有灵，先以价直告其家矣！进见其母，一钱不敢欺焉。致远与阎一村落，为言如此。此与正大中黥卒石贵事同。贵死后凭一男子，就舞阳县吏征债，诉于司农卿张公，公异其事，命部掾王仲宽为理，贵有文券可凭，立命还之。

    54

    A ghost complained, "This person's emotions and reason cannot be endured. I am already dead, and he has cloth, which he used to cover my face with a bandage." A butcher standing nearby said, "You owe me a certain amount of money for meat. Your family, because you are dead, no longer repays me. Now I am making them repay me." Yan bowed his head for a long time, then looked up at the butcher and said, "I am already dead, so what more do I care about?" The onlookers laughed. Later, Liu Jin returned home. People told him, "Earlier, it was said that Yan was very powerful, and he first informed his family about the debt!" When Liu Jin saw his mother, he did not dare to cheat by even a single coin. Zhiyuan and Yan were from the same village, and he explained the matter to him. This is the same as the case of the tattooed soldier Shi Gui during the Zhengda period. After Shi Gui's death, a man appeared to collect the debt from the officials of Wuyang County, and the matter was reported to the Minister of Agriculture, Zhang Gong. The minister found the matter unusual and ordered his subordinate, Wang Zhongkuan, to handle it. Shi Gui had written evidence to prove the debt, and it was immediately ordered to be repaid.

    55

    延寿丹
    　　神仙辟谷延寿丹，一丸，终身不饥。光明朱砂一两，飞过用之；定粉一两，烧之黄色者；白茯苓如雪者一两，或加半两；黄丹、轻红者一两，飞过；秤乳香七钱半；水银三钱；大金箔三十片；白沙蜜一两；净蜡二两。右各择精细者。先将定粉入乳钵研开，次下水银再研，直侯无水银星子为度。次下黄丹、朱砂、金箔，再研，次下茯苓、乳香等细末同研匀。将药入垍碗，坐热汤上，勿令汤冷。另将蜜蜡开鋊，入药在内，木匙搅匀。众手丸。每一两作十二丸子，勿令有剂缝。或朱砂或水银为衣，不为衣亦可。如欲以水银为衣，取水银三、二粒，手心内用津唾擦青色，取药三、五丸搓之。合时忌鸡犬、妇人。药成，入垍器内贮之。如欲住食，先用油三两、蜡一两、白面一斤，入蜜一两，和烧饼或煎饼。如无，食不托面或糯米粥亦可。须极饱，然后服药。以乳香汤下一丸。

    Explanation

    55

    Immortal Elixir for Longevity and Food Abstinence
    A single pill of the Immortal Elixir for Longevity and Food Abstinence allows one to abstain from food for life. One catty of bright cinnabar, processed and purified; one catty of alum, burned until it turns yellow; one catty of white茯苓 as white as snow, or optionally half a catty more; one catty of yellow oxide of lead, light red in color, processed and purified; seven and a half taels of frankincense, weighed by scale; three taels of mercury; thirty sheets of large gold leaf; one catty of white honey; two catties of purified wax. Each ingredient should be carefully selected. First, grind the alum in a mortar until it is fine, then add the mercury and grind further until no mercury specks remain. Next, add the yellow oxide of lead, cinnabar, and gold leaf, and grind again. Then, add the powdered茯苓 and frankincense, and grind until all are thoroughly mixed. Place the mixture in a jade bowl and set it over a warm pot, ensuring the water does not cool. Separately, melt the honey and wax in a pan, mix them together, and combine with the mixture using a wooden spoon. Form the pills by hand, with each catty making twelve pills, ensuring there are no seams. Optionally, coat the pills with either cinnabar or mercury, or leave them uncoated. If coating with mercury, take three or two grains of mercury, rub them with saliva in your palm to make a paste, and mix with three or five pills to coat them. During preparation, avoid contact with chickens, dogs, and women. Once the elixir is prepared, store it in a jade container. If one wishes to abstain from food, first prepare a meal of three catties of oil, one catty of wax, one catty of white flour, and one catty of honey, making a pancake or flatbread. If unavailable, plain rice or porridge can be eaten instead. One must eat until full, then take the elixir. Take one pill with a decoction of frankincense.

    56

    又一时辰许，再将白面炒熟，蜜蜡为丸，如桐子大，温白汤或乳香汤下百丸，名曰“后药”。先已饱食，又服后药，故二三日不困。虽困亦无伤。服药后当万缘不染。夫心动则气散，语多则气伤，故辟谷者以宁心养气为本，事来则应，事过勿留于心，时时向日咽气，以为补助。茶汤任意，勿食有滓之物，忌怒，忌大劳。十日后，饥肉虽瘦，而筋骨轻健，神观开朗。如欲开食，须二七日以后，候药在丹田，可开食。不及二七日而食，则药随脏腑而下矣！开食之后，如更欲住食，不必服药，止以乳香汤匀之。凶年饥岁，至父子夫妇相啖，捣为泥丸，作弹子大，黄丹为衣，纸带子盛此药一丸，缝合著脐中，上用裹肚系定。每遇箭镞未出，先如上系定，顷用象牙末擦疮口。若中箭已久，须用锋刃或针，少少取破，搽象牙末，则箭镞自出。如鱼骨鲠喉，以至针、钱、麦芒，不限久近，皆验。

    Explanation

    56

    About an hour later, cook white flour until done, make it into pills with honey wax, as large as the seed of the paulownia tree. Take one hundred pills at a time with warm white soup or frankincense soup. This is named "Post-medicine." Having already eaten a full meal, and then taking the post-medicine, therefore, for two or three days, there is no fatigue. Even if tired, it is not harmful. After taking the medicine, one should avoid all distractions. When the heart moves, the qi disperses; speaking too much injures the qi. Therefore, those who practice辟谷 (fasting) should focus on calming the heart and nurturing the qi. Respond to events as they come, but do not dwell on them afterward. Frequently face the sun and swallow qi as a supplement. Tea and soup can be consumed at will; do not eat things with residue. Avoid anger and excessive labor. After ten days, the hunger may cause the flesh to become lean, but the muscles and bones become light and strong, and the spirit becomes clear and bright. If you wish to resume eating, you must wait until fourteen days later, until the medicine has settled in the dantian. Then you can resume eating. If you eat before fourteen days, the medicine will descend with the organs! After resuming eating, if you wish to stop eating again, you do not need to take the medicine; just use frankincense soup to balance it. In times of famine, fathers, sons, and spouses may resort to cannibalism. Crush the medicine into small clay balls, as large as a ball, coat them with yellow ochre, wrap one pill in a paper strip, sew it onto the navel, and use a cloth belt to secure it. Whenever an arrowhead has not been removed, first follow the above method to secure it, then use ivory powder to rub the wound. If the arrow has been in for a long time, use a sharp blade or needle to gently break the skin, apply ivory powder, and the arrowhead will come out. If a fish bone is stuck in the throat, or a needle, coin, or grain awn, regardless of how long it has been there, all of these methods are effective.

    57

    救熏死
    　　辛未冬，德兴西南磨石窑，居民避兵其中。兵人来攻，窑中五百人，悉为烟火熏死。内一李帅者，迷闷中摸索得一冻芦菔，嚼之，汁才咽而苏。因与其兄，兄亦活。五百人者因此皆得命。芦菔，细物，活人之功乃如此！中流失船，一壶千金，真不虚语！河中人赵才卿又言：“炭烟熏人，往往致死。临卧削芦菔一片著火中，即烟气不能毒人。如无芦菔时，豫暴干为末，备急用，亦可。”

    Explanation

    57

    Rescuing from Smoke Death

    In the winter of the year Xinhui, during the reign of Emperor Ling, a cave in the southwest of Dexing was inhabited by residents who had sought refuge there to escape the soldiers. The soldiers attacked, and all five hundred people inside the cave were killed by smoke. Among them was a leader named Li, who, in a state of confusion, managed to find a frozen turnip. He chewed it, and as soon as he swallowed the juice, he revived. He then shared it with his brother, who also survived. As a result, all five hundred people were saved. The turnip, a small and seemingly insignificant object, had the power to save lives! A ship lost in midstream is worth a thousand gold pieces—this is no empty saying! Zhao Caiqing from the River region added, "Carbon smoke can often be fatal. Before going to bed, cut a piece of turnip and place it in the fire; the smoke will not be harmful. If you don't have turnips, dry and grind them in advance for emergency use, and they will also be effective."

    58

    神人方
    　　阿魏散。治骨蒸、传尸劳、寒热、困羸、喘嗽方：阿魏三钱；斫青蒿一握，细切；东北桃枝一握，细剉；甘草如病人中指许大，男左女右；童子小便二升半。先以小便隔夜浸药，明旦煎取一大升，空心温服，分为三服以进。次服调槟榔末三钱。如人行十里，更一服。丈夫病，妇人煎药；妇人病，丈夫煎药。合时忌孝服、孕妇、病人及腥秽物、鸡犬见。服药后忌油腻、湿面、冷硬物。服至一二剂，即吐出虫或泄泻，更不须服余药。若未吐利，即当尽服。病在上即吐，在下即利，皆出虫如马尾、人发之类，即当差。天下治劳，直须累月或经岁，唯此方得于神授，随手取效。

    Explanation

    58

    Divine Formula:
    Astragalus Powder. Treats bone steaming, transmitted corpse labor, alternating chills and fever, exhaustion, and coughing: three money of Asafoetida; chop a handful of Artemisia and finely cut it; a handful of northeastern Peach branches and finely chop them; Licorice the size of the patient's middle finger, left for men and right for women; two and a half liters of a child's urine. First soak the medicine overnight with the urine, the next morning boil and extract one liter, take it warm on an empty stomach, divided into three doses. The next dose should be mixed with three money of Areca nut powder. After walking ten li, take another dose. If a man is ill, a woman should prepare the medicine; if a woman is ill, a man should prepare the medicine. During preparation, avoid those in mourning, pregnant women, the sick, and unclean things or animals. After taking the medicine, avoid greasy, damp, and cold foods. After taking one or two doses, the patient may vomit worms or experience diarrhea, and no further medication is needed. If there is no vomiting or diarrhea, the patient should take the full dose. If the disease is above, it will cause vomiting; if below, it will cause diarrhea. The worms will look like horse tails or human hair, and the patient will then recover. Treating such diseases typically takes months or years, but only this formula was divinely granted and works instantly.

    59

    陵川进士刘俞字彬叔，任都运司幕官日，得于阎郎陟，云是古崔家方。阎先患此疾，垂死，得方而愈。刘以治宁州一官妓，利寸白虫三四升，状如葱根，随即平复。服药后遂去诸疾，五藏虚羸，魂魄不安，即以白茯苓汤补之：白茯苓一钱；茯神一钱；人参三钱；远志三钱，去心；龙骨二钱；防风二钱；甘草三钱；麦门冬去心四钱，犀角五钱，错为末，生干地黄四钱；肥大枣七枚；水二大升，煎作八分。分三服，温下。如人行五里许，更进一服。仍避风寒。若觉未安，隔日更作一剂。已上两药，须连服之。好问案：此方本出普济加减方，其语简略，又不著所从来，而世人不甚敬信，故备论之。

    Explanation

    59

    Liu Yu, a scholar from Lingchuan and a graduate of the imperial examinations with the courtesy name Binshu, obtained the prescription from Yan Lang Zhi, who said it was an ancient prescription from the Cui family. Yan first suffered from this disease, nearly dying, but was cured by the prescription. Liu used it to treat an official courtesan from Ningzhou, benefiting from three to four sheng of inch-long white worms shaped like scallion roots, and she immediately recovered. After taking the medicine, all diseases were eliminated, and the five zang organs were weak and the spirit was unsettled. Immediately, White Poria Decoction was used to tonify it: one qian of white Poria; one qian of Poria cocos; three qian of ginseng; three qian of Polygala, with the heart removed; two qian of dragon bone; two qian of windproof; three qian of licorice; four qian of Ophiopogon, with the heart removed; five qian of rhinoceros horn, ground into powder. Fresh dried rehmannia four qian; seven large jujubes; two large sheng of water, decocted to make eight fen. Divided into three doses, taken warm. After walking about five li, take another dose. Still avoid wind and cold. If not feeling well, prepare another dose the next day. The above two medicines must be taken continuously. According to Hao Wen's note, this formula originally comes from the Puji Jiajian Fang. The language is concise, and it does not specify the origin, so people do not take it very seriously, hence a detailed discussion is provided.

    60

    背疽方二
    　　治发背、脑疽，一切恶疮：初觉时，采独科苍耳一根，连叶带子细剉，不犯铁器。用砂锅熬水二大碗，熬及一半。疮在上，饭后徐徐服之，吐出，候吐定再服，以尽为度。疮在下，空心服。疮自破出脓，更不溃引。疮上别以膏药傅之。此方京兆张伯玉家榜示传人，后昆仲皆登第。人谓善报。治一切恶疮，服瓜蒌方：悬蒌一枚，去皮，用穰及子；生姜四两；甘草二两，横文者佳，细切生用；无灰酒一碗，煎及半，浓服之，煎时不犯铜铁。病在上，食后；在下，空心。

    Explanation

    60

    Two Remedies for Boils on the Back

    For treating boils on the back, brain abscesses, and all kinds of bad sores: At the initial stage, pick a single stalk of Xanthium, finely chop the leaves and seeds, and do not use iron tools. Use a clay pot to boil water for two large bowls, boiling until half done. If the sore is in the upper part of the body, take it slowly after a meal, and if it causes vomiting, wait until the vomiting stops before taking more, until all is consumed. If the sore is in the lower part of the body, take it on an empty stomach. The sore will break open by itself and discharge pus, and it will no longer spread. Apply a separate medicinal ointment to the sore. This remedy was displayed in the family of Zhang Boyu from the capital region to pass down to descendants, and all his later generations passed the imperial examinations. People say it was a reward for good deeds. For treating all kinds of bad sores, take the Trichosanthes remedy: Use one piece of Trichosanthes, remove the skin, and use the pulp and seeds; four ounces of ginger; two ounces of licorice, preferably with horizontal veins, finely chopped and used raw; one bowl of alcohol without ash, boil until half done, and take it concentrated. Do not use copper or iron during the boiling process. If the disease is in the upper part of the body, take it after a meal; if in the lower part, take it on an empty stomach.

    61

    见洪氏方、陈日华方。中州初得于张户部林卿。其方有加大黄、或木香、或乳香、没药者。大率以瓜蒌、生姜、甘草为主。病疮先疏利，次用瓜蒌药，日以乳香、菉豆粉温下三五钱，防毒气入腹。外以膏涂傅之，病者亦无虑矣。好问年二十一，侍先君官陇城。大安庚午春，先人疽发于鬓。好问愚幼，平居作举子计，于药医懵然无所知。庸医满前，任其施设，先君竟用是捐馆。其后还乡，得此方于家塾，以治他人，遂有百验之效。感念畴昔，惭恨入地。为人子不知医，其受祸乃如此！故并记之为戒。

    Explanation

    61

    Seeing the formulas of Hong Shi and Chen Rihua. Originally obtained in the Central Plains from Zhang Linqing, the Ministry of Revenue official. The formula includes the addition of rhubarb, or costus root, or frankincense, or myrrh. Generally, it uses Trichosanthes fruit, ginger, and licorice as the main ingredients. For skin diseases, first use laxatives, then apply the Trichosanthes formula. Daily, take three to five qian of frankincense and mung bean powder, to prevent toxins from entering the abdomen. Externally, apply ointment, and the patient need not worry. At the age of twenty-one, I served my father in Longcheng. In the spring of Da'an, the year Gengwu, my father developed a boil on his temple. I was young and foolish, usually occupied with the studies of a scholar, and knew nothing about medicine. Surrounded by quacks, I let them do as they pleased, and my father ultimately passed away due to this. After returning home, I obtained this formula from the family school and used it to treat others, achieving a hundredfold effectiveness. Reflecting on the past, I feel deep regret and shame. As a son, not knowing medicine led to such a disaster! Therefore, I record this as a warning.

    62

    内藏库龙
    　　辽祖神册五年三月，黑龙见拽刺山阳水。辽祖驰往。三日乃得至，而龙尚不去。辽祖射之而毙。龙一角，尾长而足短，身长五尺，舌长二寸有半。命藏之内库。贞祐南渡尚在，人见舌作蒲稭形也。
    　　都城夜怪
    　　从舅张伯达知、征飞卿翱，崇庆二年正月同赴省试。所挈仆夫戏以王兴目之者，宿迎銮坊。夜起便旋，足才出门，见对街一鬼，青面赤发，目光如炬，腕悬一剑而坐。旁一卒侍立，狞恶尤可怖。兴大叫而仆，三四时许乃苏。问之，言所见如此。

    Explanation

    62

    内藏库龙
    In the fifth month of the fifth year of the Shenchu era, a black dragon appeared at the Yang Water of Zhaoli Mountain. The founder of the Liao Dynasty, Yelü Abaoji, rushed to the location. After three days, he finally arrived, and the dragon was still present. Yelü Abaoji shot and killed the dragon. The dragon had one horn, a long tail, short feet, a body five chi long, and a tongue two and a half cun long. He ordered it to be stored in the imperial treasury. It remained there even after the Jin Dynasty moved its capital southward in the Zhenyou era, and people saw its tongue in the shape of straw.

    都城夜怪
    My maternal uncle Zhang Boda and Zeng Feiqing, who were preparing for the provincial examination in the second month of the Chongqing era, stayed at the Welcome Dragon Street. One night, Wang Xing, the servant, got up to relieve himself. As soon as his feet stepped out the door, he saw a ghost on the opposite street. The ghost had a green face and red hair, eyes like torches, and was wielding a sword on the wrist. Beside him stood a soldier who was especially terrifying and fierce. Wang Xing screamed and fell down. After about three or four hours, he woke up. When asked, he said what he had seen.

    63

    都城大火
    　　大安末，都城频岁大火。凡被焚之家，或墙壁间，先有朱书字记之，寻即火起。互相访问，无不然者。凡延烧三数万家。市中佛阁，自唐日有之，辽人又谓之护国仁王佛坛、千手眼大悲阁，字虞世南所书。及阁被焚，卫绍王有旨，令救世南书榜，顾盼中已无及矣！识者谓护国坛被焚，不祥之甚！不一年，遂有虎贼弑逆之变。
    　　骈胎
    　　兴定、元光闲，阳翟小学王奉先，其妻先产四子，再生三子。辛未十一月，秀容福田寺农民范班妻，连三岁举三男三女，皆死矣。此岁复生一男一女。其母从旁叹讶云：“汝必不活，得早过去亦好。”儿忽能言，连曰：“不去！不去！”母惊，语其父；语未竟，儿依前言不去。未几儿女皆死。南齐褚侍中澄《医说》，论受形有云：“阴阳俱至，非男非女之身；精血散分，骈胎品胎之兆。如言化生，固有是理，不足为讶。”予谓褚论固不可废，然骈胎品胎二家者，世亦不多见耳！

    Explanation

    63

    Great Fire in the Capital City

    At the end of the Da'an era, the capital city was repeatedly struck by great fires. In every household that was burned, there were often red inscriptions on the walls, which were followed by the outbreak of fire. When people asked each other about these inscriptions, they found that they were all true. The fires spread to burn several ten thousand households. There was a Buddhist pavilion in the marketplace, which had existed since the Tang dynasty. The Liao people called it the National Protection King Buddha Altar, the Thousand-Handed and Thousand-Eyed Great Compassion Pavilion, and it was written by Yu Shinan. When the pavilion was burned down, Emperor Wanyan Yong issued an order to save Yu Shinan's calligraphy, but it was already too late! Those who understood the situation said that the burning of the National Protection King Buddha Altar was extremely ominous! Within a year, there was a coup d'état by the tiger bandits.

    Twin Fetuses

    During the Xingding and Yuanguang eras, Wang Fengxian, a teacher at a primary school in Yangzhai, his wife first gave birth to four sons, and then to three more sons. In November of the Xinwei year, Fan Ban, a farmer from Xiurong's Fuchan Temple, his wife gave birth to three boys and three girls for three consecutive years, all of whom died. This year, she gave birth to one more boy and one more girl. Her mother-in-law, standing by, lamented, "You will surely not survive. It would be better if you could pass away early." The child suddenly spoke, saying, "I won't go! I won't go!" The mother was shocked and told her husband; before she finished speaking, the child repeated, "I won't go!" Soon after, both the boy and the girl died. In the Southern Qi dynasty, Zhu Cheng, the Grand Secretary, wrote in his Medical Discourse about the formation of life: "When both yin and yang come together, it is neither male nor female; when essence and blood are scattered and divided, it is a sign of twin fetuses. If one says it is transmigration, there is indeed such a principle, and there is no need to be surprised." I believe that Zhu Cheng's theory cannot be discarded, but such cases of twin fetuses are not commonly seen in the world.

    64

    童哥
    　　南渡后，京师一满师者，事一神童。自言出贵家，姓阿不罕氏。八岁遭平章进忠弃都城，人负之，夺门出，人马蹂践而死。夙世负满师钱无算，今来偿之。京师贵家无不迎，至传达宫禁。问者焚香、酹酒，满袖手其旁，童自与人语，明了可辨。寻其声在空中，酹酒在地，则飕然而下，如就饮之者。问逋亡、遗失，不涉争讼，不关利害，则言之。问以千里外事，则曰：“我往问之。”良久至，必以困乏为言。所经之家，他日虽满不在，亦自来语话。满由是致富。汴京破后，闻复北上，出入贵近家矣。
    　　生子两头
    　　正大辛卯十二月，阳翟士人王子思家一婢，生子一身两头。乳媪以为怪，摘去其一，气系分两岐而出。明年正月，西行诸军有三峰之败。

    Explanation

    64

    Translation

    Tong Ge
    After the Southern Migration, there was a monk in the capital who served a divine child. The child claimed to be from a noble family, surnamed Abuhuan. At eight years old, he was abandoned by Pingzhang Jinchong, the chief minister, as they fled the capital. People carried him, forcing their way out through the gates, where he was trampled to death by horses and people. He had owed the monk countless debts from past lives and now came to repay them. Noble families in the capital welcomed him, and he even conveyed messages to the imperial palace. Those who asked questions burned incense and poured wine, while the monk stood by with folded hands. The child spoke to people on his own, clearly and distinctly. Seeking his voice in the air, when the wine was poured on the ground, he descended swiftly, as if drinking it. He answered questions about fugitives and lost items, but not those involving lawsuits or interests. When asked about matters far away, he would say, "I will go and ask." After a long time, he would return, always speaking of poverty and hardship. The families he had passed through, even if the monk was not there later, he still came to speak. The monk thus became wealthy. After the fall of Kaifeng, he was heard to return to the north, entering and leaving the homes of the nobility and the court.

    Two-Headed Child
    In the twelfth month of the Xinmao year of Zhengda, a servant in the household of Wang Zisi, a scholar from Yangdi, gave birth to a child with two heads. The wet nurse thought this was strange and removed one head, but the child's breath divided into two branches and exited. In the following January, the western expeditionary forces suffered a defeat at the Three Peaks.

    65

    生死之数
    　　王右司仲泽，识归德一武弁奥里光禄者，清州人，其子、孙、曾孙，男女俱以九月生，凡十六人。李昂霄同舍生刘远之，燕人，兄弟五人俱以七月生。高唐阎内翰子秀之祖、之父洎其母，后俱以六月二十九日物故，子秀亦然。岂偶然哉！
    　　党承旨生死之异
    　　承旨党公，初在孕，其母梦唐道士吴筠来托宿。为人仪表修整，望之如神仙。在西掖三十年，以承旨致仕。大安三年九月十八终于家。是夕，有大星殒于居。公篆籀入神，李阳冰以后，一人而已！尝谓唐人韩、蔡不通字学，八分自篆籀中来。故公书上轧钟、蔡，其下不论也。小楷如虞、褚，亦当为中朝第一。书法以鲁公为正，柳诚悬以下不论也。古人名一艺，而公独兼之，不谓之全可乎？其为当世所推重如此。东坡谓韩退之，生也有自来，而逝也有所为；以公生死之际观之，亦可以无愧斯语矣！

    Explanation

    65

    Fate of Birth and Death

    Wang Yousi, known as Zhongze, recognized Guideyi Wu Bian Aoli Guanglu, a military officer and high-ranking official from Qingzhou. His descendants, including his son, grandson, and great-grandson, all males and females, were born in September, totaling sixteen people. Li Angxiao's fellow student Liu Yuanzhi, from Yan, had five brothers all born in July. The grandfather, father, and mother of Yan Zishou from Gaotang all died on June 29th, and Zishou also died on the same date. Could this be by chance?

    The Unusual Birth and Death of Party Censuring Director

    Party Gong, the Director of the Secretariat, was conceived when his mother dreamed that the Tang Taoist Wu Jun came to lodge. He had a well-groomed and dignified appearance, looking like a deity. He served in the Western Office for thirty years and retired as the Director of the Secretariat. He passed away at home on the eighteenth day of the ninth month in the third year of Da'an. That night, a large star fell in his residence. His seal script and clerical script reached a divine level; after Li Yangbing, he was the only one! He once said that the Tang people Han and Cai did not understand the art of writing, and the eight-part script comes from the seal and clerical scripts. Therefore, his writing surpassed Zhong and Cai, and those below are not worth mentioning. His small regular script was like Yu and Zhu, and it should also be the first in the imperial court. Calligraphy takes Lu Gong as the standard, and those below Liu Chengxuan are not worth mentioning. Ancient people named their arts, but he alone possessed all of them. Can we not call him complete? He was so highly esteemed by his contemporaries. Dongpo said about Han Tuozhi, "life has its own origin, and death has its own purpose"; observing his life and death, one can also be without shame in these words.

    66

    天赐夫人
    　　广宁闾山公庙，灵应甚著，又其象设狞恶，林木蔽映，人白昼入其中，皆恐怖毛竖。旁近言：静夜时闻讯掠声。故过者或迂路避之。参知政事梁公肃，家此乡之牵马岭。作举子时，与诸生结夏课，谈及鬼神事，历数时人之胆勇者，梁公都不之许。因自言：“我能以昏暮或阴晦之际，入闾山庙、巡廊庑一周。诸生从臾之曰：“能往，何以取信？”梁公曰：“我当就周行处以物画之，用是为验。”明日晚，约偕往。诸生待于庙门外。奋袖径去。画至庙之东隅，摸索有一人倚壁而立，梁公意其为鬼，负之出。诸生迎问何所见？梁公笑曰：“我负一鬼至矣！可取火照之。

    Explanation

    66

    Lady Bestowed by Heaven

    The temple of the public deity in the mountain of the town in Guangning is renowned for its miraculous responses. The statues within are fearsome and ugly, with trees obscuring and shadowing the area. Even during the day, people who enter the temple feel terrified and their hair stands on end. Those nearby say that at quiet nights, one can hear the sound of pursuit or plunder. Thus, passersby may take detours to avoid it. Liang Gong Su, a high-ranking official, lived in this village on Qianma Ridge. When he was a scholar preparing for the imperial examinations, he formed a study group with other scholars during the summer and discussed matters of ghosts and spirits. They listed contemporary people known for their courage, but Liang Gong did not agree with them. He then said, "I can enter the temple of the mountain of the town at dusk or during a gloomy, overcast time and walk around the corridors once." The other scholars urged him, saying, "If you can go, how can we believe you?" Liang Gong replied, "I will mark the places I walk with something, using this as proof." The next evening, they agreed to go together. The other scholars waited outside the temple gate. He waved his sleeves and went straight in. He marked the eastern corner of the temple, and as he felt around, he found a person leaning against the wall. Liang Gong thought it was a ghost and carried it out. The other scholars greeted him and asked what he saw. He laughed and said, "I carried a ghost with me! You can light a fire to see it."

    67

    ”及火至，见是一美妇，衣装绝与世俗不同。欲问诘之，则气息奄奄，状若昏醉。诸生真谓鬼物，环立守之。良久开目，见人环绕，惊怖不自禁。问此为何地？诸生为言其处，及庙中得之者；且诘其为人、为鬼？何所从来？妇言：“我扬州大族某氏女，以吉日迎往婿家。在舆中忽为大风所飘，神识散乱，不知何以至此？”诸生喜曰：“梁生未受室，神物乃从扬州送一妻至，诚有冥数存乎其间！可因而成之。”梁公乃携妇归。寻擢第。不十数年，致身通显。妇举数子。故时人有“天赐夫人”之目，至于传达宫禁。梁公以大定二十年，节度彰德，相下耆旧仍有及见之者。兵乱后，梁氏尚多，问其家世，多“天赐”诸孙行云。

    Explanation

    67

    When the fire arrived, they saw a beautiful woman whose attire was completely different from that of ordinary people. They wanted to question her, but she was breathing weakly, as if she were in a stupor. The students truly believed her to be a ghostly entity and stood in a circle around her, guarding her. After a long time, she opened her eyes and saw people surrounding her, and she was terrified and could not control herself. They asked her where she was, and the students told her the place and that they had found her in the temple. They also questioned her about whether she was a human or a ghost, and where she had come from. She replied, "I am a woman from a prominent family in Yangzhou, who was escorted to my husband's home on an auspicious day. In the carriage, I was suddenly carried away by a strong wind, and my senses became scattered; I do not know how I came to be here." The students were delighted and said, "Liang has not yet married, and this divine being has sent a wife to him from Yangzhou. Truly, there is a fate at work here! We can make this work." Liang then took the woman back with him. Soon after, he passed the imperial examination and was promoted to an official position. Within a few years, he achieved a high and prominent position, and the woman gave birth to several children. Therefore, people at the time gave her the title "Heavenly Bestowed Lady," and she even conveyed messages to the imperial palace. Liang, in the year of Dading, governed with virtue, and many of the elderly still saw him. After the war, the Liang family remained numerous, and when people asked about their family background, they often mentioned the descendants of "Heavenly Bestowed Lady."

    68

    北面大王
    　　参政梁公肃，举子时，祈仙问前途。仙批云：“六十入相而已。”后节度彰德，年适六十，以入相未应。会世宗怒宋人就驿中取国书，选于朝，孰可为详问使、不辱君命者，宰相以公应诏。使还，称旨，拜参政。入相之应乃在此。阎内翰子秀笔录，记公临终前二日言：“上帝召我为北面大王。”遂卒。
    　　刘政纯孝
    　　洺州人刘政，初，幼有至性。母老失明，政以舌舐之，经旬复见。及病，昼夜奉医药，衣不解带，刲股肉啖之，至于再三。母死，负士成坟，邻愿助之，不受。禽鸟哀鸣集于墓树。庐墓侧终丧。守臣以闻，世宗嘉之，授太子掌饮丞。以事附史院《本纪》。

    Explanation

    68

    The North-facing King
    Liang Gong Su, when he was a candidate for office, sought immortals to ask about his future. The immortals wrote: "Enter the position of chancellor at the age of sixty." Later, he became the military governor of Zhengde at the age of sixty, but the prophecy of becoming a chancellor had not yet been fulfilled. When Emperor Shizong was angry that the Song people took the national letter from the imperial post, he selected someone from the court who could serve as a detailed inquiry envoy and not disgrace the king's command. The chancellor recommended Liang Gong Su, who was then appointed as a deputy prime minister. Upon his return, he met the emperor's expectations and was appointed as a deputy prime minister. The prophecy of becoming a chancellor was fulfilled in this way. The Inner Courtian Yan Zixiu recorded this, and Liang Gong Su said two days before his death: "God summoned me to be the North-facing King." He then died.

    Liu Zheng's Pure Filial Piety
    Liu Zheng, a man from Mingzhou, was a noble person from a young age. His mother was blind, and Liu Zheng licked her eyes, and after ten days, her sight returned. When she fell ill, Liu Zheng administered medicine to her day and night, never removing his clothes, and cut meat from his thigh to feed her, doing so multiple times. After his mother's death, he carried earth to build her grave, and birds mourned and gathered around the tomb tree. He built a hut beside the grave and stayed there until the mourning period ended. The local official reported this to the emperor, who praised Liu Zheng and appointed him as the Chief of Wine for the Crown Prince. His story is recorded in the historical annals.

    69

    卷三
    　　杨洞微
    　　道士杨谷，字洞微，代州人，隐居华山。为人仪观秀伟，道行卓绝，平生未尝与物忤。通《庄》、《易》，世以“《庄子》杨先生”目之。明昌闲，诏征高道，隶天长观。未几还山。其将归也，与知观侯生食于市，书数“火”字于食案。又属侯言：“昨过沃州，闻君母病，可速归。”侯以假去。及至沃州而母不病。侯生谇语曰：“渠绐我邪！”及北还，天长已被焚矣！又尝与客游崧山白龟泉上。见一石蠏出，客曰：“蠏横行，殆天性乎？”洞微曰：“此物固横行，恨不值正人耳！”随以手指之蠏即正行。晚爱中方，卜居之。中方旧无泉，苦于远汲。洞微言：“山秀如此，不应无泉。”乃斋沐致祷。筮之，得吉征。

    Explanation

    69

    Chapter Three
    Elan Dongwei

    The Taoist priest Yang Gu, courtesy name Dongwei, was from Dai Prefecture and lived in seclusion on Mount Hua. He was a man of noble appearance and outstanding spiritual cultivation, never having conflicted with others throughout his life. Proficient in the Zhuangzi and the Yijing, he was known as "Mr. Yang of the Zhuangzi" by the world. During the reign of Emperor Shengzong (Mingchang era), he was summoned by imperial decree as a highly accomplished Taoist and assigned to the Tianshang Temple. Not long after, he returned to the mountains. On his way back, he ate with the head of the temple, Hou Sheng, in the marketplace and wrote several "fire" characters on the dining table. He then instructed Hou to say, "Yesterday, I passed through Wozhou and heard that your mother was ill. You should return quickly." Hou took leave and went home. By the time he arrived in Wozhou, his mother was not sick. Hou, in frustration, said, "Did he deceive me?" Upon returning north, he found that the Tianshang Temple had already been burned down. Once, while traveling with a guest on White Turtle Spring at Mount Song, he saw a stone crab emerge. The guest remarked, "Crabs walk sideways; is this their nature?" Elan replied, "This creature indeed walks sideways, but it is a pity that it does not encounter a righteous person!" As he pointed to the crab, it immediately walked straight. Later, he grew fond of Aizhongfang and chose to settle there. Aizhongfang previously lacked a spring, making it difficult to fetch water from a distance. Elan said, "The mountain is so beautiful; it should not lack a spring." He then purified himself through fasting and washing, offered prayers, consulted the oracle, and received a favorable sign.

    70

    是时十月，庵旁近葵花荣茂。洞微云：“于文，“草癸”为“葵”，此殆水征也！”与众道士行寻之。见巽隅草树间隐隐有微润，掘之，果得泉，可供数百指。然东隔绝涧，南限群峰，石壁峻峭，几百步不可越。洞微与弟子吕泽辈沿壁作栈道，以通往来。人以栈木易朽，虑有颠挤之患，乃就壁取石，凿窍嵌之，叠为石梁，甃泉为池。自是中方得水甚易。至今人目为“杨公泉。”闲闲尝为作文记之。又言：“吾友潘若净，字清容，有道之士也。尝从洞微游，甚叹服之。云：‘杨洞微，当求之古人中耳！’”闲闲后过华州，追怀洞微云：“前年曾就云台宿。知有先生在华山。今日白云峰顶起，却疑骑鹤下人间。”其称道如此。

    Explanation

    70

    At this time in October, the sunflowers near the hermitage were luxuriant and flourishing. Yang Dongwei remarked, "In classical texts, 'grass chrysanthemum' is often used interchangeably with 'sunflower,' which is likely a sign of water!" He and other Taoist priests went to search for it. They saw a faint moisture in the grass and trees at the southeastern corner, and upon digging, they indeed found a spring that could supply water for several hundred people. However, it was separated by a deep ravine to the east and limited by a range of mountains to the southeast, with a steep and rugged stone wall hundreds of steps high, making it impossible to cross. Yang Dongwei and his disciple Lu Ze, along with others, built a suspension bridge along the cliff face to facilitate passage. People were concerned that the wooden planks of the suspension bridge would rot and cause accidents, so they carved holes in the stone and embedded them to create a stone bridge, lining the spring with stone to form a pool. From then on, obtaining water became much easier. Today, people call it the "Yang Gong Spring." Xianxian once wrote an essay to commemorate this event. He also said, "My friend Pan Ruojing, courtesy name Qingrong, is a man of virtue and learning. He once accompanied Yang Dongwei on a journey and greatly admired him. He said, 'Yang Dongwei should be sought among the ancients!'" Afterward, Xianxian passed through Huazhou and recalled Yang Dongwei, saying, "Last year, I stayed at the Cloudy Terrace. I knew there was a master in Mount Hua. Today, he seems to have descended from the peak of White Cloud Peak, as if riding a crane down to the mortal world." This is how the master was praised.

    71

    测影
    　　司天测景，冬夏二至，中都以北渐差。中都冬至一丈五尺七寸六分，夏至二尺二寸六分；昼六十一刻，夜三十九刻。山后凉陉金莲川在都西北四百里而近，其地最高。夏至昼六十三刻，夜三十七刻。上京临潢府在都北三千里，夏至昼六十四刻，夜三十六刻。《吕氏碣石录》云。
    　　猎犬
    　　泰和五年，道陵猎云龙川。兴州产犬，宗室咬住进数犬云：“可备射虎，”上因令试之。犬见虎，一前出诱之，虎奔逐；众犬群起，或前或后，左右伺便挦啮。虎艰于周旋，或怒跃一二丈，意欲逸去，而群犬随及。虎既困而卧，卫士前射之。竟毙于群犬。

    Explanation

    71

    Translation

    Shadow Measurement
    The practice of measuring shadows for astronomical observations shows that the measurements for the winter and summer solstices gradually increase in areas north of the capital. In the capital, the winter solstice shadow measures one zhang five chi seven cun six fen, and the summer solstice shadow measures two chi two cun six fen; the day is divided into 61 time units (ke) for daylight and 39 for nighttime. The high-altitude area of Jinlian Plain, located in the northwest of the capital, is about four hundred li away and is the highest place. During the summer solstice, the daylight lasts 63 time units and the nighttime 37 time units. Linhuangfu, the northern capital, is about three thousand li north of the capital, and during the summer solstice, the daylight lasts 64 time units and the nighttime 36 time units. This is recorded in the "Jie Shi Lu" (碣石录) by Lu Shi.

    Hunting Dogs
    In the fifth year of the Taihe era, Emperor Xuanzong hunted in Yunlong River. Hunting dogs from Xingzhou were presented by a member of the imperial family named Yaotu, who said, "These can be used for hunting tigers." The emperor then ordered a test of the dogs' abilities. When the dogs saw a tiger, one dog led the charge and lured the tiger, which chased after it. The other dogs then joined the chase, attacking from various angles. The tiger struggled to maneuver and, in anger, jumped one or two zhang, attempting to escape, but the dogs continued to pursue it. The tiger became exhausted and lay down, and the guards shot it. Ultimately, the tiger was killed by the dogs.

    72

    雷震佃客
    　　陕州卢村张海，与同里一农民有。佃客发谋，诬此人以烧麦积。渠从旁证之。海缚农民解尉司。农性纯质，不能自明，分一死矣！三人者行至南城外，忽雷震佃客，从空而下，骨肉皆尽，惟皮发存耳！士人牛叔玉亲见。时郭敬叔为陕令也。
    　　方长老前身
    　　丹霞长老义方，字志道，尉氏人。前身柳小二，亦县人。大定初，群小聚议烧相国寺三门，乘乱劫军资库。凡五十人，分部探姓名，柳小二与一人当放火。先就门下行视可以谋度举火。柳私自念言：“此门国力所成，大如木山，一火之后，再不可得。如此功缘，我乃坏之，可惜、可惜！”感叹之际，被擒州桥上，讯掠而死。死后托生县中陈家。六七岁能言前世事。访父母妻子、及垫财所在，信为柳小二无疑。小二家供给之。出家法云寺，后嗣法铸和尚。住丹霞寺，亲为予言。

    Explanation

    72

    Translation:

    Thunder Strikes the Tenant Farmer

    In the village of Lu, Shaanxi, Zhang Hai had a dispute with a fellow villager, a farmer. The tenant farmer hatched a plot and falsely accused the farmer of burning the wheat stack. Zhang Hai, acting as a witness, bound the farmer and took him to the county magistrate's office. The farmer, being simple and honest, could not defend himself and was sentenced to death! As the three of them walked to the south gate of the city, suddenly, a bolt of lightning struck the tenant farmer, causing him to fall from the sky, his bones and flesh reduced to nothing, leaving only his skin and hair intact! The scholar Ni Shuyu witnessed this event. At that time, Guo Jingshu was the magistrate of Shaanxi.

    The Former Life of Venerable Fang

    Venerable Fang, known as Yifang, was a monk at Danxia Temple in Weishi. His former life was as Liu Xia'er, also a native of the county. In the early years of the Dading era, a group of ruffians gathered to plan the burning of the three gates of Xiangguo Temple and to seize the military treasury during the chaos. There were fifty people in total, divided into groups to investigate names. Liu Xia'er and one other person were assigned to set the fire. First, they went down to the gate to survey the area and plan how to ignite the fire. Liu Xia'er thought to himself, "This gate was built with national resources, as large as a wooden mountain. Once it is burned, it cannot be rebuilt. Such a great achievement, I am destroying it, how regrettable, how regrettable!" As he was reflecting, he was captured on the bridge in the city, interrogated and beaten to death. After his death, he was reborn into the Chen family in the county. At the age of six or seven, he could recount the events of his previous life. He found his parents, wife, and the location of their property, and there was no doubt that he was indeed Liu Xia'er. The family provided for him. He left home and entered the monastic life at Fayan Temple, later succeeding the teachings of Venerable Zhuang. He resided at Danxia Temple and personally told me this story.

    73

    老赵后身
    　　巩州仇家巷解库赵九老父赵三，大安二年病殆。寻生临洮西小字街银孙家。年十六托人访赵九，说前后身事，且呼赵九来看。赵九遣人往迎。将出巩州，家人奔走来迓，赵九在众中、疑信尚未决。孙童遥见赵九，呼小字大骂，怒其不即来认，见妻亦骂之。指妻臂上烧瘢及树下窖粟处。从是往来两家。州将宗室荣禄、倅李好复、节度副使史舜元异其事，亲问之，说初为人所召，至一大官府。卒令候于门。良久而出曰：“不须见长，但从我行。”乘一骡，至数里外，入河滨。一妇先在此。卒指妇云：“此汝母也！”错愕之际，为卒推水，中遂不记。至三岁始悟前生云。

    Explanation

    73

    The Reincarnation of Old Zhao
    In the year Da'an 2, Zhao San, the father of Zhao Jiu, who lived in the Caojia Alley of Gongzhou, fell gravely ill. Soon after, he was reborn in the Silver Sun family in the West Small Street of Lintao. At the age of sixteen, the boy entrusted someone to visit Zhao Jiu and told him about his past and present lives, calling Zhao Jiu to come and see. Zhao Jiu sent someone to welcome the boy. As the boy was about to leave Gongzhou, his family rushed to meet him. Zhao Jiu, among the crowd, was still unsure whether to believe the story. The boy servant saw Zhao Jiu from afar, called him by his nickname, and cursed him, angry that he did not come immediately to recognize him. When he saw Zhao Jiu's wife, he also cursed her. He pointed out the burn scar on his wife's arm and the place where grain was stored under a tree. From then on, the boy visited both families. The state governor, the royal family member Ronglu, the deputy governor Li Haofu, and the vice-commander Shi Shunyuan were amazed by the event and personally questioned him. The boy said he was first summoned by someone and arrived at a large official residence. A soldier ordered him to wait at the gate. After a long time, the soldier came out and said, "No need to see the master, just follow me." The boy rode a donkey, went several miles, and entered the riverbank. A woman was already there. The soldier pointed to the woman and said, "This is your mother!" In a moment of shock, the boy was pushed into the water by the soldier and lost consciousness. He did not remember anything until he was three years old, when he began to recall his past life.

    74

    刘致君见异人
    　　龙山刘仲尹致君，年二十。“不贵异物民乃足”榜擢第。释褐赞皇尉。一日巡捕，早至山寺中，见壁上有诗云：“长梢叠叶正飕飕，枕底寒声为客留。野鹤不来山月堕，独眠滋味五更秋。”问僧谁所题？言：“一客年可六十许，衣著丰神奇异，昨夜寄宿，今旦题诗而去。墨尚未干，去未远也。”致君分遣弓兵踪迹之。少焉，兵来报：“客在山中大树下待君。”致君载酒往，见客前揖，客亦与之抗礼。问姓名，不答，指酒索饮。致君见其谈吐洒落，知其异人。以平生《经》、《传》疑事质之，酬对详尽，得所未闻。客亦谓致君为可与语。举杯引满，引及从者。日将夕，致君与吏卒皆大醉。及醒，失客所在。致君此后诗学大进。其外孙李内翰钦叔为予言。

    Explanation

    74

    A Strange Encounter with Liu Zhongyin

    Liu Zhongyin, from Longshan, was twenty years old when he passed the examination with the inscription "By not valuing rare objects, the people will be content." He then began his official career as a magistrate of Zanhuang. One day, while patrolling, he arrived early at a mountain temple and saw a poem on the wall: "The long branches and layered leaves rustle softly, the cold sound under the pillow lingers for the guest. The wild crane does not come, and the mountain moon sets; the taste of sleeping alone in the fifth watch of autumn." He asked the monk who had written it, and the monk replied, "A guest, about sixty years old, with rich and strange attire, stayed here last night and wrote this poem this morning before leaving. The ink is not yet dry, so he has not gone far." Liu Zhongyin dispatched archers to track the guest down. Soon, the soldiers reported, "The guest is waiting for you under a big tree in the mountains." Liu Zhongyin took wine with him and went to meet the guest, who greeted him with a bow. The guest also reciprocated with a respectful bow. When Liu asked for his name, the guest did not respond but pointed to the wine and asked for a drink. Liu Zhongyin saw that the guest's conversation was graceful and realized he was a strange and extraordinary person. He asked the guest about questions from his life concerning the Five Classics and Transmission, and the guest answered in detail, revealing things Liu had never heard before. The guest also thought that Liu was someone he could converse with. They raised their cups and drank, inviting their followers to join. As the day grew late, Liu Zhongyin and his attendants all became very drunk. When they woke up, the guest was gone. After this encounter, Liu Zhongyin made great progress in his poetry. His grandson, Li Qinshu, an imperial historian, told me about this.

    75

    潼山庄氏
    　　灵壁北四十里，地名潼山。有南华观。庄子之后余二百家，族长以行第数之，有二十八翁、二十九翁之目。官给杖印，主词讼。风俗醇厚。俗中有善谈玄者。介休乌元章题其《南华》诗云：“试拈真理问南华，生死元如觉梦何？昼夜曾停觉梦否？古今还续死生么？潼山岁岁生春草，雎水年年有绿波。子逝于今已千岁，觉时何少梦时多？”

    75

    Tongshan Zhuang Family
    Forty li north of Lingbi lies a place called Tongshan. There is a Taoist temple named Nanhuaguan (Southern Flower Temple). Descendants of Zhuangzi number over two hundred families. The clan leader is counted by his order of birth, with titles such as "the Twenty-Eighth Elder" and "the Twenty-Ninth Elder." Officially provided with a staff and seal, he handles legal disputes. The customs are simple and genuine. Among the common people, there are those skilled in discussing profound matters. Jieyou's Wu Yuanchang inscribed a poem about the Nanhua:
    "Try to grasp the truth by asking the Nanhua,
    Life and death originally are like waking from a dream.
    Have day and night ever stopped waking from a dream?
    Do past and present still continue life and death?
    Tongshan grows spring grass year after year,
    Jui River has green waves year after year.
    You have passed away up to now for a thousand years,
    Awake time is how little, while dream time is much."

    END TRANSLATION

    76

    王登庸前身
    　　王登庸，平州人，“日合天统”榜进士，历宰数县，皆有能声，为予同年。苏鼎臣说：渠前身同里刘氏女，年十六七岁，采桑堕树下，伤重、气未绝，而灵识已托生王家。满月剃胎发，前身亦知痛而哭。甫求往刘家。其后两家供承，令举子。刘氏父母死，皆为服心丧三年。
    　　大明川异卵
    　　曲阳医者郭彦达，曾居大明川。闻一田夫董成者扫地至门限，地即高起，以锸铲平之，已而复高。如是三四。疑而掘之，先得一卵如椀许，壳膜见中有二蛇，一黑一斑。又掘得一卵，比前差大。彦达晓之曰：“神物不可触，祭拜而送之。”成如言，送滨河中。是岁川下上雷雨拔大木数千。人以疫死者数百人。

    Explanation

    76

    A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms.

    Example 3

    Source: 凡為文章，猶乘騏驥，雖有逸氣，當以銜勒制之，勿使流亂軌躅，放意填坑岸也。

    Translation: In all writing, it is like riding a swift steed — though it may possess a wild and unrestrained spirit, one must control it with bit and bridle, and must not let it run wild, straying from the proper path or indulging in aimless wanderings.

    Example 4

    Source: 自古明王聖帝，猶須勤學，況凡庶乎！此事遍於經史，吾亦不能鄭重，聊舉近世切要，以啟寤汝耳。

    Translation: From ancient times, wise kings and sage emperors still required diligent study; how much more so, then, for common people! This matter is found throughout the classics and histories. I cannot elaborate further, but I will briefly mention a few essential points of recent times in order to enlighten you.

    Example 5

    Source: 夫文章者，原出五經：詔命策檄，生於書者也；序述論議，生於易者也；歌詠賦頌，生於詩者也；祭祀哀誄，生於禮者也；書奏箴銘，生於春秋者也。朝廷憲章，軍旅誓誥，敷顯仁義，發明功德，牧民建國，不可暫無。至於陶冶性靈，從容諷諫，入其滋味，亦樂事也。行有餘力，則可習之。

    Translation: As for writings, their origin lies in the Five Classics: edicts, memorials, and military proclamations arise from the Shujing (Book of Documents); expository and argumentative writings arise from the Yijing (Book of Changes); songs, odes, and praises arise from the Shijing (Book of Poetry); ritual sacrifices, mourning, and elegies arise from the Liji (Book of Rites); memorials, admonitions, and inscriptions arise from the Chunqiu (Spring and Autumn Annals). Court regulations, military oaths and decrees, the proclamation of benevolence and righteousness, the elucidation of virtue and merit, governing the people and establishing the state—all are indispensable. As for cultivating the mind and spirit, offering gentle admonition in a relaxed manner, and savoring the flavor of such writings, these too are pleasant pursuits. When one has spare energy, then one may study them.

    Final Translation of the Source Text

    Wang Dengong's Previous Life

    Wang Dengong was from Pingzhou and passed the imperial examination of the "Rihetiantong" list, becoming a successful scholar. He served as the magistrate of several counties and was known for his ability and reputation. He was my contemporary. Su Dingchen said: His previous life was that of a woman from the Liu family in the same village, who was about sixteen or seventeen years old. She fell from a tree while picking mulberry leaves and was severely injured, but she did not die. Her soul had already been reborn in the Wang family. On the day of the full moon, when her hair was shaved, she felt pain and cried. She immediately requested to go to the Liu family. Later, both families supported her, encouraging her to pursue scholarship. When the Liu family's parents died, she observed a three-year period of heart mourning for them.

    The Strange Egg from the Great Bright River

    Guo Yanda, a physician from Quyang, once lived by the Great Bright River. He heard that a farmer named Dong Cheng swept the threshold of his door, and the ground rose up. He used a spade to flatten it, but it rose again. This happened three or four times. Suspecting something, he dug and found an egg about the size of a bowl, with a membrane inside showing two snakes, one black and one spotted. He dug up another egg, which was slightly larger than the first. Guo Yanda explained to him, saying, "This is a divine creature and should not be touched. Worship it and send it away." Dong Cheng followed his advice and sent it to the riverbank. That year, the river experienced severe storms and floods, uprooting thousands of trees. Hundreds of people died from the resulting epidemic.

    This translation aims to capture the essence of the original text while ensuring it reads naturally in English. The idiomatic expressions, cultural allusions, syntactic ambiguities, and proper nouns have been handled as planned to

    三姑庙龙见
    　　大名蚕神三姑庙旁近龙见，横卧三草舍上。观者数百人。见龙鳞甲中幽黄色，其形如驼峰，头与一大树齐。腥臭不可近。既堕夭矫不得上。良久，云雾复合，乃去。时己酉岁七、八月间也。
    　　镜辨
    　　蔡内翰正甫云：大定七年秋，与萧彦昭俱官都下。萧一日见过，出古镜相示曰：“顷岁得之关中。虽爱之甚，然背文四字不尽识，且不知为何时物。”予取视之，汉物也。文曰：“长宜子孙。”《宣和博古图》有焉。出图示之，殆若合符。彦昭惊喜。有姚仲瞻在坐，言曰：“仆家一镜，制作亦奇。宋末得于长安土人家。相传为太真奁中物，不之信也。”使取而观，背有楷字数十，为韵语，句四言。

    The Appearance of a Dragon at the Three Nuns Temple

    Near the Three Nuns Temple in Daming, a dragon appeared, lying horizontally across three thatched huts. Hundreds of spectators gathered to witness the event. The dragon's scales were a deep yellow, and its shape resembled a camel's hump, with its head level with a large tree. The stench was so foul that it could not be approached. After falling, the dragon could not rise again. After a long time, the clouds and mist reformed, and the dragon departed. This occurred during the seventh or eighth month of the year of Gengyou.

    Identification of the Mirror

    Cai Neihan Zhengfu said: In the autumn of the seventh year of Dading, I was serving in the capital with Xiao Yanzhao. One day, Xiao Yanzhao visited me and showed me an ancient mirror, saying: "I recently obtained this from Guanzhong. Although I loved it very much, I did not fully recognize the four characters on the back, and I did not know what period it belonged to." I took a look at it, and it was from the Han dynasty. The inscription reads: "May your descendants thrive." It is recorded in the Xuanhe Catalogue of Ancient Artifacts. I showed him the catalogue, and it matched almost perfectly. Xiao Yanzhao was surprised and delighted. Yao Zhongzhan was present, and he said: "In my family, there is a mirror that is also uniquely crafted. It was obtained in the late Song dynasty from a family in Chang'an. It is said to have been a mirror from Yang Guifei's makeup box, but I did not believe it." I asked him to bring it over, and on the back, there were dozens of regular script characters forming a rhythmic poem with four-character lines.

    78

    其略有：“华屋交映，珠帘对看，潜窥圣淑，丽则常端”等语，而纽有开元二字。姚曰：“考其年则唐物，安知为太真之旧耶？”予笑而不答。徐出浮休居士张芸叟所作《冗长录》使读。其间载：“元祐中有耕望贤驿故地、得镜遗予者，铭为四字诗。中有‘潜窥圣淑’之句。‘圣淑’二字皆少空，意取圣为君，淑为后耳。”与此制正合。望贤去马嵬数十里，盖迁幸时遗之。浮休，陕右人。得之长安，信矣！彦昭欢甚，以为一日有二奇事，不可不书。予曰：“多言屡中，仲尼所以讥子贡也。然世喜道其偶中，予不书可乎？”
    　　吕内翰遗命
    　　吕防御忠嗣，生平经学有所得，故每以古人自期。临终敕诸子云：“我死无火葬，火葬是为戮尸。无斋僧作佛事。斋僧佛事是不以尧、舜、文、武、周、孔之教待我。有违我言，非吕氏子孙！”诸子从教，无一敢违者。范司农拯之，梁都运斗南每为予言。近岁斗南遗令：“送终不以僧佛从事。”有自来矣！

    Here is the final translation of the source text:

    It briefly contains phrases such as "magnificent buildings reflecting each other, pearl curtains facing each other, secretly peering at the sacred and the virtuous, beautiful and consistently upright," and the inscription has the words "Kaiyuan" (the reign title of Emperor Xuanzong of Tang). Yao said, "Considering the year, it is a Tang artifact; how can we know it was once owned by Yang Guifei?" I smiled without answering. Gradually, I took out the Redundant Record written by the recluse Zhang Yunshou, and asked him to read it. It records that during the reign of Emperor Shenzong, in the old site of the post station called Gengwang Xianyue, an ancient mirror was found, inscribed with a four-character poem. Among its lines was the phrase "secretly peering at the sacred and the virtuous." The characters "sacred" and "virtuous" were slightly empty, suggesting that "sacred" refers to the sovereign and "virtuous" to the empress. This perfectly matches the inscription. Gengwang Xianyue is several miles from the Ma嵬 Slope, where it was likely left during the imperial journey. Zhang Yunshou, from the right side of Shanxi, obtained it in Chang'an, and indeed, it is true! Yanzhao was greatly delighted, thinking that there were two extraordinary events in one day, and it could not be left unrecorded. I said, "Often speaking and often hitting the mark—this is why Confucius criticized Zi Gong. However, the world enjoys talking about his occasional hits; how can I not write it down?"

    Lü Neihan's Last Will

    Lü Zhongsi, throughout his life, gained insights from the study of the classics and always set his standards according to ancient sages. On his deathbed, he gave instructions to his sons: "After I die, do not cremate me; cremation is equivalent to mutilating the body. Do not chant by monks or perform Buddhist ceremonies. Such practices are not treating me according to the teachings of Yao, Shun, Wen, Wu, Zhou, and Confucius. If anyone violates my words, they are not a true descendant of the Lü family!" His sons followed his instructions, and none dared to disobey. Fan Sinao and Liang Duyun Dou Nan often spoke to me about this. Recently, Liang Duyun Dou Nan left a will stating, "No Buddhist rituals at the end of life." This practice has been this way from the beginning.

    宣德狂僧
    　　宣德圣国寺狂僧，布衣蓝缕，独处暗室。夏月不浣濯，无秽气。常于寺家厩舍，合爪向牛马言：“饱斋！饱斋！”生徒大恶之。承安中，春旱。州倅田公问：“何日当雨？”僧言：“四月二十日，雨足矣！”及期果然。刺史为中秋酿酒，僧云：“刺史即东去，何必酿为？”十四日除兴中尹，乘传之官。他所言多验。范拯之说。
    　　吕状元梦应
    　　吕内翰造，字子成。未第时，梦金龙蜿蜒自天而下，攫而食之。是岁经义魁南省，词赋继擢殿元。合门请诗，有“状头家世传三叶，天下科名占两魁。”谓其大父延嗣、父忠嗣与子成，俱状元也。
