    79

    The Mad Monk of Xuan De Temple
    　　The mad monk of the Xuan De Temple wore coarse clothes and lived alone in a dark room. In the summer, he did not wash, yet he had no foul odor. He often stood in the temple's stables and clapped his hands, speaking to the cattle and horses, saying, "Enjoy your meal! Enjoy your meal!" The students greatly disliked him. During the reign of Emperor Cheng'an, there was a spring drought. The deputy governor, Mr. Tian, asked, "When will it rain?" The monk replied, "On the 20th day of the fourth month, it will rain enough!" As expected, it rained on the specified day. The governor was brewing wine for the Mid-Autumn Festival, but the monk said, "The governor is going east. Why bother brewing wine?" On the 14th day, the governor was appointed as the magistrate of Xingzhong and rode in the official carriage to take office. Most of what the monk said came true. As told by Fan Zheng.

    The Imperial Scholar's Dream
    　　Lu Zao, the inner historian, styled himself Zicheng. Before passing the imperial examinations, he dreamed of a golden dragon coiling down from the sky, seizing and eating it. That year, he won first place in the provincial examination for Confucian classics and then won first place in the palace examination for poetry and prose. The imperial gate requested a poem from him, which included the lines, "The imperial scholar's family has three generations of imperial scholars, and the family holds two first-place positions in the imperial examinations." This referred to his great-grandfather Yanshi, grandfather Zhongsu, and himself, all of whom were imperial scholars.

    80

    张子云祈仙
    　　张子云以荫补官，尝作《金人捧露盘》乐府，道退闲之乐，一时哄传之。道陵召为书画都监，累迁冀州倅。一日祈仙，仙批《青门引》词，末句云：“半纸虚名，白发知多少？一桌武陵归计，不如闲早。怕桃花、笑人老。”子云即日致仕。张故人仲叔说。
    　　麻姑乞树
    　　宁海昆仑山石落村刘氏，富于财，尝于海滨浮百丈鱼，取骨为梁，构大屋名曰“鲤堂”。堂前一槐，阴蔽数亩，世所罕见。刘忽梦女官自称麻姑，问刘乞槐树修庙。刘梦中甚难之。既而曰：“庙去此数里，何缘得去？”即漫许之。及寤，异其事，然亦不之信也。后数十日，风雨大作，昏晦如夜。人家知有变，皆入室潜遁。须臾开霁，惟失刘氏槐所在。人相与求，之麻姑庙，此树已卧庙前矣！

    Explanation

    80

    Zhang Ziyun Seeks Immortality

    Zhang Ziyun was appointed to an official position through hereditary privilege. He once wrote a Yuefu poem titled "Jin Ren Peng Lu Pan" (Golden Man Holding the Dew Tray), describing the joy of retirement, which became widely known at the time. Dao Ling summoned him to serve as the supervisor of painting and calligraphy, and he was gradually promoted to the deputy governor of Jizhou. One day, he sought immortality, and a deity responded with a poem titled "Qing Men Yin," ending with the lines: "A mere piece of paper fame, how many gray hairs does it bring? A single boat plan to return to Wuling, it's better to retire early. I fear the peach blossoms will mock my old age." Zhang Ziyun immediately retired. This story was told by his friend Zhong Shu.

    Menggu Asks for a Tree

    In the village of Shiluo near Mount Kunlun in Ninghai, there was a wealthy Liu family. They once caught a hundred-zhang fish in the sea, took its bones to make beams, and constructed a grand hall named "Li Tang" (Hall of the Carp). In front of the hall stood a large locust tree, whose shade covered several acres, a rarity in the world. Liu suddenly dreamed of a female official who identified herself as Menggu and asked Liu to give her the locust tree to build a temple. Liu was hesitant in his dream and replied, "The temple is several miles away. How could the tree be moved there?" He then vaguely agreed. Upon waking, he found the dream strange but did not believe it. After several days, a fierce storm arose, and the sky was dark as night. People knew something was happening and hid indoors. Soon after, the storm cleared, and the locust tree was no longer in Liu's yard. People searched for it and found it lying in front of Menggu's temple!

    81

    孝顺马
    　　宣宗朝，一亲军卒畜一铁色骢，能知人指使。此卒无兼丁，每上直，马自负卧具继至；下直则负之而归。他人或遮关牵掣，则作声势蹄啮之，人莫敢近。虽在军伍或此卒他适，马自寻之，必得所在。卒南征，堕坑堑中，不能起；马跪前二足，因得揽辔而上。何中盛传为“孝顺马。”一日，中贵人劳军淮上，戏令此卒藏匿，纵马自寻。马振辔长鸣，径到主人处。中贵闻之宣宗，为增卒月给。
    　　蝎台
    　　东京宫城东北隅有蝎台。大定中修城，役夫毁台取土。及半，得石函；启之，中有块石，圆滑天成，撼摇作动物声。破之，二大蝎尾捎相钩，旋转不解，见风即死。人有问张都运复亨者云：“辽东无蝎。而蝎在石中，石在函，又为土所埋，人何以知其有蝎而名台也？”张筹度久之，乃云：埋石函者必以数知之。不然，是神告之也。此外我不知。”

    Explanation

    Translation

    Filial Horse

    During the reign of Emperor Xuanzong, a soldier in the imperial guard owned a dark gray horse that could understand and follow human commands. This soldier had no family members to assist him. Every time he was on duty, the horse would bring its own bedding to the location; when his duty ended, the horse would carry the bedding back home. If someone else tried to obstruct or pull at the horse, it would make threatening noises and bite, and no one dared to approach it. Even when the soldier was away from his unit or elsewhere, the horse would find him, always reaching his location. Once, the soldier fell into a pit during a southern campaign and could not get up; the horse knelt on its front two legs, allowing the soldier to grab the reins and climb onto its back. The story of this horse, known as the "Filial Horse," became widely known. One day, a high-ranking eunuch came to console the troops in the Huai region and playfully ordered the soldier to hide, then released the horse to find him. The horse shook its reins and neighed loudly, and immediately went directly to its owner. The eunuch reported this to Emperor Xuanzong, who then increased the soldier's monthly stipend.

    Scorpion Platform

    In the northeastern corner of the eastern capital's palace city, there was a platform called the Scorpion Platform. During the reign of Emperor Shizong, when the city walls were being repaired, laborers dismantled the platform to extract soil. When they had dug halfway through, they found a stone box. Upon opening it, they discovered a round, smooth stone that made animal-like sounds when shaken. When the stone was broken, two large scorpions were found with their tails intertwined and rotating, unable to separate. They died as soon as they were exposed to the air. Someone asked Zhang Duyun Fuheng, "There are no scorpions in Liaodong. How did scorpions end up in the stone, in the box, and buried in the earth? How did people know there were scorpions and name the platform after them?" Zhang pondered for a long time and said, "Those who buried the stone box must have known the number. Otherwise, it must have been a divine message." Beyond that, he did not know.

    82

    陵川瑞花
    　　先人宰陵川。泰和甲子元夕，县学烧镫，有以杏棣棠枯枝为翦彩花者。镫罢，家僮乞之，供于县署佛屋中。四月上七日，先夫人焚诵次，乃见杏棠皆作花，真赝相间。先人会宾示之，以为文字之祥，为赋《瑞花诗》。予年始十五矣。
    　　不食而孕
    　　东京牛氏妇，年未二十，因异梦遂不食，食则吐且病。数年之后，都不减瘦。乙巳岁举一女，又自乳之。其姑挈见范炼师。范谕其姑：“妇已不食，又无便溲，何不令入道？”姑曰：“妇恋小女，不能离耳。”识者意此妇食生气，故动作如常，天癸时至；而爱根不能割，所以有子。书传中亦不多见也。

    Explanation

    82

    陵川瑞花

    My father served as the magistrate of Lingchuan. On the Lantern Festival of the year Jiazi in the Taihe era, the local school burned lamps, and there were paper flowers cut from colored paper made from dried branches of apricot, pear, and hawthorn trees. After the festival, the household servants asked for them and placed them in the Buddha hall of the county office. On the seventh day of the fourth month, my mother was burning incense and reciting scriptures, and she saw that the apricot and hawthorn branches were all in bloom, mixed with real and fake. My father showed this to his guests, who believed it was an auspicious omen for literature, and he wrote a poem titled Ruihua Shi (Poem of Auspicious Flowers). I was just fifteen years old at the time.

    不食而孕

    In the city of Tokyo, a woman from the family of Niu, who was not yet twenty years old, stopped eating because of a strange dream. If she ate, she would vomit and fall ill. After several years, she did not lose weight. In the year YiSi, she gave birth to a daughter, and she nursed her herself. Her mother-in-law took her to see Master Fan, the Daoist. Master Fan told her mother-in-law, "The woman has not eaten, and she has no bowel movements. Why don't you let her join the Dao?" Her mother-in-law replied, "The woman is attached to her little daughter and cannot leave her." Those who understand think that this woman is eating the vital energy, so she acts normally, and her menstrual cycle has come; but her attachment cannot be severed, so she gave birth. Such cases are not common in books and records.

    83

    右腋生子
    　　李炼师湛然，戊申秋入关，亲见一妇娩，身临月，忽右腋发一大疮；疮破，胎胞从疮口出，子母皆安。
    　　李茂相法
    　　完州守杨秀实，正大中权刑部主事，供输关、陕。相者李茂自南中来，相人言休咎殊验。官府以其惑众，羁管之。杨与之熟狎。私自言：“此人言休咎，或寿永、末路荣显，差以自慰；如言前途不远，或日久有他难，只增忧挠耳！”因与茂食次，问曰：“休咎不愿知。但某离老母十月，见面当在何时？”茂且食且笑曰：“君三日当拜太夫人矣！”杨窃谓关、陕去京千里余，三日何缘得到？食未竟，平章芮公急召杨、驿奏边事。三日未日中至家。杨至今以为奇。茂后入京，寓惠安寺，朝士争往叩之。近侍焦春和甫入门，茂即言：“五品、五品，恨来处不高耳！”焦本世宗家童，闻茂言，深耻之。茂未几被戮，年三十三。

    Explanation

    83

    Right Armpit Birth
    Li Zhanran, the Daoist priest, entered the pass in the autumn of 1238 and personally witnessed a strange birth. A woman who was about to give birth suddenly developed a large wound on her right armpit. When the wound opened, the baby emerged from the wound, and both the mother and child were safe.

    Li Moxiang's Prediction
    Yang Xiushi, the governor of Wan Prefecture, was appointed as the chief clerk of the Ministry of Punishments during the Zhengda period. He was responsible for supplying goods to Guanzhong and Shaanxi. A fortune-teller named Li Moxiang came from the south and could predict the future with great accuracy. The government considered him a charlatan and kept him under surveillance. Yang became familiar with Li and said to himself, "He can predict the future, but if he says I will live long and have a distinguished career later, it will be comforting. If he says I will not have much time left or will face difficulties in the future, it will only increase my worries!" During a meal, Yang asked Li, "I don't want to know about my fate. But I have been away from my mother for ten months. When will I see her again?" Li, while eating, laughed and said, "You will meet your mother in three days!" Yang thought it was impossible to travel from Guanzhong and Shaanxi, which were over a thousand miles from the capital, in three days. Before he finished his meal, Prime Minister Rui urgently summoned Yang to report on border affairs. Three days later, Yang arrived home before noon. Yang still considers this event miraculous. Li later went to the capital and stayed at Huian Temple. Many court officials visited him to seek predictions. When a court official named Jiao Chunhe entered the temple, Li immediately said, "You will hold a fifth-rank position, but you wish you came from a higher social status!" Jiao was originally a servant of Emperor Shizong of Jin. Upon hearing Li's prediction, he felt ashamed. Li was eventually executed at the age of thirty-three.

    84

    雷氏节姑
    　　雷氏，浑源人，是西仲、南仲从姊妹行。年十七，嫁为应州丁倅妻。雷氏群从有不悦者，讦告服内成亲，婚遂听离。丁谓夫人言：“绝婚固非我二人意。然夫人此去，再适人否？”雷曰：“我若再嫁，当令两目瞎！”丁云：“夫人果有此心，我亦当同此誓。”其后丁违前言，再娶，未几果丧明。雷氏十八寡居，九十七乃终。从孙希颜，常欲为文记之，竟不及也。
    　　刘生青词之谴
    　　正和初，中牟阳桥人刘慎，字荣辅，为里人刘六作延荐青词。刘平生有秽行，荣辅作词，曲为辨理，又依例荐拔。后数日，荣辅作首，学生鲁罗儿者，病中忽为物所凭，令家人请荣辅来。刘至，罗儿作色呵之曰：“汝昨为刘六作青词，汝于谁处敢妄语耶？”荣辅听罢，惶惧殊甚，手写首状，言自后更不敢复作青词！罗儿不复有言。此儿甫成童，初不知青词为何物。殆是刘过恶显著，荣辅妄为饰说，邀福，神故假此儿以警之耳。

    Explanation

    84

    The Virtuous Maiden of the Lei Family

    The Lei family, from Hunyuan, were related to the Western and Southern branches of the family. At seventeen, she married the deputy magistrate of Yingzhou. Some members of the Lei family who were displeased, accused her of having a pre-marital relationship, and the marriage was then annulled. The deputy magistrate's wife said to her, "Breaking off the marriage was certainly not our intention. But will you remarry?" She replied, "If I remarry, I will make my eyes blind!" The deputy magistrate said, "If you truly have this resolve, I will take the same oath." Later, the deputy magistrate broke his promise and remarried. Not long after, he indeed lost his sight. The Lei maiden remained a widow at eighteen and lived to be ninety-seven years old before passing away. Her grandson, Xiyan, often wanted to write a record of her, but he never got around to it.

    The Punishment for the Green Script

    In the early years of the Zhenghe era, Liu Shen, a native of Yangqiao in Zhongmu, with the courtesy name Rongfu, wrote a green script to recommend Liu Liu to the gods. Liu had a history of immoral behavior, and Rongfu wrote the script, defending Liu's actions, and followed the usual procedure for recommendation. Several days later, Rongfu became the head. A student named Lu Luo'er, who was suddenly possessed by a spirit while ill, ordered his family to summon Rongfu. When Rongfu arrived, Lu Luo'er scolded him, saying, "You wrote a green script for Liu Liu yesterday. Who gave you the right to speak falsely?" After hearing this, Rongfu was extremely frightened and wrote a confession with his own hands, stating that he would never write another green script again. Lu Luo'er said nothing more. This boy was just a young boy and initially did not know what a green script was. Perhaps Liu's sins were so evident, and Rongfu made false statements to seek merit, so the spirit used this boy to warn him.

    85

    陵川人祈仙
    　　陵川士人刘方元卿说：兵乱后，县中人祈仙。杨征君朴降笔，诗尤奇伟不凡。如论“书”字云：“汝知毫端心，万物不可碍。”又云：“龙盘一气云雷定，鲸化三山草木枯。”一席评事者，出高丽疋纸求诗，云：“霜入词锋月痕缺，手中不觉风雷掣。”如是八句，后批云：“慎勿触污！神物终当飞去。”席氏子妇产乳未终月，窃视之。三日后开卷，乃无一字，但空纸而已。刘曾问：“生死之际，其理何如？”云：“死、死，恶死、速死、生非可乐，死非可恶。鬼之恶生，犹人之恶死。但生人不知死者乐耳！”县人都俞，字舜卿，素不信仙鬼事。

    Explanation

    85

    People of Lingchuan Pray for Immortals

    Lingchuan scholar Liu Fangyuanqing said: After the turmoil of war, people in the county prayed for immortals. Yang, the recluse, had a spirit descend and write, and the poetry was particularly extraordinary and remarkable. For instance, when discussing the character "书" (shū), it was said: "Do you know the heart at the tip of the brush, which cannot be obstructed by anything?" It also said: "The dragon coils in one breath, determining the thunder and lightning; the whale transforms into three mountains, causing the grass and trees to wither." One official, during a gathering, presented a sheet of paper from Goryeo and requested a poem, which read: "Frost enters the sharpness of the words, and the moon's trace is incomplete, but in the hand, one does not feel the lightning and thunder." Thus, eight lines were written, followed by a postscript: "Be careful not to touch or stain it! The divine entity will eventually fly away." The wife of the official's son, who had not yet completed her postpartum period, secretly observed the paper. Three days later, when it was opened, there were no words, only an empty sheet of paper. Liu once asked: "What is the nature of life and death?" The spirit replied: "Death, death, hate death, quick death, life is not necessarily enjoyable, death is not necessarily bad. The aversion of ghosts to life is like the aversion of humans to death. But the living do not know that the dead find joy!" County scholar Du Yu, with the courtesy name Shunqing, had always been skeptical of immortals and ghosts.

    86

    一日召舜卿至前云：“与汝银杏。”问：“安在？”批云：“在汝怀中。”都探怀得之。又批云：“与汝樱桃。”都问：“腊月安得有？”批云：“已在汝掌中矣。”都展手，果有。一日，分遗诸人连枝红杏三十余枝，正应在坛诸人之数，或问：“盛冬安得有此？”批云：“此土之冬，非他境之夏乎？”又问：“他境安在？”批云：“在数万里之外。”问云：“那得逡巡至此？”批云：“不疾而速，不行而至，汝不知之乎？”元卿问：“神仙果有无？幸明以告我！”批云：“子尚见疑乎？”元卿今客顺天，屡为予言。故续记于笔，陈于丧乱之后也。

    Explanation

    86

    One day, he summoned Shunqing to the front and said, "I give you a ginkgo." Shunqing asked, "Where is it?" He replied, "It is in your bosom." Shunqing searched his bosom and found it. He then said, "I give you a cherry." Shunqing asked, "How can there be any in the twelfth month?" He replied, "It is already in your hand." Shunqing opened his hand, and indeed there was a cherry. One day, he distributed to many people thirty or more branches of a red apricot tree, which exactly corresponded to the number of people in the assembly. Someone asked, "How can there be such things in the severe winter?" He replied, "This land's winter is not like another place's summer, is it?" Another person asked, "Where is that other place?" He replied, "In a place tens of thousands of miles away." Someone asked, "How can one arrive here in such a short time?" He replied, "Without haste, yet swift; without traveling, yet arrived. Do you not know this?" Yuanqing asked, "Do the immortals truly exist? Please enlighten me!" He replied, "Do you still doubt?" Yuanqing is now a guest in Shuntian and often recounts this story to me. Therefore, I continued to record it with my pen and presented it after the chaos of war and disorder.

    抱阳二龙
    　　顺天西北四十里抱阳岩宝教院，大小二青龙在寺潭中。庙曰“显济。”古碑说：‘二青’见于隋、唐之间，有将军之目，官比刺史。大青崇宁五年封崇惠侯，政和七年进灵益公；小青嘉霈侯，进英泽公。”二龙各长二三尺许，色深翠，朱墨细点间之脊间仿佛成方胜花。行则昂首，不类他蛇。出则绳行木上。能兴云雨，变现不测。乡人祈赛，与之酒，则直立，高二尺余，俯首就盏饮之。故前人诗有“青蛇立饮祭神酒”之句。“二青”居山阳，各有种类，至数十百个，都不毒螫。大青一目眇，其种悉然。

    Explanation

    87

    Baoyang's Two Green Dragons

    Forty li northwest of Shuntian is Baoyang Rock, where the Baojiao Temple stands. Within the temple's pond live two green dragons, large and small. The temple is named "Xianji" (Manifest Aid). Ancient steles recount that the "two greens" were first seen during the Sui and Tang Dynasties, bearing the eyes of generals and holding a rank equivalent to that of a prefect. In the fifth year of Chongning, the larger dragon was enfeoffed as the Lord Chonghui, and in the seventh year of Zhenghe, it was promoted to the Duke Lingyi. The smaller dragon was enfeoffed as the Lord Jiapai and later promoted to the Duke Yingze. Each dragon measures about two to three feet in length, with a deep green hue and red and black fine dots between their spines, vaguely forming square victory flowers. When they move, they raise their heads, unlike other snakes. They walk like ropes on trees. They can summon clouds and rain, and their transformations are unpredictable. The locals offer prayers and sacrifices, and when they are given wine, the dragons stand upright, about two feet tall, bending their heads to drink from the cup. Thus, ancient poets wrote, "The green snake stands upright, drinking the wine of the divine." The "two greens" reside in the sunny slopes of the mountains, each with their own kind, numbering in the dozens or even hundreds, and they do not poison or sting. The larger dragon has one blind eye, and its offspring are all the same.

    88

    凡在山阴者皆杂蛇，例毒螫，然不敢犯山阳“二青”之境，至则为“二青”之族啮杀之。二族亦不往山阴。村落小儿辈与之习惯，至以手捧之。而常夜宿民家卧具中，人亦不骇怪也。此事唐张燕公说、冯瀛王道、宋崇仪使大名总管邢仲良、近代郑州刺史赵摅子充皆尝读书于此。有邢氏继志庵忘归轩，燕公石穴读书堂。明珠窝。初，山石崩，出一穴如杯椀之半，莹滑无琢削痕，似有光彩。土人传有明珠飞出，故以名之。近山三四里所，有升贤村，属满城，冯王故居也。辛亥冬，予与毛正卿德义昆仲、郝伯常、刘敬之诸人一游。寺僧显，淳质有道行，时年七十八，说龙之美。

    Explanation

    88

    All those in the south of the mountain are mixed snakes, typically venomous. Yet they dare not intrude into the territory of 'Two Greens' on the north side of the mountain. If they do, they are bitten and killed by the 'Two Greens' clan. The two clans also do not go to the south of the mountain. The children in the village are accustomed to them and even hold them with their hands. They often sleep in people's bedding at night, and people do not find it strange. This matter was mentioned by Zhang Yan Gong of the Tang Dynasty, Feng Ying Wang, Xing Zhongliang, and Zhao Shu Zichong of the Song Dynasty, all of whom studied here. There is Xing's Ji Zhi An, the Forgetful Pavilion, and Yan Gong's Stone Cave Study Hall. Pearl Nest. Initially, the mountain rocks collapsed, revealing a hole half the size of a cup or bowl, smooth and shiny without any signs of carving, as if it had a luster. The locals say that a pearl flew out, hence the name. Near the mountain, about three to four miles away, there is Shengxian Village, which belongs to Mancheng and was the former residence of Feng Wang. In the winter of Xin Hai, I and my brothers Mao Zhengqing, Hao Bochang, and Liu Jingzhi visited once. The temple monk Xian, simple and virtuous, was 78 years old at the time and spoke of the beauty of dragons.

    三秀轩
    　　李都运有之、高户部唐卿、赵礼部廷玉读书永平西一山寺。腊月，桃树一枝作花，大金蝉集其上，又竹林出一笋。故名所居为“三秀轩”。后三人皆登上第，极品。
    　　王处存墓
    　　王处存墓，在曲阳燕川西北，白虎山之青龙碣。己卯八月，完州人劫破之。骨已灰烬，得银百余星、一砚、一镜、唐哀帝所赐铁券；券刻金字云：“敕葬忠臣王处存，赐钱九万九千九百九十九贯九百九十九文。”其孙周臣说。

    Explanation

    89

    Three Auspicious Pavilion
    Li Duyun, Gao Tangqing, Minister of Revenue, and Zhao Tingyu, Minister of Rites, studied at a temple in a mountain west of Yongping. In the twelfth lunar month, a branch of a peach tree bloomed, a large cicada perched on it, and a bamboo shoot emerged from the bamboo grove. Thus, they named their dwelling "Three Auspicious Pavilion." Later, all three achieved high positions in government, attaining the highest rank.

    Tomb of Wang Chucun
    The tomb of Wang Chucun is located northwest of Yanchuan in Quyang, at the Azure Dragon Monument on White Tiger Mountain. In the eighth month of the year 1579, people from Wan Prefecture raided and destroyed the tomb. The bones were reduced to ashes, and they found over a hundred silver coins, a writing stone, a mirror, and an imperial decree from Emperor Ai of Tang. The decree, inscribed with golden characters, read: "Order to bury the loyal minister Wang Chucun and grant him nine million nine hundred ninety-nine thousand nine hundred ninety-nine coins and nine hundred ninety-nine wen." This was recounted by his grandson, Zhou Chen.

    90

    张女夙慧
    　　顺天张万户德明，第八女小字度娥，资质秀爽，眼尾入鬓。丙午秋入小学。生七年矣，日诵数百言。比戊申二月，女史属词。《孝经》、《论语》、《孟子》、《易干传》至《下系》，诗《二南》、《曲礼》、《内则》、《少仪》、《中庸》、《大学》、《儒行》、《祭统》、《祭义》、《经解》、《冠婚》、诸篇，班氏《女戒》、郝氏《内则》、《内训》、《通丧记》六卷，皆成诵。日兼二诗，古律至十篇。学书，下笔即有成人之风。旦夕家居，见家人或不整肃，以礼责之。又所诵书多能通大义，时为讲说。其对属、才思敏捷，无小儿女子语：“睡思昏昏如醉思，闺心寂寂似禅心。桃李东风蝴蜨梦，关山明月杜鹃魂。”识者谓此诗不佳。后日果得病，又四日亡。甫九岁。郝伯常为诗吊之。

    Explanation

    90

    A Girl of Early Wisdom

    Zhang Wanheng of Shuntian, an official of high rank, had an eighth daughter named Du'e. She was endowed with exceptional grace and intelligence, her eyes so expressive that they seemed to reach her eyebrows. In the autumn of Bingwu (1366 AD), she entered primary school. By the age of seven, she could recite hundreds of words daily. By the second month of Wu Shen (1368 AD), she was composing poetry. She had memorized the Classic of Filial Piety, the Analects, the Mencius, parts of the Yijing (Book of Changes) from the Qian hexagram to the Xiaxi section, the Shijing (Book of Poetry) Ernan collection, the Quli, Neize, Shaoyi, Zhongyong, Daxue, Ruxing, Jisong, Jiyi, Jingjie, and Guangun chapters, as well as Ban Zhao's Ladies' Admonitions, Hao's Neize, Nixun, and Tongsangji (six volumes). She recited two poems daily, both ancient and regulated, up to ten in total. In calligraphy, her writing already showed the style of an adult. At home, she would rebuke family members if she saw them behaving improperly or not adhering to proper etiquette. She also understood the main ideas of the books she read and sometimes explained them. Her talent in composing poetry was quick and agile, and she wrote without the usual speech of a child: "Sleepy thoughts are like those of someone drunk, her quiet heart is like that of a monk. Peach and plum blossoms in the east wind, dreams of butterflies; the moon over mountains and passes, the soul of the cuckoo." Scholars considered this poem to be poor. Later, she indeed fell ill and died four days later. She was just nine years old. Hao Bochang wrote a poem to mourn her.

    91

    脱壳楸
    　　代州寿宁观，宋天圣中，一楸树老且枯矣。海蟾子过州卖不死药，三日不售。投药此树中。明年枯枿再茂，人目之为脱壳楸。白皞子西题诗云：“一粒丹砂妙有神，能教枯木再生春。仙翁用意真难晓，只度枯楸不度人。”泰和中，王嘉言子告过寿宁，戏道判白生云：“子西诗讥观中人，汝曹尚刻石耶？”白因掩覆此石。
    　　金宝牌
    　　宣政闲，方士能化泥为金，名“金宝牌”。长三寸半，阔二寸半，文曰：“永镇福地”。代州天庆、寿宁二处有之。天庆者今尚在。承平时人传玩，显是泥所成，指文宛然。

    Explanation

    91

    The Shedding-Shell Paulownia
    In the Shouning Temple of Dai Prefecture, during the Tian Sheng period of the Song Dynasty, an old and withered paulownia tree stood. A legendary alchemist, known as Hai Chanzi, passed through the town selling the elixir of immortality. For three days, he was unable to sell his wares. He then threw the elixir into the tree. The following year, the withered branches sprouted anew, and people called it the "Shedding-Shell Paulownia." Bai Hao, a poet from the Jin Dynasty, wrote a poem about it, which reads: "A single grain of cinnabar wondrously possesses divine power, capable of reviving a withered tree and bringing back spring. The immortal's intention is truly difficult to comprehend, for he only transforms the withered paulownia, not the people." During the Taihe period of the Jin Dynasty, Wang Jiayan passed by Shouning and playfully remarked to Bai Hao, "Your poem criticizes the people of the temple. Do you still have the stone inscription engraved?" Bai then covered the stone inscription.

    The Golden Treasure Plate
    During the Xuanzheng period, a Daoist adept could transform mud into gold, creating an object known as the "Golden Treasure Plate." It was three and a half inches long and two and a half inches wide, inscribed with the words: "Forever to protect the blessed land." Two such plates were found in the Tianqing and Shouning temples of Dai Prefecture. The one from Tianqing is still in existence today. During the peaceful times, people circulated and admired it, and it was evident that it was made of mud, with the inscriptions clearly visible.

    92

    揩牙方
    　　茯苓、石膏、龙骨各一两；寒水石二两半；白芷半两；细辛五钱；石燕子大者一枚、小者一对。末之，早晚揩牙。繁畤王文汉卿、得此方于麟抚折守，折守得于国初洛阳帅李成。折年逾九十，牙齿都不疏豁，亦无风虫。王文今亦九十，食肉尚能齿决之。信此方之神也。
    　　碑子鱼
    　　海中有鱼，尾足与龟无异，背上聚一壳，如碑石植立之状。潮退则出岸上曝壳，十百为群，闻人声则爬沙入海。海滨人谓之“碑子鱼”。或鱼或兽，未可必也。旧说蒲牢海兽，遇鲸跃则吼，其声如钟。今人铸钟作蒲牢形，刻撞钟槌为鲸，于二者有取焉。盖古人制器象物，如舟车、弧矢、杵臼之属，初不漫作，特后人不尽能知之耳然则碑表之制，将亦有所本耶？抑人见鱼形似，傅会为名也？
    　　神告胥莘公
    　　胥莘公尝梦泰山神告之曰：“敬我无福，慢我无殃；当行善道，家道久长。”每以此语人。事见家传。

    Explanation

    92

    Final Translation

    Tooth-Cleaning Formula

    The formula consists of: Poria, gypsum, dragon bone, each one liang; cold water stone, two liang and a half; angelica root, half a liang; fine cinnamon, five qian; large stone sturgeon, one piece; small stone sturgeon, a pair. Grind these into powder and use them to brush your teeth morning and evening. Fanzhou Wang Wen Hanqing obtained this formula from Lin Fu Zhe Shou, who in turn obtained it from the early period military leader Li Cheng of Luoyang. Zhe was over ninety years old, and his teeth were neither loose nor affected by wind or parasites. Wang Wen is also now ninety years old and can still chew meat with his teeth. This truly demonstrates the miraculous efficacy of the formula.

    Stone Tablet Fish

    In the sea, there is a fish whose tail and feet are no different from those of a turtle. On its back, it carries a shell that stands upright like a stone tablet. When the tide recedes, the fish come ashore to expose their shells, gathering in groups of ten or a hundred. Upon hearing human voices, they dig into the sand and return to the sea. People living by the sea call them "Stone Tablet Fish." Whether they are fish or a kind of beast, it is uncertain. According to ancient lore, the Pu Lao sea creature roars when a whale jumps, and its sound is like a bell. Today, people cast bells in the shape of Pu Lao and engrave the hammer that strikes the bell as a whale, drawing inspiration from both. It seems that ancient people made objects to resemble things, such as boats, chariots, bows, arrows, mortars, and pestles, not without reason. Perhaps the design of stone tablets also has its origins? Or did people give it this name because the fish resembles a stone tablet?

    Divine Message to Xuxin Gong

    Xuxin Gong once dreamed that the god of Mount Tai told him, "Respect me and you will not gain merit; disrespect me and you will not suffer harm. Follow the path of virtue, and your family will prosper for a long time." He often shared this message with others. This event is recorded in family records.

    93

    蛙化鼠
    　　燕南安州白羊淀，南北四十里，东西七十里，旧为水所占。近甲午岁，忽干涸，淀中所有蛙黾，悉化黑鼠，啮茭草根尽。土脉虚松，不待耕垦，投麦种即成就。其居民不胜举，听客户收获，但取课而已。此地山草根胶固，不受耕，其因鼠化得麦，亦异事也。淀有石刻云：“天荒地乱，莫离此淀；有水食鱼，无水食面。”是则前此亦尝得麦乎？张侯德明说。
    　　驴腹异物
    　　完州旧永平县磨户，其人家畜一驴，忽受病。比死，大叫七日夜不绝声。剖之，大腹内得物，非铁非石，形如栝楼而褊，色深褐，其坚若铁石。磨家不以为异，掷之麦囤中。日课麦皆取于此，而都不减秏。如是一年，乡人传以为神。官长石生者索去，亦置麦中，竟无神变。今在顺天张侯家，余亲见。
    　　暴雨落羊头
    　　贞祐二年，竖州杨云卿为崞县令。夏月暴雨过，南关外十余里落羊头一，大如车毂，角上竖，高三尺。以物怪申代州。州下军资库收，闻之朝。

    Explanation

    93

    Frogs Turning into Rats

    In the Baiyangdian region of Anzhou, in the southern part of Yan, which spans forty li north to south and seventy li east to west, it was once entirely covered by water. Recently, in the year of the Horse (1904), it suddenly dried up. All the frogs and toads in the pond transformed into black rats, which devoured all the roots of the reeds. The soil became loose and soft, requiring no plowing or cultivation; simply planting wheat seeds resulted in a successful harvest. The local residents could not manage the abundance, allowing tenants to harvest and only collecting a small tax. This area, with its dense and firmly rooted grass, was not suitable for farming, yet the transformation of rats into wheat was also an extraordinary event. There is an inscription on a stone that reads: "In times of chaos and disorder, do not leave this pond; if there is water, eat fish; if there is no water, eat noodles." Is it possible that wheat was also obtained before? According to Zhang Hou Deming.

    A Strange Object Found in a Donkey's Stomach

    In the old Yongping County of Wanzhou, a family that ground grain owned a donkey. Suddenly, the donkey fell ill. When it died, it cried out for seven days and nights without stopping. Upon dissection, a strange object was found in its large abdomen. It was neither iron nor stone, shaped like a gourd but narrower, with a deep brown color and as hard as iron or stone. The family did not find it unusual and threw it into the wheat storage. Daily rations of wheat were taken from there, and there was no reduction in the supply. This continued for a year, and the villagers began to believe it was a divine object. The official Shi Sheng took it away and placed it in the wheat storage, but there was no miraculous change. It is now in the home of Zhang Hou in Shuntian, and I have seen it myself.

    A Sheep's Head Falling from the Sky

    In the second year of the Zhenyou era (1214), Yang Yunqing of Shuzhou served as the magistrate of Gou County. During a summer storm, a sheep's head fell from the sky, about the size of a carriage wheel, with horns standing upright and three feet high. The magistrate reported this strange occurrence to the state of Dai. The military supply warehouse collected it, and the news reached the imperial court.

    94

    关中丁亥岁灾变
    　　正大四年丁亥，关中灾变二事：平凉西草场，天王塑像前后飐动，凡两昼夜不止，而泥塑衣纹都不剥落。知府徒单百家奴往拜之，拜至三，像即不动。知府去，动如故。临洮城中鼠昼夜作声，比屋皆然。一日近四更、鼠群出，中一大者如海鼠而白，引群鼠出南门。门下弓手排卧，鼠争道，踏人面而过。有不及出者，入东南白草原，乃不见。府至此六十里。刘善甫从弟润之说。
    　　珠子冰
    　　临洮城外洮水，冬月结小冰子如芡实，员洁如一耳奭阝之珠。洮城中富人收贮。盛夏以蜜浆调之，如真珠粉然。此水上下三百里，冬月望之，凝白无际，而著脚即陷。盖冰珠虽冱寒，亦不融结为一也。
    　　炭谷琼花
    　　鄠县西南十里曰“炭谷”。入谷五里，有琼花树。树大四人合抱，逢闰即花。初伏开，末伏乃尽。花白如玉，攒开如聚八仙状。中有玉蝴蜨一，高出花上，花落不著地，乘空而起。乱后为兵所斫云。

    Explanation

    94

    Disasters in Guanzhong during the Year Dinghai

    In the fourth year of the Zhengda era (丁亥), two disasters occurred in Guanzhong: In the western pasture of Pingliang, the statue of the Heavenly King swayed back and forth for two days and nights without stopping, yet the clay clothes did not peel off. The governor, Tu Dan Baiqian, went to pay respects to it. After bowing three times, the statue stopped moving. When the governor left, it resumed its motion as before. In Lin洮, mice made noise day and night, and every house was affected. One night near the fourth watch, a group of mice emerged, with one large white mouse leading the way, guiding the others out through the south gate. The archers lying in wait at the gate were trampled on as the mice rushed past. Some mice who did not manage to escape entered the southeast White Grass Plain and were no longer seen. The distance from the city to the White Grass Plain is sixty li. This account was provided by Liu Shanfu's younger brother, Runzhi.

    Pearl Ice

    Outside the walls of Lin洮, the洮 River formed small ice particles in winter, resembling water chestnuts, round and clean like pearls. Wealthy residents of the city collected and stored these ice particles. In the height of summer, they mixed them with honey syrup, creating a powder as smooth as real pearls. Along the river for three hundred li, the ice appeared to stretch endlessly when viewed from afar in winter, but if one stepped on it, it would sink. The ice pearls, though extremely cold, did not melt into a single mass.

    Jade Butterfly Flower in Carbon Valley

    Ten li southwest of Hu County is called "Carbon Valley." Five li into the valley, there is a tree of jade flowers. The tree is so large that four people must hold hands to encircle it. It blooms only during leap years. It begins to flower at the beginning of the first ten-day period of summer and continues until the end of the third ten-day period. The flowers are white as jade, clustering together in a shape resembling a gathering of eight immortals. Among the flowers, there is one jade butterfly that rises above them. When the flowers fall, they do not touch the ground but rise into the air. After the chaos, the tree was cut down by soldiers.

    95

    古钱
    　　东平人钱信中，按《钱谱》收古钱。凡得数十种，付之茶店刘六。刘本漕司胥吏家，素称好事。及多收古钱，聚两家所有，以锦囊贮之。如谱中不记年代，品最在前；刘亦有之。金错刀尤重厚，今世所见才二、三分耳。又有方寸匕，形制与错刀同，最多，推为众钱之冠。王莽大钱作燕尾状者，比今所有，其大四倍。文曰“端布当千”。背后有两字，有“丝布”、“泉布”、“货布”、“流布”，如是近十布。又有一铢、二铢、三铢至五铢。有内四出纹，是方孔、四角、金文通轮郭者。复有钱背四出文者，榆荚其文，一曰“五金”，一曰“五朱”。殆分“铢”字为二也。既有“涌金”，亦有“镂金”。开元钱有涌金月牙，复有镂金月牙，有孔方之上，有横涌金月牙一线通轮郭者，亦有孔方之下一线通轮郭者。此家所畜，不特古钱，书、画、琴暨古物，无不略具。士大夫日聚于此，杂客不豫也。东平破后，不知古物在否也。

    Explanation

    95

    Ancient Coins

    A man from Dongping named Qian Xinzong, following the Qianpu (Catalog of Coins), collected ancient coins. He gathered dozens of varieties and gave them to Liu Liu, who ran a tea shop. Liu was from a family associated with the Cao Si (a government office responsible for grain transportation) and was known for his interest in collecting. As he collected more ancient coins, he combined them with those from Qian Xinzong's collection, storing them in brocade pouches. If the Qianpu did not record the era of a coin, it was placed at the front of the collection; Liu also had some of these. The jin cuo dao (coins with gold inlay) were particularly heavy and thick, and today only a few are seen. There were also fang cun bi (small coins), which had the same design as the cuo dao and were the most numerous, considered the finest among all the coins. The large coins of Wang Mang, shaped like swallow tails, were four times the size of modern coins. They bore the inscription "Duan Bu Dang Qian" (meaning "Duan Bu is worth a thousand"). On the reverse side, there were two characters: "Si Bu," "Quan Bu," "Huo Bu," and "Liu Bu," among others, nearly ten in total. There were also coins weighing one zhu, two zhu, three zhu, up to five zhu. Some had nei si chu wen (a pattern on the inner edge), featuring square holes, four corners, and gold inscriptions. Others had qian bei si chu wen (a pattern on the back), resembling yu jia (a type of coin), one called "Wu Jin" and another "Wu Zhu." It seems the character "zhu" was divided into two. There were both "yong jin" (coins with gold waves) and "lou jin" (coins with gold carvings). The Kaiyuan Qian (coins from the Kaiyuan period of the Tang Dynasty) had yong jin yue ya (gold wave crescents) and lou jin yue ya (gold carving crescents), with some having a horizontal yong jin yue ya line running through the rim, and others having a vertical yong jin yue ya line running through the rim. This collection was not limited to ancient coins; it also included books, paintings, musical instruments, and other antiquities. Scholars and officials gathered there daily, while ordinary guests were excluded. After the fall of Dongping, it is unknown whether the ancient artifacts still exist.

    96

    神救甄帅军
    　　定州帅甄全，己卯岁为北兵所攻，求救恒山军。恒山逗遛不进，全逾城逃死，为北所获。恒山以全为叛，乞诛甄族之在军中者，又劫全入头山砦。砦上人半出运粮，外军猝至，守者不之备，杀虏甚众。运粮者不知被劫，坦然还砦。恒山军阴伺之，谋尽杀而后已。是夜，砦上大青鬼现，眼如杯，赤红、有光焰。军士惊怖散走，甄众乃得脱。

    Explanation

    96

    The Spirit Saves General Zhen's Army

    In the year of the Rabbit, the commander of Dingzhou, Zhen Quan, was attacked by the northern army. He sought help from the Hengshan army, but they delayed their advance. Zhen Quan jumped over the city wall to escape and ultimately died, being captured by the northern army. The Hengshan army regarded Zhen Quan as a traitor and requested the execution of Zhen's clan members who were in the army. They also kidnapped Zhen Quan and took him to the Toushan stronghold. Half of the people in the stronghold went out to transport grain, and the external army suddenly arrived. The defenders did not prepare for it, and many enemies were killed. Those transporting grain did not know they were being kidnapped and returned to the stronghold calmly. The Hengshan army secretly watched them, planning to kill all and then stop. That night, a large green ghost appeared on the stronghold, with eyes like cups, red, and with flames. The soldiers were frightened and scattered and ran away, and the Zhen group was able to escape.

    97

    猪善友
    　　洛西永宁一屠肆，豢猪数十头。一日，子弟问屠伯当宰何猪？屠伯攀圈指示，群猪惊扰，独一猪安然不动。屠伯指此猪云：“此猪食甚少，养饲已久，可宰之。”子弟入圈曳之，就缚，噤不出一声，及刺刃，喉无血，亦不死。子弟白之屠伯，屠伯自加刃，以手探之，此猪乃无心肺！屠伯大惊悟，以为神佛所化。掷刃于地，拜天地四方，誓愿改业。此猪既不死，安然入圈。尔后其家不复以糟糠饲之，目曰“猪善友。”闾里喧传，有自远来观者。无不惊叹。一邻家来请，“猪善友”斋，此猪如应诺。明旦，请者未至，猪已坐于此家之门。此家以斋食与之。如是三十三日，历旁近民家几遍。蹲坐一墓园中，不动，视之，已死矣。辛愿敬之为作传。

    Explanation

    97

    A Pig of Virtue
    In the west of Luoyang, in the village of Yongning, there was a butcher's shop where dozens of pigs were raised. One day, a young apprentice asked the head butcher which pig should be slaughtered. The butcher climbed into the pen to point out a pig, causing the other pigs to become startled and restless, except for one pig that remained calm and still. The butcher pointed to this pig and said, "This pig eats very little and has been raised for a long time; it can be slaughtered." The apprentice entered the pen and dragged the pig, tying it up. The pig remained silent and made no sound, and when the knife was stabbed into its throat, there was no blood, and it did not die. The apprentice reported this to the butcher, who then added another cut and touched the pig with his hand, discovering that the pig had no heart or lungs! The butcher was greatly surprised and realized that the pig must have been transformed by a deity. He threw the knife on the ground, bowed to heaven and earth and the four directions, and vowed to change his profession. The pig, not having died, calmly returned to the pen. Afterwards, the butcher no longer fed the pig coarse food and called it "Pig of Virtue." The news spread throughout the neighborhood, and people came from afar to see the pig. Everyone was amazed. A neighbor invited the pig to a fasting ritual called "Pig of Virtue Fast," and the pig seemed to agree. The next morning, before the invitee arrived, the pig was already sitting at the neighbor's door. The neighbor gave the pig fasting food. This continued for thirty-three days, during which the pig visited almost all the nearby households. Finally, the pig sat cross-legged in a cemetery, not moving. When they looked at it, it was already dead. Xin Yuan, in honor of the pig, wrote this biography.

    98

    宫婢玉真
    　　大定中，广宁士人李惟清元直者，与鬼妇故宋宫人玉真遇。玉真有《杨柳枝》词云：“已谢芳华更不留，几经秋；故宫台榭只荒邱，忍回头；塞外风霜家万里，望中愁；楚魂湘血恨悠悠，此生休。”一诗云：“皓齿明眸掩路尘，落花流水几经春。人间天上归无处，且作阳台梦里人。”又一诗云：“自怜华色镜中衰，轻弃前欢已自宜。不恨相逢情不尽，直须白鼠望归期。”李生后以庚子夏六月暴心痛死，辽东人为作传，以《东都行记》文多不载。

    Explanation

    98

    During the Da Ding period, a scholar from Guangning named Li Weiqing Yuanzhi met a ghostly woman who was formerly a palace maid of the Song dynasty, named Yu Zhen. Yu Zhen composed a poem in the style of the "Willow Branch," which reads: "The beautiful spring has already faded and will not return, after several autumns; the imperial palaces and pavilions now stand only as ruins, how can one bear to look back; the harsh winds and frost of the frontier are far from home, grief in sight; the lingering sorrow and resentment of Chu and Xiang, this life is over." Another poem she wrote says: "Her beautiful teeth and bright eyes are obscured by the dust of the road, flowers fall and water flows after several springs. There is no place to return to in either the human world or the heavenly realm, and she is but a dream of being with a loved one in the Baidi Palace." Yet another poem reads: "Self-pitying the fading beauty seen in the mirror, lightly abandoning past joys is already fitting. Not hating the fact that feelings are not fully expressed, one must wait for the return of the emperor like the white rat." After this encounter, Li Weiqing died suddenly from heart pain in the sixth month of the summer in the year Gengzi. The people of Liaodong wrote a biography for him, but many details are not included in the historical text Dongdu Xingji.

    99

    项王庙
    　　正隆南征，过乌江项羽庙，引妃嫔视之。因为说垓下事。顾谓众妃曰：“汝辈中亦有似虞姬者否？”此语传达民闲，有为之缩颈者。
    　　广宁寺钟声
    　　广宁寺有巨钟。一日，撞之不鸣，其声乃在城西南桥下。行人闻之，无不骇惧。有告寺僧，具饶钹就桥下迎，钟复鸣。宗室仲章说。
    　　石桥大火
    　　泰和八年冬，京师大悲阁前幡竿石桩缝间，连夕出火，四十余日乃止。明年，大火延烧万余家，阁亦被焚。卫王有旨，救虞世南所书“千手眼大悲阁”题榜。火气炽盛，人离百步外不敢近云。

    Explanation

    99

    1. 项王庙

    During Emperor Shizong's southern campaign, he passed by the Temple of Xiang Yu (Xiang Wang) at the U River. He led his consorts to see it and told them about the events of Gaixia. Turning to the consorts, he said, "Is there anyone among you who resembles Yu Ji?" This remark was passed on to the common people, and many of them recoiled in fear.

    2. 广宁寺钟声

    Guangning Temple had a large bell. One day, when the bell was rung, it did not make a sound. Instead, the sound came from the southwest bridge. All passersby who heard it were terrified. Someone told the temple monks, and they took a pair of cymbals and went to meet the bell at the bridge, and the bell rang again. This was recounted by Prince Zhong Zhang.

    3. 石桥大火

    In the winter of the 8th year of the Taihe era (1192), a large fire broke out in front of the Great Compassion Pavilion in the capital city. The fire started in the gap between the stone pillars supporting the flagpoles and lasted for more than 40 days. The following year, the fire spread to over 10,000 households, and the Great Compassion Pavilion was also destroyed. Emperor Shizong issued an edict to rescue the plaque inscribed by Yu Shiniang with the words "Thousand-Armed and Thousand-Eyed Great Compassion Pavilion." The fire was so intense that people could not approach within a hundred steps.

    100

    永安钱
    　　海陵天德初，卜宅于燕，建号中都，易析津府为大兴。始营造时，得古钱地中，文曰：“永安一千”。朝议以为瑞，乃取“长安”例地名，改东平中都县曰“汝阳”，河南永安曰“芝田”，中都永安坊曰“长宁”。然亦不知“永安一千”何代所用钱也。
    　　续夷坚志四
    　　临淄道院
    　　大定初，山东人杨善渊，买地临淄市南，立道院。掘地得古砖，上刻四十二字云：“大齐戌二年四月八日，南郭石羊巷杨道圆，施花砖笆三千口，在天齐观玉清宫殿上。永记杨押，砖匠杨本坚。”有为考按者：“此地盖北齐时天庆观，今巷东道北尚有石羊存焉。戌二年，高纬天统二年丙戌岁也。县前此无宫观，善渊拨土主之，偶与古观地合。善渊又与道圆同姓，亦异事也。

    100

    Translation

    Yong'an Money

    At the beginning of the Tiande era under Emperor Xizong of Jin, a residence was chosen in Yan, and the name Zhongdu was established. The name Xijin Prefecture was changed to Daxing. At the start of construction, an ancient coin was found in the ground, inscribed with "Yong'an One Thousand." The court considered this a sign of good omen and, taking the example of the name Chang'an, renamed Dongping Zhongdu County as Ruyang, Yong'an in Henan as Zhiti, and Yong'an Ward in Zhongdu as Changning. However, it is not known which dynasty used the "Yong'an One Thousand" coin.

    Xuyijian Zhi, Volume 4

    Daoist Temple in Linzi

    In the early Dading era, a man from Shandong named Yang Shan Yuan bought land south of Linzi City and established a Daoist temple. During the excavation, an ancient brick was discovered with forty-two characters inscribed on it: "The second year of Xiu in the Great Qi era, on the eighth day of the fourth month, Yang Dao Yuan from the Stone Sheep Lane in the southern suburb donated three thousand flower-patterned brick slabs for the Jade Clear Palace in the Tianqi Temple. Eternally recorded by Yang's seal, brickmaker Yang Benjian." Some scholars have noted that this place was the Tianqing Temple of the Northern Qi dynasty, and there are still stone sheep remaining to the east of the lane and north of the road. The second year of Xiu, which was the second year of Tian Tong in the reign of Emperor Gao Wei, the year of Bing Xu. There were no palaces or temples in the county before, and Yang Shan Yuan's land purchase coincidentally matched the site of the ancient temple. Yang Shan Yuan also shares the same surname as Yang Dao Yuan, which is also a remarkable coincidence.

    101

    盗谢王君和
    　　冯翊士人王献可，字君和，元礼中试京师。待榜次。一日晨起，市人携新鱼至，掷骰钱赌之。君和祝骰钱以卜前程，一掷得鱼。市人拊膺曰：“我家数口，绝食已二日；就一熟分人赊此鱼，望获数钱，以为举家之食。子乃一掷胜之。我家食禄尽矣！”君和恻然哀之，不取鱼，又以数钱遗之。市人谢而去。及下第西归，路经渑池，早发山谷间，猝为群盗所执，下路十数里。天明阅客行囊，一少年忽直前问君和：“非京师邸中乞我鱼不取者乎？今日乃相见于此！”再三慰谢，并同行皆免。同郡徐安上记其事云。

    101

    A Thief Thanks Wang Junhe

    Wang Xianke, a scholar from Fengyi, courtesy name Junhe, passed the imperial examination in the capital. He waited for the results. One morning, a market vendor brought fresh fish and gambled with dice. Wang Junhe prayed to the dice to predict his future and won the fish. The vendor, clapping his hands over his chest, said, "My family of several people has gone without food for two days; I cooked the fish, shared it, and borrowed money for it, hoping to earn a few coins to feed the whole family. You won it with one throw. Our livelihood is gone!" Wang Junhe felt pity for him, did not take the fish, and gave him some money. The vendor thanked him and left. When Wang Junhe failed the exam and returned west, passing through Mianchi early in the morning, he was suddenly captured by a group of bandits in the valley. They took him down the road for several miles. At dawn, they inspected the travelers' luggage. A young man suddenly stepped forward and asked Wang Junhe, "Are you not the one who begged for fish in the capital without taking it? Today we meet here!" He repeatedly consoled and thanked him, and all fellow travelers were spared. Xu Anshang from the same prefecture recorded this event.

    102

    广宁山龙斗
    　　甲辰乙巳岁，广宁夏五六月间，大阴晦，雷雨环作，声不断。夜望闾山上，白气直与海接。须臾雨下，终夜不息。平明水没村落，死者无限，大崖高数百尺，皆荡为平土。下漫石，石上有杵臼痕，不知何代为冈厓所覆压也。山颠龙斗处，留迹数十，所印泥鳞甲爪痕，有长五六十尺者，有长百余尺者。意群龙聚斗于此，土人遭此大变。
    　　宣靖播越兆
    　　宣和中，龙德宫花竹池沼间，散起庐舍，象村落田家所居。山庄、渔市、旗亭、茶店，无所不有。悉以宫婢主之。上皇策蹇其间，从以轻侠少年。所至，主人馆客留连笑谑，一与外间无异。将去，即以金钱遗之。播越之祸已见于此。《吕氏碣石录》。
    　　女真黄

    Explanation

    102

    Final Translation

    The Dragon Fight at Guanning Mountain

    In the years of the Wood Dragon and Wood Snake, during the late spring and early summer months of the sixth year of the Guangning era, there was great darkness and gloom. Thunderstorms raged continuously, and at night, looking up at Lü Mountain, one could see white vapor extending straight to the sea. Soon after, rain poured down all night without stopping. By dawn, the water had inundated the villages, and countless people perished. Great cliffs, hundreds of feet high, were flattened into level ground. The stones below were wet, and there were marks of pestles and mortars on them, indicating they had been used for grinding or pounding. It is unknown which dynasty covered and pressed them. At the mountain peak, where the dragons fought, dozens of traces were left, including imprints of mud, scales, claws, and marks. Some were fifty to sixty feet long, and some were over a hundred feet long. It is believed that a group of dragons gathered and fought here, and the local people suffered this great calamity.

    The Omen of the Exile and Chaos

    During the middle of the Xuanhe period, in the Dragon Virtue Palace, among the flower and bamboo ponds, scattered houses were built, resembling the dwellings of village farmers. There were mountain villages, fishing markets, flag pavilions, and tea shops, all present. All were managed by palace maids. The emperor rode slowly through the area, accompanied by young, daring youths. Wherever they went, the host entertained the guests with laughter and jest, no different from the outside world. As they were leaving, they gave money to the people. The disaster of exile and chaos had already been foretold here. (From Lü Shi Jieshi Lu)

    The Jurchen People

    The Jurchen people, a nomadic group, played a significant role in the historical events of the time.

    103

    文潞公元丰间镇洛水南，银李以千叶淡黄牡丹来献，且乞名。公名之曰“女真黄”。后人始知其谶。
    　　日本国冠服
    　　大定末，日本国贩硫黄沙木将往明越，为风漂至登州海岸。其人华冠缟服，上画鸡犬，将如挽郎。自言先世秦人，是徐市船载入海者。市死，为五蕃菩萨。国人至今为凶服，会裕陵上仙，取沙水供葬。
    　　焦燧业报
    　　开封焦燧，以廉能擢大兴推官。凡鞫囚有不伏者，即脑勘。及为河东路提刑官，忽病脑疽，不胜楚。自叹曰：“吾鞫狱用脑勘，人亦痛如是乎？”百方疗之，竟不起。
    　　
    　　孔孟之后
    　　宣圣五十三代孙名元措，字梦得，仕至大常卿，遥领泰宁军节度使。颜子五十三世孙名珍，辛丑年见之，六十余矣。长清有子贡之后木老，尝有官广威将军，人目之为“木威”。冉子之孙一农家，在长清之鹊巢，小儿子牛儿，子改曰阿鞬。孟氏亦有后，予未之见也。孔氏在曲阜者避圣讳，读“丘”曰“区”。此亦不可不知也。

    Explanation

    103

    During the Yuanfeng period, Wen Yuke was stationed south of the Luo River. Yin Li presented a peony with multiple petals and a pale yellow color, and requested a name for it. Wen Yuke named it "女真黄." Later people realized that the name was prophetic.

    Japanese National Costume

    At the end of the Dading period, Japanese traders carrying sulfur and sandalwood were heading to Mingzhou and Yue Prefecture when they were blown off course by the wind and landed on the coast of Dengzhou. They wore white mourning robes adorned with flowers and pictures of chickens and dogs, resembling funeral attendants. They claimed to be descendants of Qin people who were taken to sea by Xu Fu. Xu Fu died and became one of the five Buddhas of the Five Directions. The Japanese people continue to wear mourning attire and, during the imperial burial rites at the mausoleum of Emperor Shenzong, they brought sand and water to be used in the rituals.

    Jiao Sui's Karmic Retribution

    Jiao Sui of Kaifeng was promoted to the position of judicial official in the Daxing district due to his integrity and capability. Whenever he interrogated prisoners who did not confess, he would use the method of brain beating. Later, when he became a high-ranking judicial official in the Hedong Circuit, he suddenly fell ill with a severe head abscess and could not bear the pain. He lamented, "When I interrogated prisoners using brain beating, did they also suffer such pain?" Despite various treatments, he eventually died.

    Descendants of Confucius and Mencius

    The 53rd generation descendant of Confucius, named Yuan Cu and styled Mengde, served as a high-ranking official in charge of rituals and ceremonies and was appointed as the military governor of the Taining Circuit. The 53rd generation descendant of Yan Hui, named Zhen, was seen in the year of the Ox and was over sixty years old. In Changqing, there was an elderly man named Mujia, a descendant of Zigong, who once held the rank of Guangwei General and was nicknamed "Mujia." The grandson of Ran You, a farmer in the village of Quechao in Changqing, had a son named Niu'er, who was later called Ajian. The descendants of Mencius also exist, though I have not seen them. The descendants of Confucius in Qufu avoid the character "Qiu" out of respect for their ancestor and read it as "Qu." This is also something one should know.

    This translation aims to be both faithful to the original text and natural in English, incorporating the insights from the pre-drafting research.

    104

    张孝通冤报
    　　大定末，武清人赵士诠，商贩西京。每过白登，多宿张孝通家，其妻私焉。孝通知，阴图之。一日，乘士诠醉，与其子定国缢杀之，投尸野中。士诠久不归，子来白登访之。孝通先与店户白忠友有仇，私告赵子云：“汝父去向，白忠友宜知之。”赵子诉官，官系忠友，讯掠不胜苦楚，虽已诬服而狱终不决。明昌初，白妻诉朝。朝差贾公守谦往廉之。贾密访县人，人有言一异事云：张孝通及其子驱一骡往某处，憩于道旁树下。骡逐草而逸，定国怒鞭之。骡忽人语云：“你杀赵客，更来打我！”父子相顾失色。他日，孝通妇汲水饮骡，骡又语云：“你杀人，却冤白家。”孝通父子恐语泄，谋杀之以灭口，而县人无不知者。贾公以是归报朝廷。随差邢部员外孙某，驰驿至县，收孝通父子，一问即承。人知神理之不可诬也！贾公仕至右丞。

    Explanation

    104

    Zhang Xiaotong's Retribution

    At the end of the Dading era, Zhao Shiquan from Wuqing was a merchant in Xijing. Whenever he passed through Bai Deng, he often stayed at Zhang Xiaotong's house, where his wife had an affair with him. Zhang Xiaotong discovered this and planned to kill him secretly. One day, taking advantage of Zhao Shiquan's drunkenness, Zhang Xiaotong and his son Dingguo strangled and killed him, throwing the body into the wilderness. Zhao Shiquan did not return for a long time, so his son came to Bai Deng to look for him. Zhang Xiaotong had previously had a grudge against the store owner Bai Zhongyou and falsely told Zhao Shiquan's son, "Your father's whereabouts, Bai Zhongyou should know." Zhao Shiquan's son reported to the authorities, who arrested Bai Zhongyou. Under torture, Bai Zhongyou confessed falsely, but the case remained unresolved. In the early Mingchang era, Bai Zhongyou's wife appealed to the court. The court dispatched Mr. Jia Gong Shouqian to investigate the matter. Jia Gong Shouqian secretly interviewed the county residents, and one person mentioned an unusual incident: Zhang Xiaotong and his son were driving a donkey to a certain place, resting under a tree by the roadside. The donkey ran off after some grass, and Dingguo angrily whipped it. The donkey suddenly spoke human words: "You killed Zhao Shiquan, and now you come to beat me!" The father and son looked at each other in shock. Another day, Zhang Xiaotong's wife fetched water to drink the donkey, and the donkey spoke again: "You killed someone, but you wronged Bai Zhongyou's family." Fearing that the truth would be revealed, Zhang Xiaotong and his son plotted to kill the donkey to silence it. The entire county knew about this. Jia Gong Shouqian reported this back to the court. The court then dispatched an official named Sun from the Ministry of Punishment to ride on a fast horse to the county, where he arrested Zhang Xiaotong and his son. Upon questioning, they confessed everything. People understood that the principle of divine retribution cannot be defied! Jia Gong Shouqian rose to the position of Right Chancellor.

    105

    魏相梦鱼
    　　参知政事魏子平，嗜食鱼。厨人养鱼百余头，以给常膳。忽梦群鱼集其身，挥斥不去；复梦为鱼所鲠，痛不能出。闷乱久之乃寤。自是不食鱼。
    　　相字
    　　宋末，有相字知休咎者。上皇书一“朝”字，令人试之。相者云：“十月十日天子生，绍兴南渡，将驻于杭。”书一“杭”字问之，相者云：“兀术将至，当避其锋。”太师梁王小字兀术，果拥兵而南。其验如此！尝与同舍生孟津李蔚庆之论及此。予谓：“古无相字法，殆是挟以他术耶？”李曰：‘不然，此龟卜之余意耳！’
    　　梦灵丸

    Explanation

    105

    Wei Xiang Dreams of Fish

    Wei Zhiping, a high-ranking official known as a vice-premier, loved to eat fish. His cook raised over a hundred fish to provide for his regular meals. One day, he suddenly dreamed that a group of fish gathered around him, persistently and unyieldingly. In another dream, he was choked by a fish, feeling pain and unable to breathe. He felt confused and disoriented for a long time until he woke up. From then on, he no longer ate fish.

    Xiang Divines

    At the end of the Song Dynasty, there was a person named Xiang who could predict the future. The emperor wrote the character "朝" and had someone test it. Xiang interpreted it as: "On the tenth day of the tenth month, the emperor will be born; the Southern Migration of the Song Dynasty will settle in Hangzhou." The emperor then wrote the character "杭" and asked about it. Xiang said: "Wu Zhu will come, and you should avoid his sharpness." The Grand Tutor and Prince of Liang, with the nickname Wu Zhu, indeed led troops southward. Someone asked: "There was no method of divination by characters in ancient times, perhaps he used other methods?" Another person replied: "Not so, this is just the residual meaning of turtle divination."

    Dream of the Magic Pill
