    106

    京师法云寺僧律师，失明数年。梦中有人授一方，治内外障，但瞳神水在者，皆可疗。艾二两；蔓菁子。枸杞、蒺藜、甘菊、荆芥穗各一两；当归、地黄、川芎、赤芍药、防风各一两半；十一味末之。水面糊凡，桐子大。空腹、食前，温水下三二十几。僧服之，目复明。因目曰“梦灵丸。”
    　　吕氏所记古印章
    　　党承旨有周亚夫铜印。束鹿柴揖调历城簿，有彭宣私印。临淄农郑氏耕地，得方寸铜印，钮作九猨猴，细小如豆；谛视之，形状俱备。郑先未有子，自是产九男。因宝藏此印。
    　　古鼎
    　　燕都庙学，有夹铜鼎焉。高二尺，受数斛。篆有“离明神鼎养火”六字。后归裕陵。竟不晓古人作何用也。郭太傅舜俞说：“博平路氏一鼎，无款识，无文章，而黄金丹碧，绚烂溢目，受五升许，三足而一稍大，路氏用之煮茶。以少火燎其大足，则水随沸。大定中，铜禁行，不敢私藏，摧大足折，送之官。足中虚，折处，铜楂作火焰上腾之状。

    Explanation

    106

    A Monk Named Lawyer from Fayun Temple in the Capital, Blind for Several Years, Regained His Sight After Taking a Prescription Given to Him in a Dream, Which He Later Named "Dream Spirit Pill"

    A monk named Lawyer from Fayun Temple in the capital had been blind for several years. In a dream, he was given a prescription to treat both internal and external eye conditions, stating that those with intact eye fluids could be cured. The prescription included two liang of mugwort, radish seeds, wolfberry, tribulus, chrysanthemum, schizonepeta, angelica, rehmannia, ligusticum, red peony, and siler, all ground into powder. The pills were made with water paste, the size of tujiao, and should be taken on an empty stomach or before meals, with warm water, three to twenty pills at a time. The monk took the pills and regained his sight. Because of this, the pill was named "Dream Spirit Pill."

    Records of Ancient Seals by the Lu Family

    Party Cai, a high-ranking official, had a copper seal of Zhou Yafu. Cai, who served as a clerk in Licheng, had a private seal of Peng Xuan. Zheng, a farmer from Linzi, found a square-inch copper seal while plowing his field. The seal's handle was shaped like nine tiny monkeys, each as small as a bean. Upon closer inspection, the shapes were all clearly defined. Zheng had no children before this, but after finding the seal, he went on to have nine sons. He treasured the seal as a precious treasure.

    Ancient Tripod

    At the temple school in Yan capital, there was a copper tripod. It was two chi high and could hold several dou. The inscription on the tripod read "Limi Shendong Yanghuo" (离明神鼎养火). It was later sent to Yuling tomb. No one knew what the ancients used it for. Guo, the Grand Tutor and Shunyu, said: "The Lu family from Boping had a tripod without any inscriptions or decorations, but it was adorned with gold, cinnabar, and lapis lazuli, shimmering and dazzling. It could hold about five dou and had three legs, one of which was slightly larger. The Lu family used it to boil tea. When they lit a small fire to warm the larger leg, the water would immediately boil. During the Dading period, when there was a ban on copper, they dared not keep it privately and had to break the larger leg and send it to the authorities. Inside the broken leg, the copper fragments resembled flames rising upward."

    107

    ”天壤间神物奇宝，成坏俱有数，特见毁于庸人之手，为可惜耳！蔡内翰正夫《古器类论》记二鼎云：“其一明昌三年二月、蓝田玉山乡农民李兴穿地得之，高二尺，两耳，有字一十行，文曰：“王四月初吉丁亥。”以长历考之，鲁庄公十二年四月丁亥，即周安厘王初立之岁，未改元，故不称年而仅以月数焉，又有一百二字，必周侯伯所作之器也。其一太原三交西南，大定九年汾水坏东岸古墓，有鼎及钟磬之属；鼎小者五寸许，大几三尺，中作黄金色。所实牛羹尚可辨。钟磬小者不及二尺，凡十六等，盖音律之次也。虽无款识，皆周物也。”

    Explanation

    107

    Divine objects and rare treasures in the world, both their creation and destruction are governed by fate, yet they are especially destroyed by the hands of ordinary people, which is indeed a pity! In his work The Categories of Ancient Objects, Cai Zhengfu, the Inner Historian, records two bronze tripods: "One was discovered in February of the third year of Mingchang by a farmer named Li Xing from Yushan Village in Lantian. It stands two feet tall, has two ears, and bears ten lines of inscriptions, reading: 'On the first day of the fourth month, Dinghai.' According to the long calendar, this corresponds to the 21st day of the fourth month of the 12th year of Duke Zhuang of Lu, which is also the year when King Anli of Zhou first ascended the throne. He had not yet changed the era name, so only the month is mentioned. Additionally, there are one hundred and two characters, which must have been made by a Zhou feudal lord. The other was found in the ninth year of Dading in the southwest of Sanjiao in Taiyuan, where the Fen River destroyed the eastern bank of an ancient tomb, revealing a tripod along with bells and chimes. The smaller tripods are about five inches tall, while the larger ones are nearly three feet tall, with interiors of a golden hue. The beef stew inside is still discernible. The smaller bells and chimes are less than two feet in length, totaling sixteen ranks, which are the sequences of musical tones. Although there are no inscriptions, they are all Zhou artifacts."

    108

    西阴井移
    　　戊申正月，武城之东有村落名西阴，民家一井移四五步，而井桩如故也。又数日，一道士过此村，形服与常人异。见农具中二地碾石咄咤曰：“业畜！乃在此耶？”并挟之而去。村民惧凶祸将及，弃家远徙。后亦无他。南宫士人董德卿亲见之。”
    　　海岛妇
    　　王内翰元仲《集录》：“近年海边猎人，航海求鹘。至一岛，其人穴居野处，与诸夷特异，言语绝不相通。射之中，则扪血而笑。猎者见男子则杀之，载妇人还。将及岸，悉自沉于水。他日再往，船人人执一妇，始得至其家。妇至此不复食，有逾旬日者。一旦，皆自经于东冈大树上。”元仲，黄华之父也。

    Explanation

    108

    Translation:

    The Moving Well of Xiyin
    In the first month of the year Wushen, there was a village named Xiyin to the east of Wucheng. A well in a household moved several steps, yet the well structure remained unchanged. A few days later, a Taoist priest passed through the village, dressed differently from ordinary people. Upon seeing two millstones among farming tools, he exclaimed sharply, "Stubborn beast! Are you here?" He took the millstones away. The villagers, fearing impending misfortune, abandoned their homes and moved far away. Later, there were no further incidents. Scholar Dong Deqing from Nan Gong witnessed this firsthand.

    Island Women
    From the collection of Wang Yuansheng, the Inner Historian: "Recently, hunters by the sea sailed to an island to hunt hawks. Upon arriving at the island, the people lived in caves and wild places, distinct from other tribes, and their language was completely incomprehensible. When they were shot and hit, they touched the blood and laughed. The hunters killed the men they saw and took the women back. As they approached the shore, all the women drowned themselves in the water. Another day, when they returned, each person on the boat held a woman, and they finally reached their homes. The women stopped eating, some for more than ten days. One day, all of them hanged themselves on a large tree on the eastern hill." Wang Yuansheng is the father of Huang Hua.

    109

    鸡泽神变
    　　鸡泽农民五人，同采樵出门。望西风势甚恶，迟回不欲往，又为一叟所难。四人者还家，一人往采樵次。大风从西北来，震荡天日。此人走避不及，伏于沟中。为一人捽起同行。行时，此人踏风而行，见同行皆神鬼。迤逦过一城，神人曰：“此朝城也。”又东行。路旁一长髯人拜、劝酒；神人共入庙中，留此人庙门下。少之，呼入行酒。见神人各长丈余，有鬼形者、人形者，衣皆锦绣，香气袭人。此人从中坐劝酒，中坐者不语，以右手拇指指令从次坐者劝。劝毕，复出庙门下。须臾饮散，神人出，大风随起。置此人不复问。此人伺风定，出问人，知此地为东平界，庙即岳祠也。行丐数日，乃至家，犹恍惚如心恙云。智仲可说

    Explanation

    109

    Translation

    The Divine Transformation at Jize

    Five farmers from Jize went out together to gather firewood. Seeing that the west wind was very fierce, they hesitated and did not want to go, and were also challenged by an old man. Four of them returned home, while one continued to gather firewood. A strong wind came from the northwest, shaking the sky and earth. This person could not avoid it and hid in a ditch. He was grabbed by one person and forced to go with them. While walking, this person walked on the wind, seeing that those accompanying him were all spirits and ghosts. They slowly passed through a city, and a divine being said, "This is the city of Chao." They then continued eastward. On the side of the road, a man with a long beard bowed and offered wine; the divine beings all entered a temple, leaving this person at the temple gate. After a short while, they called him in to serve wine. He saw that the divine beings were each over ten feet tall, some with ghostly forms and others with human forms, all dressed in brocade and silk, their fragrance permeating the air. This person sat in the central seat and served wine, but the person in the central seat did not speak and pointed with his right thumb to the person next to him to serve. After serving, he returned to the temple gate. Soon, the drinking session ended, and the divine beings left, with a strong wind following. They left this person without further questioning. This person waited for the wind to settle, then went out to ask people and learned that this place was in the territory of Dongping, and the temple was the Yue Temple. After wandering and begging for several days, he finally returned home, still feeling dazed and as if his heart was sick. This story is told by Zhi Zhong.

    110

    临晋异瓜
    　　临晋上排乔英家，业农，种瓜三二顷。英种出西瓜一窠，广亩二分，结实一千二三百颗。他日耕地，瓜根如大椽。辛亥年，定襄士人樊顺之亲见。
    　　舜麦
    　　河东县舜砦出麦，颗粒如常麦而无缝，又色稍白，每斗得面十三斤。此地二顷余，农民数家主之。喻如今岁东家舜麦成，至明岁西家成熟，无定处，然终不出二顷之外也。定襄周梦卿说。
    　　平阳贡院鹤
    　　大安初，高子约、耿君嗣、阎子秀、王正之考试平阳，举子万人。主司有梦绯衣人来谢谒者。明旦试题下以语同官。俄，群鹤旋舞《至公楼》上，良久不去。主司命胥吏揭榜大书示众云：“今场状元，出自河东。”当举府题《圣人有金城》，解魁宋可封、泽州；省《俭德化民家给之本》，省魁孙当时；御题《获承休德不遑康宁》，状元王纲，平阳。三元者果皆河东云。

    Explanation

    110

    A Strange Melon in Linjin
    　　In the village of Qiao Ying, located in Linjin, there was a farmer who grew melons on several acres of land. One day, a large melon grew that was two fen wide and produced 1,200 to 1,300 seeds. When the farmer plowed the field later, he found the melon's root to be as large as a large beam. In the year 1551, a scholar from Dingxiang named Fan Shunzhi personally witnessed this event.

    Shun's Wheat
    　　In Shun's village in Hedong County, a type of wheat grew that had grains similar to regular wheat but without seams, and it was slightly whiter. Each dou of this wheat yielded 13 jin of flour. The area where this wheat grew was about 2 qing, and it was managed by several farming families. It was said that this year, the wheat would grow in the east, and next year, it would grow in the west, with no fixed location, but it would never exceed 2 qing in total. This was reported by Zhou Mengqing from Dingxiang.

    White Cranes at the Examination Hall in Pingyang
    　　In the early years of the Da'an era (1209-1213 CE), during the examinations in Pingyang, four examiners—Gao Ziyue, Geng Junsi, Yan Zixiu, and Wang Zhengzhi—were present, with ten thousand candidates taking the exam. The chief examiner had a dream where a man in red robes came to thank him. The next day, the chief examiner shared the exam questions with his colleagues. Soon after, a group of white cranes danced around the "Zhi Gong Building" and stayed for a long time. The chief examiner then ordered the clerks to post a notice publicly, which read: "The top candidate in this examination comes from Hedong." The questions in the examination included: "The Sage has a golden city," "Frugality transforms the people and provides for the family," and "Receiving the blessings of peace and prosperity." The top candidates were Song Ke, from Zhezhou; Sun Dang, from the provincial examination; and Wang Gang, from the imperial examination, all from Pingyang. Indeed, all three top candidates came from Hedong.

    111

    史学优登科岁月
    　　河中李钦叔初生，其父之才作汤饼局。有相者为延安史学优言：“君后当擢第，但当出此儿门下，为太晚耳！”学优雅以才名自负，不以相者之言为然。其后钦叔二十三，省元赐第，中廷试，策宏词科，除应奉翰林文字。两豫主贡。学优竟出其门云。
    　　日中见异物
    　　崇庆元年冬十月，北京进士赵天瑞、张仲和辈十五人，赴试回，晓行道中，日中见三物：一四足兽在前，一蛇继之，二物行甚速；次一鸟跳跃稍缓。少顷，无所见。是后兵动，中原丧乱。兰仲大说。

    Explanation

    111

    The Years of Excelling in History Studies and Passing the Imperial Examinations

    Li Qinsu, from the Hezhong region, was born, and his father, a talented man, hosted a banquet where soup dumplings were served. A fortune-teller told Shi Xueyou from Yan'an, "You will pass with distinction, but it will be too late to come under this child's tutelage!" Shi Xueyou, proud of his talent and reputation, did not believe the fortune-teller's words. Later, Li Qinsu, at the age of twenty-three, was awarded first place in the provincial examination, passed the imperial examination, and was appointed as a compiler in the Hanlin Academy. He was selected twice to represent the region in the imperial examinations. Shi Xueyou eventually became his teacher, as predicted.

    Seeing Strange Objects at Noon

    In the tenth month of the first year of the Chongqing era, fifteen successful candidates from Beijing, including Zhao Tianrui and Zhang Zhonghe, returned from taking the imperial examinations. As they traveled early in the morning, they saw three strange objects at noon: one was a four-legged beast in front, followed by a snake, both moving very quickly. Then came a bird that jumped more slowly. Soon, they saw nothing. After this, there was military activity, and the Central Plains fell into chaos. Lan Zhong was very pleased.

    112

    镇城地陷
    　　镇城欲陷日，州长、佐史率妓乐迎官出城。坐待驿亭次，见一妇被发跣足，喘汗入城，问之，云其姑卒病，买药欲救之。良久，亭中人闻空际有相问答者云：“出城未？”答者言：“未”。吏卒闻之大骇怪，不知所谓。少之，妇得药而出，城随陷，城中无一人免者。此妇殆以孝感脱此祸欤？中京史监时亦在亭中，亲见其妇。惜不问此妇姓氏耳。
    　　王子明获盗
    　　副枢刚中王公晦，字子明，泽州人。初任长葛簿。一日行水边，忽见回风逐马行，或前或后，数里不去。子明疑其有异，缓辔从之。回风入水复出者数四。子明召旁近居民，杂驺卒入水索之，得一尸，是近日被害者。检视衣著，于所佩小革囊中得买布单目及木印一。子明默藏之不以语人。既入县，即召布行赍布来官，欲买之，积布盈庭。子明一一辨视，果有布是木印所记者。因甲乙推之，盗寻获。一县称为神明。事见闲闲公所撰《墓志》。

    Explanation

    112

    Translation

    The Collapse of the City

    On the day when the city was about to collapse, the governor and his aides led musicians and entertainers out of the city to greet the official. They sat and waited at the post station, where they saw a woman with unbound hair and barefoot, breathing heavily and sweating as she entered the city. They asked her, and she said that her grandmother had suddenly fallen ill, and she had bought medicine to save her. After a while, people in the post station heard voices in the air asking, "Have you left the city yet?" The answer was, "Not yet." The officials and soldiers were greatly startled and puzzled, not knowing what this meant. After a while, the woman returned with the medicine, and the city collapsed, with no one in the city surviving. This woman must have been saved from this disaster due to her filial piety. The official from Zhongjing was also in the post station and personally saw the woman. It is a pity that he did not ask the woman's name.

    Wang Ziming Catches a Thief

    Wang Gong, the Deputy Chancellor and Minister of Justice, whose courtesy name was Ziming, was from Zhe Prefecture. He was initially appointed as the magistrate of Changge County. One day, while walking by the water, he suddenly saw a whirlwind following his horse, sometimes in front and sometimes behind, for several miles. Ziming suspected that there was something unusual and slowed down his horse to follow it. The whirlwind entered the water and came out several times. Ziming called nearby residents and soldiers to search the water, and they found a corpse, which was a recent victim. Upon examining the clothing, they found a small leather bag with a single eye and a wooden seal. Ziming kept it hidden and did not tell anyone. After entering the county, he immediately summoned the cloth merchant to bring the cloth to the official. The courtyard was filled with cloth, and Ziming examined each piece carefully. Indeed, there was a piece of cloth marked with the wooden seal. He then questioned the people and eventually caught the thief. The entire county praised him as a divine figure. The story is recorded in the epitaph written by Xianxian Gong.

    113

    泗州题壁词
    　　兴定末，四都尉南征。军士掠淮上良家女北归。有题《木兰花》词逆旅间云：“淮山隐隐，千里云峰千里恨；淮水悠悠，万顷烟波万顷愁；山长水远，遮断行人东望眼；恨旧愁新，有泪无言对晚春。”
    　　贺端中见鬼
    　　吾州进士贺端中，大定中，宣圣庙齐宿。镫下见一大青鬼，发上指，目光如炬，口出火焰。贺以被蒙头，伏床下。日高，诸生至，乃敢出，战悚尚未定也。起视，水瓮皆干，砚池亦然，溺器亦空。人知其为渴鬼云。端中出孙国镇之门，有赋声。此举登科。
    　　介虫之变
    　　东平薛价，阜昌初进士。尝令鱼台，嗜食糟蠏。凡造蠏，厨人生揭蠏脐，纳椒一粒，盐一捻，复以绳十字束之，填入糟瓮，上以盆合之。旋取食。薛一日梦昨所获强寇，劫狱而去，夜半惊寤，索烛召吏，将问之。烛至，乃见糟蠏蹒跚满前，不知何从出也。薛自此不食蠏。外曾孙东平贾显之说。

    Explanation

    113

    Translation

    Poem on the Wall in Sizhou

    At the end of the Xingding era, four military commanders were sent south on a campaign. Soldiers from the Huai River region captured virtuous women and brought them north. One of these women wrote a poem titled "Woodland Orchid" on a wall in an inn, which read:

    "Mountains of the Huai are faint, a thousand miles of cloud peaks and a thousand miles of sorrow; the Huai River flows gently, ten thousand acres of mist and waves, ten thousand acres of grief. The mountains are long and the waters are far, blocking the view of travelers looking east. Old and new sorrows, tears but no words in late spring."

    Ge Duanzhong Sees a Ghost

    My state's Jinshi Ge Duanzhong, during the Dading era, stayed overnight in the Confucius Temple. Under the lamp, he saw a large green ghost with hair standing on end, eyes like torches, and a mouth emitting flames. Ge covered his head with a quilt and lay under the bed. As the day grew late, the students arrived, and he dared to come out, still trembling with fear. Upon rising, he saw that all the water jars were dry, the inkstone pool was also empty, and the urinal was empty as well. People knew it was a thirsty ghost. Ge Duanzhong, who came from the school of Sun Guozhen, had a reputation for his poetry. This incident contributed to his success in the imperial examinations.

    The Transformation of Interstitial Creatures

    Xue Jia from Dongping, a new Jinshi from the Fuchang era, once served as magistrate in Yutai. He loved eating fermented crabs. Whenever he prepared crabs, the cook would open the crab's belly, put in a grain of pepper and a pinch of salt, tie it up with a cross-shaped string, and fill it into the fermented crab jar, covering it with a bowl. He would then eat it. One day, Xue Jia dreamed that the strong bandits he had captured the previous day had broken out of prison and fled. In the middle of the night, he woke up in a panic, called for a candle, and summoned the officials to ask about it. When the candle was lit, he saw the fermented crabs crawling all around him, not knowing where they had come from. From then on, he no longer ate crabs. This story was told by his great-grandson Jia Xianzhi from Dongping.

    114

    天庆殿柱
    　　太原士人刘进之，客卫州。所居近河，三夜闻哭声，访之邻里，云：“旁近无哭者，当是鬼哭欤？”进之忽忆临河有汴宫天庆殿所撤大木，将作筏下河，候涨落乃行，云是彰德帅欲用修药棚者。古时石言于晋意此木哭乎？明日筏下河，哭声乃绝。曹魏青龙中，取汉武帝承露金人，欲置之许都。临发，金人潸然出涕。李长吉有《金人辞汉歌》。
    　　神觜涡水
    　　西京大同府之南神觜涡，泊水广百余亩，深三丈。居人取鱼其中。十三年前，一夕大雷雨，水忽飞去，入浑源东南山娘子村中，复为大陂。凡神觜水所经，遗鱼不绝。
    　　空中人语
    　　张显卿，名德，辽州人。明昌二年经童，贞祐四年进士。自说大安庚午岁，曾与客饮，向日酹酒，语执壶者云：“不必满，荐诚而已！”忽闻空中有人言：“安知空中无海量者乎？”众客骇，立酹数满杯。

    Explanation

    114

    Final Translation

    Pillars of the Tianqing Hall

    A scholar from Taiyuan named Liu Jinzhi was residing in Weizhou. His residence was near the river, and for three consecutive nights, he heard crying sounds. He inquired among his neighbors, who said, "There is no one nearby crying; it must be a ghost." Suddenly, Liu recalled that there were large wooden beams from the Bian Palace's Tianqing Hall that had been dismantled and were being used to make a raft to be lowered into the river, waiting for the water level to rise before proceeding. It was said that these beams were intended for repairs at a medicine pavilion in Zhangde. Could these beams be crying, just as stones spoke in the State of Jin in ancient times? The next day, when the raft was lowered into the river, the crying sounds ceased.

    In the year of the Azure Dragon (Alcyoneus) during the reign of Cao Wei, the golden man who collected dew for Emperor Wu of Han was taken to Xudu. Just before it was to be moved, the golden man shed tears. Li Changji wrote a poem titled "The Golden Man's Farewell to Han."

    Water of the Divine Bird's Mouth

    South of the Western Capital's Datong Prefecture lies the Divine Bird's Mouth, a body of water that covers more than a hundred acres and is three zhang deep. People living nearby fished there. Thirteen years ago, during a night of thunder and heavy rain, the water suddenly flew away, entering the southeast mountains of Hunyuan, specifically the village of Niangzi. It formed a large pond there. Everywhere the water of the Divine Bird's Mouth flows, fish are left behind.

    Voices in the Air

    Zhang Xianqing, also known as Zhang De, was from Liaozhou. In the second year of the Mingchang era, he passed the preliminary examination for the imperial examinations, and in the fourth year of the Zhenyou era, he became a jinshi (imperial scholar). He recounted that in the year of the Horse (Gengwu) during the Duanan era, he once drank with guests, pouring wine toward the sun and telling the person holding the wine vessel, "It is not necessary to fill it; it is enough to offer sincerity!" Suddenly, someone spoke from the air, saying, "How can we know there are not vast quantities in the air?" The guests were startled and immediately poured several full cups of wine.

    115

    天裂
    　　元光壬午六月二十四日，崔振之时起任咸宁令，聚县民豁口村，计会科敛。此地在灞桥六七里。日在辰巳间。忽见天裂，从东南至西北，青气分折数丈其中有光，盘曲如电，令人震荡，不敢仰视。吏民数百人皆见。振之说。
    　　高白松
    　　徐伟官京兆，梦二老人，白首而长身，身穿绿袍，谓伟言：“某他日有斧斤之阸，幸为保全之！”伟不知所以，然梦异，不忘也。及移守泰安，会岳祠灾，诏复修之，境内大木皆听采取。东六十里莱芜之高白村，有古松，干柯茂盛，阴蔽二亩，乡社相传为数百年物。亦在采斫之数。乡人父老哀祷于伟。伟因悟前梦，力为营护，竟免斩伐。是夜梦有来谢者。土人立祠其侧，辛生者为之记。文士张圣予赋诗云：“蟠根蹙足怪虬藏，平顶摩云翠盖张。不怕雪霜侵玉瘦，却愁雷雨化龙骧。异材讵肯资梁栋？灵梦还能避斧斨。万古天风吹不老，岱宗山色共苍苍。”

    Explanation

    115

    Heavenly Split

    On the twenty-fourth day of the sixth month in the Renwu year of Yuangang, Cui Zhen was appointed as the magistrate of Xianning. He gathered the county's people from Huokou Village to discuss and assess taxes. This location was about six or seven li from Bashi Bridge. The sun was between the hours of Chen and Si when suddenly the sky split, stretching from southeast to northwest. A greenish light divided and extended several zhang, coiling like lightning, causing people to tremble and dare not look up. Hundreds of officials and civilians witnessed this phenomenon. Cui Zhen recounted the event.

    High White Pine

    Xu Wei, who served as an official in Jingzhao, dreamt of two elderly men with white hair and tall stature, dressed in green robes. They told him, "One day, I will face the danger of an axe, please help me preserve my life!" Xu Wei did not understand the meaning but remembered the strange dream. Later, when he was transferred to govern Taian, there was a fire at the Temple of Mount Tai, and the emperor ordered its restoration. All major trees within the territory were allowed to be cut down. In Gaobai Village, sixty li east of Laiwu, there was an ancient pine tree with lush branches and foliage, shading two mu of land. It was said by the local community to be several hundred years old. It was also among the trees to be cut. The elders of the village mournfully prayed to Xu Wei. Xu Wei then recalled his dream and made great efforts to protect the tree, saving it from being cut. That night, he dreamt that someone came to thank him. The locals built a shrine beside the tree, and Xin Sheng wrote a record of the event. The scholar Zhang Shengyu composed a poem: "Coiling roots and pressing feet hide a strange qiu, a flat top reaching the clouds with a green canopy spread. Not afraid of snow and frost invading jade's thinness, but worried about thunder and rain transforming into a dragon's gallop. Unusual material would not willingly serve as beams and pillars? A divine dream can still avoid the axe and chisel. Through millennia, the wind of heaven blows it not old, the mountain colors of Dai Zong together are evergreen."

    116

    炭中二仙
    　　皋州人贾合春，前鄜畴丞。兴定二年丁丑十月，以戍役在渑池。此地出炭，炭穴显露，随取而足。用者积絫成堆，下以薪爇之，烈焰炽然。一日，贾与戍卒围火坐，忽一炭块爆出。块破，中有二白玉仙人，各长二寸有半，眉目口耳形体皆具，顶乌巾，系如皂勒帛状，双带下垂，雕刻所不及。贾甚珍秘。兵乱中失所在。
    　　护兰童子
    　　孟州路宣叔，未二十而娶。未几妻亡，追悼不已，郁不自聊。夜梦妻如平生，说身后为护兰童子住翡翠庵。作诗记之云：“翡翠庵前花草香，护兰童子淡云妆。夙缘还却三生债，不道未归人断肠。”“未归人”，用死者为归人，生者为行人之义。

    Explanation

    116

    Two Immortals in the Coal

    Jia Heshun, a native of Gaozhou and formerly a local official in Fuchou, was stationed in Mianchi during the month of October in the year Dingchou of Xingding's second year (1218 AD) for military service. This place was known for its coal, with coal pits exposed and coal available in abundance. Those who used it would pile it up and burn it with firewood, producing a blazing, intense flame. One day, Jia and the soldiers gathered around the fire, and suddenly a piece of coal burst open. Inside was a pair of white jade immortals, each about two and a half inches tall, with fully formed eyebrows, eyes, mouths, ears, and bodies. They wore black headscarves and had belts tied in a manner resembling black silk, with two ribbons hanging down, so finely crafted that they seemed beyond the reach of human hands. Jia treasured them greatly, keeping them secret. In the chaos of war, their whereabouts were lost.

    The Child Guardian of the Orchid

    Xuan Shu from Mengzhou Road married at an age of less than twenty. Shortly after, his wife passed away, and he mourned her incessantly, feeling depressed and unable to find solace. One night, he dreamed that his wife appeared as she did in life, telling him that after death she had become the Child Guardian of the Orchid, residing in the Jade Green Temple. He composed a poem to remember her: "Before the Jade Green Temple, the fragrance of flowers and grass, the Child Guardian of the Orchid in light cloud attire. Repaying our past karmic connection and the debts of three lifetimes, it is said that the unreturned soul suffers." Here, "the unreturned soul" refers to the deceased as the one who has returned, while the living are called travelers.

    117

    王先生前知
    　　东阿阎生者，少从醇德先生平阴王广道学。醇德尝告之曰：“汝今年二十五，却后二十年当丧明，作举子不济。辛壬癸甲之术可养生，试以吾言学之。”阎即学禄命。年五十，果丧明，而艺亦精。自言七十当有子，得年八十。卒如其言。
    　　边元恕所纪二事
    　　国兵初西来，云中先下，后复纳辽天祚。国相怒其反复，攻城破，驱壮士无榆坡尽杀之。中有喉丝不断者，亦枕藉积尸中。得雨复苏，候暮夜欲逃。人定后，忽见吏卒群至，呼死者姓名，随呼皆应。独不呼此人。吏卒去，此人匍匐起，仅能至家。求医封药，疮口渐合。又数月平复。年七十余病终。同时曹氏小童，为军士驱逐。与群儿乱走，追及者皆以大棓击杀之。次第及曹，忽二犬突出，触军士仆地。军士怒逐犬入人家。比出，儿辈得散走，逃空室中。俄有执黄旗过者，大呼曰：“国相军令，杀人者斩！”残民皆得活。曹氏儿后至节度。
    　　王内翰诗谶

    Explanation

    117

    Mr. Wang, the Seer

    A man named Yan from Dong'e, in his youth, studied under the virtuous teacher Wang Guangdao from Pingyin. The teacher once told him, "You are twenty-five years old now, and in twenty years, you will lose your sight. You will not succeed as a scholar-official. The art of the zodiac can be used to maintain health; try to learn it from my words." Yan then studied the art of fortune-telling. At the age of fifty, he indeed became blind, but his skills also became highly refined. He said to himself that he would have a child at seventy and live to be eighty. In the end, his words came true.

    Two Events Recorded by Bian Yu'su

    When the national army first came from the west, Yunzhong surrendered first, but later accepted the Liao Dynasty's Emperor Tianzuo. The chancellor was angry at their treachery, attacked and captured the city, and drove the strong men from Wuyu Slope to kill them all. Among them, there was one whose throat was not severed, and he also lay among the corpses. He revived after the rain, waited until nightfall to escape. After the evening, he suddenly saw a group of officials and soldiers arrive, calling out the names of the dead, and all responded. Only this person was not called out. When the officials and soldiers left, this person crawled up, only managing to reach home. He sought medical treatment and bandaged the wound, and the wound gradually healed. After several more months, he fully recovered. In his seventies, he died of illness. At the same time, a young boy from the Cao family was chased by soldiers. He ran with a group of children, and those who caught up killed them all with large clubs. Eventually, they caught up with Cao, and suddenly two dogs leaped out, running into the soldiers and falling to the ground. The soldiers, angry, chased the dogs into a house. When they came out, the children managed to scatter and run away, hiding in an empty room. Soon, someone holding a yellow flag passed by and shouted, "The chancellor's military order: those who kill will be beheaded!" All the remaining people survived. The young boy from the Cao family later became a military governor.

    The Poem Omen by Wang, the Imperial Scholar

    118

    王子端内翰，泰和中赋《残菊》云：“幽花寂寞无多子。办与黄蜂实蜜脾。”盖绝笔也。王勉道作挽诗，故有“‘幽花’绝笔更伤神”之句。
    　　张甫梦应
    　　张状元甫，唱第前梦人以物易其首，手自扪之，乃玉也。初甚恶之，继有是应。阎子秀笔记其事。
    　　山石飞堕
    　　宣和末，华山下石子冈地震之后，东西易位，摧压十八村。土人谓神物所移，为立移山祠。兰泉张吉甫作赋吊之。明昌四年秋，洽水、渭南之间，一日晨起，居人忽闻千人呼声。望之，有云如大帷幙，蔽空而过。少顷开霁，并山南原已移为北原矣！孙通祥为文记之。近天兴癸巳麦秋后，恒山公治军邓之五朵山，置仓圣朵岩以受军租。临涧大屋已置二万余斛矣！有日寅卯间，人见西北有黑云从空而过，声势甚恶，迤逦渐及涧上，仓屋随亦崩溃。云起而雨。雨后人奔视之，元得大石片，方广数亩，自天而下，横两涧之闲。麦仓崩，乃无一麦可寻。又一异也。平阴丞说。

    118

    Academician Wang Zidian, during the Tahe period, composed a poem titled "Residual Chrysanthemums" which reads: "Lonely flowers with few offspring. Prepare for the bees to fill the honeycomb." This was his final work. Wang Miantao wrote a funeral poem in response, hence the line: "The lonely flowers of his final work are even more heart-wrenching."

    Zhang Fupu's Dream

    Before Zhang Zhuangyuan was called out in the imperial examination, he dreamed that someone exchanged something for his head. He touched it with his own hand and found it to be jade. Initially, he was very displeased, but later this proved to be a favorable omen. Yan Zixiu recorded this incident in his notes.

    Flying and Falling Rocks

    At the end of the Xuanhe period, after an earthquake beneath Mount Hua, the east and west positions were swapped, destroying and pressing down eighteen villages. The locals believed this was caused by a divine entity and built a Temple of Moving Mountains in commemoration. Lanquan Zhang Jifu wrote a poem to mourn the event. In the fourth year of the Mingchang era, in the autumn, in the area between Qiashui and Weinan, one morning, the residents suddenly heard the sound of thousands of people shouting. Looking up, they saw a cloud like a large tent covering the sky and passing by. Soon after, the weather cleared, and the southern plains had already been moved to the north! Sun Tongxiang wrote an article to record this event. Recently, in the year Guisi after the wheat harvest in the Tianxing era, Lord of Mount Heng governed the army at Wuduo Mountain in Deng, setting up a granary at Duoyan to receive military taxes. Large houses near the ravine already held over 20,000 dou of grain! One day between the hours of Yin and Mao, people saw a black cloud passing through the sky from the northwest, with a very ominous sound and appearance. Gradually, it approached the ravine, and the granary houses also collapsed. The clouds rose and it rained. After the rain, people rushed to see, and found a large stone slab, several acres wide, falling from the sky, spanning the two ravines. The granary collapsed, and there was no trace of a single grain of wheat. This was yet another strange occurrence, as recounted by the magistrate of Pingyin.

    119

    闲闲公主章表
    　　壬寅岁寒食，濮州灵宝会祭孤魂，设醮。州中程威仪者当作高功会首。人言：“程未尝收箓，何缘得主醮？”程因往东平受明威箓。一阶章表，皆已具衔。复一雷师者求代程主醮，属监军董许之。乃就用文牒上名衔改程作雷。醮后百余日，雷无病而死。三日复活，说死入冥司云：“礼部闲闲赵公管词表，以我不应改程威仪名字，促寿二纪。放之暂来，令告世人再不许犯！”且言门外追卒甚众，即当去矣。言终而化。泰安布衣张知现至濮州，得此事。

    Explanation

    119

    Translation:

    The Princess Xianxian's Memorial Tablet

    In the Ninety-second year of the Renyin cycle, during the Cold Food Festival, in Puzhou, the Lingbao assembly sacrificed to wandering spirits and set up a ritual ceremony. In the state, Cheng Wei, a person of ceremony, should be the leader of the high-ranking assembly. People said, "Cheng has never received the talisman; how could he be the leader of the ritual?" Cheng therefore went to Dongping to receive the Mingwei talisman. All the formal documents, with titles, were already prepared. Then, a thunder master requested to replace Cheng as the leader of the ritual, and this was assigned by the military supervisor Dong Xu. The name on the official document was then changed from Cheng to Lei. Over a hundred days after the ritual, Lei died without illness. After three days, he revived and said that after death, he entered the underworld and said, "The idle Zhao Gong from the Ministry of Rites managed the formal documents. Because I should not have changed Cheng Wei's name, he shortened my life by two decades. Let me come back temporarily, to tell the world not to commit such a sin again!" And he said that there were many pursuers outside, and he would have to leave soon. After finishing his words, he transformed. Zhang Zhiyan, a commoner from Taian, arrived in Puzhou and learned this matter.

    120

    密崖题字
    　　明昌末，卢氏山密崖，石壁高峻，非人迹所到。忽有题字云：“道民天台司马承祯过。”字大如盌，墨色光莹而紫。予过中岩，谒白云先生祠，碑载：承祯葬松台。因有诗云：“道民初不忘天台，姓氏分明见密崖。为问松台千载鹤，白云何处不归来？”
    　　秦简夫临终诗
    　　陵川秦简夫，年四十困于名场，即不就举选。临终诗云：“躯壳羁栖宅，妻孥解逅恩。云山最佳处，随意著诗魂。”掷笔而逝。时年五十七。
    　　张子野吉征
    　　张华子野，“易无体”榜廷试后，与诸生坐庭中。忽一鸟衔小绿衣判官堕几上。未几，子野擢上第。

    Explanation

    120

    Translation

    Inscriptions on the Secret Cliff

    At the end of the Mingchang era, on the steep cliffs of Misha Mountain, there were stone walls so high and sheer that they were beyond the reach of human footsteps. Suddenly, an inscription appeared, reading: "Dao Min from Tian Tai, Sima Chengzhen passed by." The characters were as large as a bowl, and the ink was lustrous and purple. I passed by Zhongyan, visited the shrine of Mr. Baiyun, and saw an inscription on the stele that stated: "Sima Chengzhen was buried on Songtai." Inspired by this, I wrote a poem: "Dao Min never forgot Tian Tai, his name and surname clearly seen on the secret cliff. I ask the thousand-year cranes of Songtai, where does the white cloud not return?"

    Qin Jianfu's Poem on His Deathbed

    Qin Jianfu from Lingchuan, at the age of forty, was trapped in the pursuit of fame and did not pursue the imperial examinations. On his deathbed, he wrote a poem: "The body is a temporary dwelling, wife and children are fleeting companions. The best place in the clouds and mountains, let the spirit of poetry wander freely." He threw down his brush and passed away. He was fifty-seven years old.

    Zhang Huaziye's Auspicious Sign

    Zhang Huaziye, after passing the imperial examination under the "Yi Wu Ti" (No Fixed Form) list, sat with his fellow students in the courtyard. Suddenly, a bird carrying a small green-robed judge fell onto the table. Shortly after, Zhang Huaziye was selected as the top candidate.

    121

    王生冤报
    　　定襄邱村王胡，以陶瓦为业。明昌辛亥岁歉，与其子王生者就食山东。一日，有强寇九人为尉司根捕急，避死无所，就此家藏匿。以情告云：“我辈金贝不赀，但此身得免，愿与君父子平分之。”王因匿盗窑中，满实坯瓦。尉司兵随过，无所见而去。胡父子心不自安，且利其财，乘夜发火。不移时熏九人死。即携金贝还乡。数年，殖产甚丰，出乡豪之上。泰和中，王生礼五台。将及兴善镇，恍惚中有所见，惊怖堕马遂为物所凭。扶舁至其家。生口作鬼语，嗔目怒骂云：“尉司追我辈，已得脱，中分货财，足以致富；便发恶心，都将我辈烧死！寻之数年，乃今见！汝偿命即休。”时或持刃，逢人乱斫。其家无奈，召道士何吉卿驱逐之。何至，作法，鬼复凭语辨诉。何知冤对非法箓可制，教以作黄箓超度，或可解脱。胡陈状斋坛，吐露情实，人始知其致富之由。大建一祠，日夕祈祷。生未几竟死。紫微刘尊师说。

    Explanation

    121

    Wang Sheng's Retribution
    　　Wang Hu, a potter from Qiu Village in Dingxiang, along with his son Wang Sheng, faced famine in the year 1191 (the Xinhai year of Mingchang) and went to Shandong to seek food. One day, nine bandits, pursued by military officials, had nowhere to hide from death and sought refuge in their home. They revealed their situation, saying, "We have a fortune in gold and cowrie shells, but if we can escape, we wish to divide it equally with you and your son." Wang Hu hid the bandits in his kiln, filling it with clay and tiles. The military officials passed by without seeing anything. Wang Hu and his son felt uneasy in their hearts, coveting the wealth, and decided to set the kiln on fire at night. In no time, the nine bandits suffocated to death. Wang Hu then took the gold and cowrie shells back to his village. Over the years, he accumulated a great deal of wealth, surpassing the local gentry. During the Taihe period, Wang Sheng paid respects to Mount Wutai. As he approached Xingshan Town, he saw something in a daze and fell off his horse in terror, being possessed by a spirit. He was carried home on a stretcher. Speaking in the voice of a ghost, he glared and cursed angrily, saying, "The military officials were chasing us, and we managed to escape, dividing the wealth equally, which was enough to make us rich; but then you had wicked thoughts and burned us all to death! We searched for you for several years, and now I have found you! If you pay the price with your life, then it will be over." Sometimes he would hold a blade and attack people indiscriminately. His family, helpless, summoned Daoist master He Jiqing to exorcise the spirit. When He arrived, he performed rituals, and the spirit spoke through Wang Sheng to defend itself. He realized that the spirit's injustice could not be controlled by ordinary exorcism and taught them to perform the Yellow Scripture to liberate the spirit, which might help. Wang Hu revealed the truth at a ritual altar, and people finally understood the source of his wealth. They built a large shrine and prayed day and night. Wang Sheng died not long after. This story was told by Daoist master Liu from the Purple Micro Palace.

    122

    仙猫
    　　天坛中岩有仙猫洞。世传燕真人丹成，鸡犬亦升仙，而猫独不去，在洞已数百年。游人至洞前呼“仙哥”，间有应者。王屋令临漳薛鼎臣呼之而应，亲为予言。己亥夏四月，予自阳台宫将之上方。过洞前，命儿子叔仪呼之。随呼而应，声殊清远也。因作诗云：“仙猫声在洞中闻，凭仗儿童一问君。同向燕家舐丹灶，不随鸡犬上青云。”

    Explanation

    122

    Immortal Cat
    In the rocky recesses of the Heavenly Altar, there is a cave known as the Immortal Cat Cave. It is said that when Yan the True Person completed his elixir of immortality, even chickens and dogs ascended to immortality, but the cat remained behind, having stayed in the cave for several hundred years. Tourists who call out "Immortal Brother" in front of the cave sometimes receive a response. Wang Wuxing, the magistrate of Linzhang, once called out to it and it responded, and he personally told me about this. In the fourth month of the year Jihai, I was about to ascend from the Yuyang Palace and passed by the cave. I ordered my son Shuyi to call out to it, and it responded immediately, its voice especially clear and distant. Inspired by this, I composed a poem:

    "The voice of the immortal cat is heard in the cave,
    Relying on a child to ask you.
    Together, you licked the alchemist's elixir furnace,
    But did not follow the chickens and dogs to the blue clouds."

    123

    田德秀夙悟
    　　紫芝，字德秀，沧州人。其父济为部掾，娶定襄赵氏，生德秀于中都。生数月，邻李媪见之，潸然出涕。人问之，媪曰：“老妇一儿子，生二十五岁，在太学有声，以去年亡。此儿极相肖也。吾儿死时，老妇啮其面破，此儿面疮口痕宛然，可以证前身矣！”德秀幼孤，养于外家，多居于忻。六七岁知属文，一览万言。十三，赋《丽华引》，诗意惊人，有李长吉风调。十六与余游从。曾大雨后有诗见示云：“醉梦萧森蝶翅轻，一镫无语梦边明。虚檐雨急三江浪，老木风高万马兵。枕簟先秋失残暑，湖山彻晓看新晴。对床曾有诗来否？为问韦家好弟兄。”予兄敏之私谓予言：“诗首二句，非鬼语乎，吾谓其非寿者相也。”果以弱冠下世云。

    Explanation

    123

    Zi Zhi, courtesy name De Xiu, was from Cangzhou. His father, Ji, served as a deputy official, and he married Zhao from Dingxiang, giving birth to De Xiu in Zhongdu. When De Xiu was just a few months old, a neighbor, an elderly woman, saw him and shed tears involuntarily. When others asked her why, she said, "My only son, who was twenty-five years old, studied at the Imperial Academy and was renowned. He died last year. This child looks very much like him. When my son died, I bit his face, leaving a scar. This child has a similar scar, which can prove his past life!" De Xiu lost his father at a young age and was raised by his maternal relatives, mostly living in Xin. At the age of six or seven, he already knew how to compose literature, reading and understanding thousands of words in one go. At thirteen, he wrote a poem titled "Lihua Yin," whose poetic imagery was astonishing and had the style of Li He. At sixteen, he became a companion of mine. Once, after a heavy rain, he showed me a poem that read: "Drunk in a dream, the butterfly's wings are light; one lamp silently illuminates the edge of the dream. The eaves, drenched by the rain, echo the waves of the Three Rivers; old trees, swayed by the wind, seem like ten thousand horses in battle. The pillows and mats lose the lingering heat of summer before the autumn arrives; the lakes and mountains reveal a new dawn as the rain clears. Has anyone written poetry about sharing a bed? I ask the good brothers of the Wei family." My elder brother Minzhi privately told me, "The first two lines of the poem are not like ghostly words? I think he does not have the appearance of a long-lived person." Indeed, De Xiu passed away at a young age.

    124

    华陀帖
    　　米元章华陀帖，二十八字。靖康之变，流落民闲。历三四传，乃入越王府。王惧为内府所收，秘之二十年，无知者。泰和末，都城阎贯道与文士辈请仙，元章降笔。贯道因问：“先生《华陀帖》，神迹超轶，辉映今古；汴京破，失所在。先生于平生得意书，定知为何人所秘，愿以见告。”即批云：“当就越邸求之。”庞都运才卿，王妃之弟，贯道以为言。才卿请于妃，果获一见。王薨于汴，明禁随废。文士得从王之子密公游，往往见焉。东坡梦杜子美自解《八阵图》，谓是书生习气。以此事观，非讹言。

    Explanation

    124

    The "Hua Tuo Letter" by Mi Fu, consisting of twenty-eight characters, was lost among the common people during the Jinyu Incident. After passing through several hands, it eventually came into the possession of the Prince of Yue. Fearing that it would be seized by the imperial treasury, the prince kept it secret for twenty years, and no one knew of its existence. By the end of the Taihe era, in the capital city, Yan Guandao and other literati engaged in spiritual practices, and the spirit of Mi Fu descended and wrote. Yan Guandao then asked, "Your 'Hua Tuo Letter' is miraculous and surpasses all others, shining brightly throughout history. After the fall of Bianjing, it was lost. You must have known who kept it secret among those you favored in your lifetime. I wish to be informed." The spirit immediately responded, "It should be sought in the Yue residence." Pang Du Yun Cai Qing, the brother of the princess, relayed this message to her. Upon hearing this, the princess granted permission, and Cai Qing was indeed able to see the letter once. After the prince died in Bianjing, the strict prohibition was subsequently lifted. Literati were then able to view the letter with the prince's son, the Prince of Mi, and often saw it. Su Shi once dreamed that Du Fu explained the "Eight Diagrams Formation" to him, saying it was a scholarly habit. Considering this event, it is not false words.

    125

    梁梅
    　　寿阳歌妓梁梅，承安、泰和间，以才色名河东。张状元巨济过寿阳，引病后孤居，意不自聊。邑中士子有以梅为言者。时已落籍，私致之，待于尼寺。梅素妆而至。坐久干杯，唱《梅花》、《水龙吟》。张微言：“六月唱梅词，寿阳地寒可知。”然以其音调员美，颇为改观。唱至“天教占了百花头上，和羹未晚”，乃以酒属张，张大奇之。赠之乐府，有“谁知幽谷里，真有寿阳妆”之句。为留数日而行。
    　　军中犬
    　　征西军中畜一犬。每大帅举酒，部曲辈前列，唱《落叶曲》，则犬亦随之。声节高下，少不差异。曲罢，一声不复作。吾州王百户，辛丑年亲见之。

    Explanation

    125

    Translation

    Li Mei

    Li Mei, a songstress from Shouyang, was famous in Hedong for her talent and beauty during the reigns of Emperor Cheng'an and Emperor Taihe. Zhang Jujing, the状元 (zhuangyuan), passed through Shouyang, feeling aimless and disheartened after falling ill and living alone. Some scholars in the county mentioned her. She had already been deregistered and was privately invited to meet him at a nunnery. Li Mei arrived in plain makeup. After sitting for a long time and drinking, she sang the songs "Plum Blossoms" and "Water Dragon Chant." Zhang remarked, "Singing a plum blossom song in June shows how cold Shouyang must be." However, he found her melody beautiful and well-structured, which quite changed his opinion. When she sang the line, "Heaven has made her the queen of all flowers, and it's not too late to blend with the soup," she offered him a drink, which greatly amazed Zhang. He gifted her a poem with the lines, "Who would have known that in the secluded valley, there is indeed a Shouyang makeup." He stayed for several days before continuing his journey.

    Dog in the Military Camp

    In the Western Expeditionary Army, there was a dog. Every time the general raised his cup, the ranks of soldiers lined up in front and sang the song "Fallen Leaves," and the dog would follow along. The pitch and rhythm were high and low, rarely differing. After the song ended, the dog did not bark again. I, the hundred-household head of my state, personally saw this in the year XinChou.

    126

    蚩尤城
    　　华州界有蚩尤城。古老言：蚩尤阚姓，故又谓之阚蚩尤城。城旁阚氏尚多。尔朱荣，秀容人。今定襄有尔都统者，自言上世有赐田百顷，至今以“尔百顷”家自夸。管州有荣庙，土人祈赛甚灵。巢贼败，言灭巢族，族人以平人自解。有漏网者皆以“平”为氏。子孙予有识之者，貌与秘府所画巢像相肖。不欲斥其名云。
    　　德升后身
    　　乌古论德升，第进士。兴定戊寅，以参知政事行台太原。九月六日城陷遇害。以其日受生庆阳移剌仓使家儿。四五岁能说前身事，沉厚寡言，人传为异事，德升家一大奴，从太原逃出，就仓使家来问。儿望见，名呼之，奴为之恸。但说其死不同：奴言德升被斫而死；儿言赴井死。游麟之言：“当是闻城陷，一心赴井，神识已逝，不复知被斫耳！”一僧云：“不然‘赴井’者，盖杀胎耳！”

    Explanation

    126

    The City of Chiyou
    In the territory of Huazhou there is a city known as the City of Chiyou. According to ancient lore, Chiyou bore the surname Kan, hence it was also called the Kan City of Chiyou. There are still many people with the surname Kan living near the city. Er Zhu Rong, a figure from Xiu Rong, claimed that his ancestors had been granted a hundred hectares of land, and they continue to boast of their lineage as "Er Baoqin." In Guanzhou, there is a temple dedicated to Er Zhu Rong, which is said to be very effective in granting wishes. When the rebel leader Chao was defeated, it was said that his clan was exterminated, but some survivors claimed to be ordinary people. Those who managed to escape were all given the surname Ping. Among the descendants, some recognized individuals resemble the portrait of Chao kept in the imperial archives, but the name is not mentioned.

    The Reincarnation of De Sheng
    Wugu Lun De Sheng passed the imperial examinations. In the year Xingding Wuyin (1218 CE), he served as a temporary governor in Taiyuan with the title of Vice Chancellor. On the sixth day of the ninth month, the city fell and he was killed. On that same day, he was reborn as a child in the family of Yilanchangshi in Qingyang. At the age of four or five, he could recount the events of his previous life. He was deep and reserved, speaking little, and this was considered an extraordinary matter. A large servant from De Sheng's household fled from Taiyuan and came to inquire at the Yilanchangshi's home. The child saw him and called out his name, causing the servant to weep. They differed in their accounts of how De Sheng died: the servant said he was beheaded, while the child said he died by jumping into a well. You Lin remarked, "It seems that upon hearing the city had fallen, he was determined to jump into the well, and his spirit had already departed, so he did not feel the pain of being beheaded!" One monk said, "No, 'jumping into the well' means he was killed in the womb!"

    127

    田德秀诗
    　　田德秀少孤，养于外祖广宁府治中赵君家。纨袴间作诗多憔悴之语。乱后登凌云台云：“愁思纷纷不易裁，凌云台上独绯。乱鸦背著斜阳去，寒雁带将秋色来。破屋无烟空碎瓦，新坟经雨已苍茗。天翻地覆亲曾见，信得昆明有劫灰。”明年客死五台。无忧而戚，古人所忌。王荆公诗：“少壮不宜轻感慨，文章尤忌数悲哀。”真名言也！
    　　张居士
    　　澧州人张居士，于禅学有所得。临终之岁，禅坐静室，约其徒闭之，满百日乃开。及期开户，见其凝然不动，谓是已逝。良久开目，拂尘而起，沐浴更衣，周行庭宇，与亲旧相劳苦，已而复入室中，索纸留偈云：“了脱幻缘，复何幻我？游戏大方，从容自可。”掷笔而化。登封令张效景说此事。

    Explanation

    127

    Translation:

    Tian Deshou's Poem

    Tian Deshou, orphaned at a young age, was raised by his maternal grandfather, Zhao Jun, the governor of Guangning Prefecture. Though he lived a life of ease, his poetry often expressed feelings of sorrow and hardship. After a period of turmoil, he climbed the Lingyun Tower and composed this poem:

    "Endless sorrow is hard to express;
    Alone on the Lingyun Tower, I stand.
    Wild crows fly away with the setting sun,
    Cold geese bring autumn's chill.
    Ruined houses without smoke, only broken tiles remain,
    New graves, after rain, turn green and desolate.
    I have witnessed the upheaval of heaven and earth,
    And I believe that Kunming has seen its share of destruction."

    The following year, he died in exile on Wutai Mountain. His sorrow without cause was something ancient people avoided. Wang Anshi once wrote: "In youth, one should not lightly express grief; in writing, one especially should avoid frequent expressions of sorrow." These are indeed wise words!

    Master Zhang

    Zhang Jushi, a resident of Lizhou, had attained some understanding in Zen studies. In his final year, he sat in meditation in a quiet room, instructing his disciples to seal the door and not open it for a hundred days. When the time came, they opened the door and found him motionless, as if he had passed away. After a long while, he opened his eyes, brushed away the dust, and rose. He bathed, changed his clothes, and walked around the courtyard, greeting his old friends. Afterward, he returned to the room, asked for paper, and left behind a verse:

    "Free from the illusions of attachment,
    What is there to be deluded by?
    Playing in the grand manner,
    Calm and at ease, naturally."

    He then dropped his pen and passed away. Magistrate Zhang Xiaojing of Dengfeng recounted this story.

    128

    米元章心经咒
    　　米老一帖云《心经咒》。从后倒念七遍，吹气枕席闲，螫虫皆不敢近。试之信然。
    　　王尊师天坛之行
    　　吾州天庆观王尊师志常，出于农家。年十六七，牧羊田间。一道人日来相就问：“汝肯随我往天坛山否？”王许之，道人携之而行。暮至一城，忽失道人，问其地，乃济源也。又问人此去天坛近远？人云：“百余里耳！”王已无所归，明日往天坛。入阳台宫。宫中人闻此儿为道人挈来，自太原北，一日至天坛，谓当有仙分。留为香火童子。八年乃归家。人意其已死，无不惊异。而乃送之天庆。今年已八十六，神明不衰，淳质谨厚，有道者也。
    　　张先生座右铭
    　　张先生弥学，东阿人，平章政事寿国文贞公良辅之父。神道碑载其事。内座右铭云：“欲求聪明，先当积学；欲求子孙，先当积孝。”以为名言。

    Explanation

    128

    米元章心经咒

    Mǐ Yuánzhāng, a renowned calligrapher and painter of the Song Dynasty, wrote a text called the "Heart Sutra Incantation." The incantation is recited backward seven times, and when blown upon pillows and beds, it repels stinging insects. Testing it confirmed its efficacy.

    王尊师天坛之行

    Wáng Zūnshī, a respected teacher from our state, was born into a farming family. At the age of sixteen or seventeen, he tended sheep in the fields. A Taoist monk came to him daily and asked, "Will you follow me to the Heavenly Altar?" Wáng agreed, and the monk took him along. By evening, they reached a city, but the monk suddenly disappeared. When Wáng asked about the place, it was revealed to be Jìyuán. He then asked how far it was to the Heavenly Altar, and someone replied, "More than a hundred miles!" With no place to return to, Wáng decided to continue to the Heavenly Altar the next day. He arrived at the Yáotái Palace. The people in the palace, hearing that this boy had been brought by a monk from Taiyuan and had traveled to the Heavenly Altar in one day, believed he had a divine destiny. They kept him as a young disciple. After eight years, he returned home. People thought he must have died, and they were all surprised. Instead, he was sent to Tiānqìng. This year, he is eighty-six years old, with undiminished spirit and vitality. He is simple, honest, cautious, and kind, a person of virtue.

    张先生座右铭

    Mr. Zhang Míxué, from Dōng'ē, was the father of Liáng Fǔ, who held the high-ranking position of Píngzhāng Zhèngshì and was posthumously titled Shòu Guó Wénzhēn Gōng. His father's deeds are recorded on a stele. Among his sayings, one reads, "To seek intelligence, one must first accumulate learning; to seek descendants, one must first accumulate filial piety." These are considered famous sayings.
